Tayammum Intention: Does It Permit Obligatory Prayer?
Commentary on tayammum validity for different acts based on intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on tayammum intention and apply the majority view to determine whether tayammum suffices for obligatory prayer.

Core Idea
Tayammum's validity for prayer depends on its intended purpose; only an intention for a specific worship (qurbah maqsūdah) suffices.

Tayammum is a dry substitute for wudu and ghusl when water is unavailable. However, its scope depends on the intention at the time of performance. This passage from the Hanafi commentary clarifies a key ikhtilaf: whether tayammum performed for a non-specific act like touching the Mushaf permits the obligatory prayer. We will unpack the two positions and identify the operative ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Tayammum is a purification when water is absent. The passage discusses its validity for subsequent acts based on the intention at the time of tayammum.
2
State the position of the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad)
They require that tayammum be intended for a specific act of worship (qurbah maqsūdah) that requires purification. If done for a non-specific act, it does not permit obligatory prayer.
This is the mufta bihi (operative) view.
3
State the position of Abu Hanifa and the alternative
Abu Hanifa and another narrator (often Zufar) do not require such an intention; tayammum for any purpose suffices for all acts requiring purification.
This view is not relied upon for fatwa.
4
Apply the mufta bihi view to examples
If one does tayammum to recite Quran or enter a mosque (non-specific), then later wants to pray, the prayer is invalid. But the tayammum still permits the original intended act (e.g., touching Mushaf).
See the commentary's examples: visiting graves, burial, returning greetings.
5
Note the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The difference affects whether a person needs to repeat tayammum when moving from a non-obligatory act to obligatory prayer. The mufta bihi requires a new tayammum with proper intention.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعندهما: قربة مقصودة لا تصح إلا بالطهارة، فإن تيمم الصلاة الجنازة، أو لسجدة التلاوة يجوز بهذا التيمم أداء المكتوبات ، وإن تيمم لمس المصحف أو دخول المسجد لا تصح به الصلاة؛ لأنه لم ينو به قربة مقصودة، لكن يحل له مس المصحف، ودخول المسجد. وعند أبي حنيفة ومحمد لا تشترط نية القربة المقصودة التي لا تصح بدون الطهارة، وإن شئت الاطلاع على دلائل القولين مع ما لها وما عليها فارجع إلى حواشي «الهداية». [١] قوله : تيمم ... الخ؛ أي عند العجز عن استعمال الماء، وأما عند القدرة فلا يجوز التيمم لسجدة التلاوة مطلقاً ؛ لأنها مما تشترط لها الطهارة، وما في «جامع الرموز» من جواز التيمم لها مع القدرة على الماء فلا عبرة به. [٢] قوله : لصلاة الجنازة؛ هذا محمول على ما إذا لم يكن واجداً للماء، أما إذا تيمم لها مع وجوده لخوف الفوت فإنّ تيمّمه يبطل لفراغه منها. كذا في «البحر». [٣] قوله : لأنه لم ينو قربة مقصودة؛ فإنّ مس المصحف لم يشرع عبادة إلا للقراءة، ودخول المسجد لم يكن عبادة إلا لما يؤدى فيه، وكذا لو تيمم لقراءة القرآن عن ظهر القلب أو المصحف أو لزيارة القبور أو لدفن الميت، أو لرد السلام، أو تعليم الغير لا يجوز له أداء الصلاة بهذا التيمم؛ لأنها عبادات غير مقصودة. كذا في «فتاوى قاضي خان». [٤] قوله : لكن يحلّ له مس المصحف ودخول المسجد، هذا عند فقد الماء أو العجز عن استعماله، وأما عند القدرة عليه فلا يحل له مس المصحف؛ لأنه مما يشترط له الطهارة، ويحلّ دخول المسجد بناءً على أنّ ما لا تشترط له الطهارة يكفي له التيمم مع القدرة على الماء، كما فصله في «شرعة الإسلام»، وشرحه «مفتاح الجنان»، و«البزازية» وغيرها.
And according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): a specific act of worship that is only valid with purification – if one performs tayammum for the funeral prayer or for the prostration of recitation, it is permissible to perform the obligatory prayers with this tayammum. But if one performs tayammum for touching the Mushaf or entering the mosque, prayer is not valid with it, because he did not intend by it a specific act of worship, yet it becomes permissible for him to touch the Mushaf and enter the mosque. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, the intention of a specific act of worship that is invalid without purification is not a condition. And if you wish to see the proofs of the two positions with their strengths and weaknesses, refer to the glosses of al-Hidayah. [1] His statement: 'tayammum ... etc.' means when unable to use water, but when able, tayammum for the prostration of recitation is absolutely not permitted because it is an act that requires purification, and what is in Jami' al-Rumuz about permissibility of tayammum for it while able to use water is disregarded. [2] His statement: 'for the funeral prayer' – this is understood as when he has no water. But if he performs tayammum for it while having water due to fear of missing it, his tayammum becomes invalid after finishing it. As in al-Bahr. [3] His statement: 'because he did not intend a specific act of worship' – for touching the Mushaf is not legislated as worship except for recitation, and entering the mosque is not worship except for what is performed in it. Similarly, if he performed tayammum for reciting the Quran from memory or from the Mushaf, or for visiting graves, or for burying the deceased, or for returning greetings, or for teaching others, it is not permissible to perform prayer with this tayammum because they are non-specific acts of worship. As in Fatawa Qadi Khan. [4] His statement: 'but it becomes permissible for him to touch the Mushaf and enter the mosque' – this is when water is unavailable or unable to be used. But when able, it is not permissible for him to touch the Mushaf because it requires purification, but entering the mosque is permissible based on the fact that acts not requiring purification are sufficient with tayammum even when able to use water, as elaborated in Shar' al-Islam, its commentary Miftah al-Jinan, al-Bazzaziyya, and others.
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the ruling of tayammum for various acts. It begins by stating the position of the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) that tayammum performed with the intention of a specific act of worship (like funeral prayer or prostration of recitation) suffices for performing obligatory prayers. However, if tayammum is done for touching the Mushaf or entering the mosque – which are not specific acts of worship requiring intention – then it does not permit the obligatory prayer, though it does permit those acts. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold a different view: they do not require the intention of a specific act of worship for tayammum to be valid for other purposes. The commentary then clarifies that this ruling applies when water is unavailable; if water is available, tayammum for prostration of recitation is invalid because it requires purification. Similarly, tayammum for funeral prayer when water is present only due to fear of missing the prayer becomes invalid after completion. The passage lists other non-specific acts for which tayammum does not permit prayer. Finally, it distinguishes between touching the Mushaf (which always requires purification) and entering the mosque (which may be done without purification when tayammum is valid). The text follows the author's order, first presenting the main ruling, then explaining each clause.

Key Terms
قربة مقصودة (qurbah maqsūdah): A specific act of worship that is intended for its own sake and requires purification.
تيمم (tayammum): Dry purification using earth as a substitute for wudu/gusl when water is unavailable.
نية (niyyah): Intention that differentiates acts of worship; here, whether tayammum was intended for a specific 'ibadah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person performs tayammum with the intention of touching the Mushaf (due to lack of water) and then wants to perform the obligatory prayer, is his prayer valid according to the majority Hanafi view?
A) Yes, because tayammum is valid regardless of intention.
B) No, because he did not intend a specific act of worship (qurbah maqsūdah).
C) Yes, because touching the Mushaf requires the same purification as prayer.
D) No, because tayammum is only for prayer.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the validity of tayammum for subsequent obligatory prayer depends on the intention at the time: it must be for a specific act of worship (qurbah maqsūdah) that requires purification.

Validity of a Disbeliever's Wudu Without Intention
Ruling on wudu of a disbeliever without intention and its effect after embracing Islam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds a disbeliever's wudu without intention valid and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
A disbeliever's wudu is valid even without intention because water purifies by nature, not by worship.

This passage addresses a key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: whether intention (niyyah) is a condition for the validity of wudu. The Hanafi school argues that wudu is a physical purification like washing a garment, so intention is not required. The passage explores the implications for a disbeliever's wudu and its effect after embracing Islam.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: a disbeliever's wudu without intention is valid, and if he later embraces Islam, he may pray with that wudu.
This is the mufta bihi position within the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Al-Shafi'i holds that intention is a condition for wudu, so wudu without intention is invalid for both Muslim and disbeliever.
The disagreement is based on the general role of intention in acts of worship.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Shafi'i argues that wudu is an act of worship ('ibadah) and therefore requires intention (niyyah) for validity, just like prayer or fasting.
This is rooted in the hadith 'Actions are but by intentions.'
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school distinguishes wudu as a physical purification (taharah hissiyyah) akin to washing a garment; intention is not required for the purifying effect of water itself.
The nafs al-wudu (essence of wudu) is cleansing, not worship per se.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: In Hanafi, a convert may pray with his pre-Islam wudu; in Shafi'i, he must renew wudu with intention.
This difference affects actual practice for new Muslims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجاز وضوؤه بلا نية حتى إن توضأ بلا نيَّة فأسلم جاز صلاته بهذا الوضوء خلافا للشافعي، وهذا بناءً على مسألة النية في الوضوء، وإن توضأ بالنية فأسلم، فالخلاف ثابت أيضاً؛ لأنَّ نية الكافر لغو؛ لعدم الأهلية، وإنما قال: بلا نية، مبالغة فيصح وضوء الكافر مع النية بالطريق الأولى. [١] قوله : وجاز وضوؤه؛ أي الكافر بلانيّة، فإذا توضأ حال كفره بلا نية ثم أسلم جاز أداء الصلاة به؛ لأنّ الماء طهور بنفسه لا يحتاج تطهيره إلى النية، كما أنَّ الكافر إذا غسل الثوب النجس حال كفره ثمّ أسلم تجوز صلاته في ذلك الثوب. [٢] قوله : وهذا؛ الخلاف بيننا وبين الشافعي مبني على مسألة اشتراط النية في الوضوء، فعنده لما كانت النية شرطا في صحة الوضوء مطلقاً، يكون الوضوء بلا نية لغواً، سواء كان من المسلم أو الكافر. وعندنا لما لم تكن شرطاً لكون الوضوء مفتاح الصلاة، فيكون الوضوء بلا نية معتبرة أو إن صدرَ من الكافر حال كفره فيجوز أداء الصلاة به كغسل الثياب النجسة. [٣] قوله : وإن توضأ؛ أي الكافر فيه إشارة إلى أن قول الماتن بلا نية ليس احترازياً، فإنّه لو توضأ الكافر بنيّة أداء المكتوبة أو غيرها من العبادات التي يشترط لصحتها الإسلام يكون وضوؤه أيضاً لغواً عند الشافعي؛ لأن نية الكافر لمثل هذه القربات لغو؛ لعدم أهليته لأدائها؛ لفقد شرطها وهو الإسلام، فبقى وضوؤه بلا نية، فلا يصح عند الشافعي ويصح عندنا. [٤] قوله : وإنما قال... الخ؛ دفع لما يقال لما كان حكم وضوء الكافر مع النية وبدونها واحداً، وهو الصحة عندنا، وعدم الصحة عند الشافعي، فقوله : بلا نية؛ مستدرك يجب حذفه، وحاصله أنه إنما ذكره إفادة للحكم على سبيل المبالغة، وإعلاماً لحكم الوضوء بالنيّة بطريق الأولوية، فإنّه لما صح وضوؤه بلا نية يكون الوضوء مع النية صحيحاً بالطريق الأولى. فإن قلت : لما كانت نيته لغواً لعدم الأهلية كان وضوؤه بالنية وعدمها سواء، فلا يصح قوله بالطريق الأولى؛ لأنه إنّما يستقيم إذا كان لنيته اعتبار في الجملة.
And his wudu without intention is permissible, so much so that if he (a disbeliever) performs wudu without intention and then accepts Islam, his prayer with this wudu is permissible, contrary to al-Shafi'i. This is based on the issue of intention in wudu. And if he performs wudu with intention and then accepts Islam, the disagreement also exists because the intention of a disbeliever is null due to lack of eligibility. And he (the author) only said 'without intention' for emphasis, so the wudu of a disbeliever with intention is valid by even stronger reason. [1] His statement: 'And his wudu is permissible' means the wudu of the disbeliever without intention. So if he performs wudu while in disbelief without intention and then accepts Islam, performing prayer with it is permissible because water is purifying by itself and its purification does not require intention, just as if a disbeliever washes a najis garment while in disbelief and then accepts Islam, his prayer in that garment is permissible. [2] His statement: 'This' – the disagreement between us and al-Shafi'i is based on the issue of stipulating intention in wudu. According to him, since intention is a condition for the validity of wudu absolutely, wudu without intention is null, whether from a Muslim or a disbeliever. According to us, since it is not a condition because wudu is the key to prayer, wudu without intention is valid, even if it comes from a disbeliever while in disbelief, so performing prayer with it is permissible, like washing najis garments. [3] His statement: 'And if he performs wudu' means the disbeliever. This indicates that the author's saying 'without intention' is not exclusive; for if a disbeliever performs wudu with the intention of performing the obligatory prayer or other acts of worship that require Islam for their validity, his wudu is also null according to al-Shafi'i because the intention of a disbeliever for such acts of worship is null due to his lack of eligibility to perform them, lacking the condition of Islam. So his wudu remains without intention, thus it is not valid according to al-Shafi'i but valid according to us. [4] His statement: 'And he only said... etc.' is a rebuttal to what might be said: since the ruling of the disbeliever's wudu with intention and without it is the same – validity according to us and invalidity according to al-Shafi'i – then his saying 'without intention' is redundant and should be omitted. The conclusion is that he only mentioned it to convey the ruling by way of emphasis, and to inform of the ruling of wudu with intention by priority. For since his wudu without intention is correct, wudu with intention is valid by even stronger reason. If you object: since his intention is null due to lack of eligibility, his wudu with intention and without it are equal, so his statement 'by even stronger reason' is not valid, because it is only sound if his intention has some consideration in general.
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage discusses the Hanafi position on the validity of wudu performed by a disbeliever without intention. The author begins by stating the ruling: a disbeliever's wudu without intention is valid, so if he performs wudu while in a state of disbelief without any intention and later embraces Islam, he may pray with that wudu. This is contrary to al-Shafi'i. The reason is that intention is not a condition for the validity of wudu in the Hanafi school; water is inherently purifying. The commentary then clarifies that even if the disbeliever performs wudu with intention (e.g., intending an act of worship that requires Islam), the ruling remains the same because the intention of a disbeliever is null due to his lack of legal capacity. The phrase 'without intention' in the matn is not exclusive but is used for emphasis; the validity with intention is derived by priority. The commentary also addresses a potential objection: if the intention is null, then there is no difference, so how can it be 'by priority'? It explains that the phrase indicates that if wudu without intention is valid, then with intention it is even more so, as long as the intention has some general consideration even if not legally effective.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intention; here, whether it is required for validity of wudu. The passage argues it is not a condition.
كافر (kāfir): Disbeliever; one who has not accepted Islam. His acts of worship are not acceptable due to lack of faith, but physical purification (wudu) is valid.
لغو (laghw): Null, void; used here to describe the intention of a disbeliever because he lacks the legal capacity (ahliyyah) for worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a disbeliever performs wudu without any intention and then accepts Islam, is his prayer with that wudu valid?
A) Yes, because wudu does not require intention.
B) Yes, but only if he repents first.
C) No, because a disbeliever's wudu is invalid.
D) No, because intention is required for wudu.

Key Takeaway
A disbeliever's wudu without intention is valid in the Hanafi school because wudu is a physical purification, not dependent on intention, and after embracing Islam prayer with that wudu is permissible.

The Disbeliever's Wudu: Intention and Validity After Islam
Ruling on wudu of a kafir without niyyah and its effect after Islam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a disbeliever's wudu without intention and explain the a fortiori argument for wudu with intention.

Core Idea
Water is purifying by itself; intention is not required for wudu.

This lesson examines a key inter-madhhab dispute: does a disbeliever's wudu without intention become valid after embracing Islam? The Hanafi school argues it does, because intention is not a condition for wudu. The Shafi'i school disagrees. Understanding this ruling requires analyzing the role of intention and a fortiori reasoning.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: a disbeliever's wudu without intention is valid (sahih) according to Hanafis, and after Islam, prayer with that wudu is permissible.
This is based on the principle that water purifies by itself.
2
Identify the opposing view
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i holds intention as a condition for wudu absolutely, so wudu without intention is void for both Muslim and disbeliever.
The disagreement stems from the status of intention in wudu.
3
Follow the Hanafi proof
The key dalil: water is tahur (purifying) by itself, requiring no intention. Analogy: just as washing a najis garment without intention purifies it, so does wudu.
This is based on the nature of water, not on the performer's intention.
4
Understand the a fortiori argument
The matn mentions 'without intention' for exaggeration. If wudu without intention is valid, wudu with intention is valid with greater reason (awlawiyyah). An objection is raised that a disbeliever's intention is void, but the commentator resolves it by considering the act itself.
The a fortiori works because wudu with intention is more complete, even if the intention itself is not accepted.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafis allow prayer with such wudu; Shafi'is require redoing wudu with intention.
This difference matters when advising new Muslims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجاز وضوؤه بلا نية حتى إن توضأ بلا نيَّة فأسلم جازَ صلاته بهذا الوضوء خلافا للشافعي له، وهذا بناءً على مسألة النية في الوضوء، وإن توضأ بالنية فأسلم، فالخلاف ثابت أيضاً؛ لأنَّ نية الكافر لغو؛ لعدم الأهلية، وإنما قال: بلا نية، مبالغة فيصح وضوء الكافر مع النية بالطريق الأولى.
قوله: وجاز وضوؤه؛ أي الكافر بلانيّة، فإذا توضأ حال كفره بلا نية ثم أسلم جازَ أداء الصلاة به؛ لأنّ الماء طهور بنفسه لا يحتاج تطهيره إلى النية، كما أنَّ الكافر إذا غسل الثوب النجس حال كفره ثمّ أسلم تجوز صلاته في ذلك الثوب. قوله: وهذا؛ الخلاف بيننا وبين الشافعي مبني على مسألة اشتراط النية في الوضوء، فعنده لما كانت النية شرطا في صحة الوضوء مطلقاً، يكون الوضوء بلا نية لغوا، سواء كان من المسلم أو الكافر. وعندنا لما لم تكن شرطاً لكون الوضوء مفتاح الصلاة، فيكون الوضوء بلا نية معتبرة أو إن صدرَ من الكافر حال كفره فيجوز أداء الصلاة به كغسل الثياب النجسة. قوله: وإن توضأ؛ أي الكافر فيه إشارة إلى أن قول الماتن بلا نية ليس احترازياً، فإنّه لو توضأ الكافر بنيّة أداء المكتوبة أو غيرها من العبادات التي يشترط لصحتها الإسلام يكون وضوؤه أيضاً لغواً عند الشافعي؛ لأن نية الكافر لمثل هذه القربات لغو؛ لعدم أهليته لأدائها؛ لفقد شرطها وهو الإسلام، فبقى وضوؤه بلا نية، فلا يصح عند الشافعي ويصح عندنا.
قوله: وإنما قال... الخ؛ دفع لما يقال لما كان حكم وضوء الكافر مع النية وبدونها واحداً، وهو الصحة عندنا، وعدم الصحة عند الشافعي، فقوله: بلا نية؛ مستدرك يجب حذفه، وحاصله أنه إنما ذكره إفادة للحكم على سبيل المبالغة، وإعلاماً لحكم الوضوء بالنيّة بطريق الأولوية، فإنّه لما صح وضوؤه بلا نية يكون الوضوء مع النية صحيحاً بالطريق الأولى.
فإن قلت: لما كانت نيته لغواً لعدم الأهلية كان وضوؤه بالنية وعدمها سواء، فلا يصح قوله بالطريق الأولى؛ لأنه إنّما يستقيم إذا كان لنيته اعتبار في الجملة.
قلت: نية الكفار وإن كانت لغواً بالنظر إلى ذات المتوضئ لكن لا شك في أنه إذا لوحظ إلى ذات الوضوء يحكم بأنه مع النيّة أولى وأحرى بالصحة منه بلا نية، وحكم الشارح بطريق الأولوية بهذا الاعتبار لا بالاعتبار الأول، فاحفظ هذا، ولا تصغ إلى ما تفوه به الناظرون كما بيناه في «السعاية».
(ينظر: «المنهاج» (1: 47).
And his ablution without intention is permissible, such that if he performs ablution without intention and then embraces Islam, his prayer with this ablution is permissible, contrary to al-Shafi'i. And this is based on the issue of intention in ablution. And if he performs ablution with intention and then embraces Islam, the disagreement is also present, because the intention of a disbeliever is void due to lack of eligibility. He only said 'without intention' as an exaggeration, so the ablution of a disbeliever with intention is valid with greater reason.
His saying: 'And his ablution without intention is permissible,' meaning the disbeliever without intention. So if he performs ablution during his disbelief without intention then embraces Islam, it is permissible to perform prayer with it, because water is purifying by itself, its purification does not require intention, just as if a disbeliever washes a najis garment during his disbelief then embraces Islam, his prayer in that garment is permissible. His saying: 'And this' – the disagreement between us and al-Shafi'i is based on the issue of stipulating intention in ablution. According to him, since intention is a condition for the validity of ablution absolutely, ablution without intention is void, whether from a Muslim or a disbeliever. According to us, since it is not a condition because ablution is the key to prayer, ablution without intention is valid if it occurs from a disbeliever during his disbelief, so performing prayer with it is permissible like washing najis garments. His saying: 'And if he performs ablution' meaning the disbeliever, indicates that the author's expression 'without intention' is not exclusive; because if the disbeliever performs ablution with the intention of performing the obligatory prayer or other acts of worship that require Islam for their validity, his ablution would also be void according to al-Shafi'i, because the disbeliever's intention for such acts of devotion is void due to his lack of eligibility to perform them due to missing their condition, which is Islam. Thus his ablution remains without intention, so it is not valid according to al-Shafi'i and is valid according to us.
His saying: 'He only said...' is a refutation of the claim that since the ruling of the disbeliever's ablution with or without intention is the same – validity according to us and invalidity according to al-Shafi'i – his saying 'without intention' is redundant and must be omitted. The summary is that he mentioned it to convey the ruling by way of exaggeration and to inform of the ruling of ablution with intention with greater reason. Since his ablution without intention is valid, ablution with intention is valid with greater reason.
If you say: Since his intention is void due to lack of eligibility, his ablution with or without intention is equal, so his statement of greater reason is not sound, because it is only correct if his intention has some consideration in general.
I say: The intention of disbelievers, even if void with regard to the person performing ablution, there is no doubt that when considering the ablution itself, it is judged that with intention it is more appropriate and more deserving of validity than without intention. The commentator's ruling of greater reason is with this consideration, not with the first consideration. Preserve this, and do not listen to what the viewers have spoken as we have explained in al-Sa'aya.
(Refer to: al-Minhaj 1:47)
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage discusses the validity of a disbeliever's wudu without intention and its effect after embracing Islam, and the difference between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i. The author begins by stating that a disbeliever's wudu without intention is valid according to Hanafis, so if he later embraces Islam, he may pray with that wudu. This is contrary to Shafi'i, who requires intention for wudu's validity. The commentator explains that the basis of the dispute lies in the role of intention: Shafi'i considers intention a condition for wudu absolutely, while Hanafis do not, as wudu is the key to prayer. The commentator further clarifies that even if the disbeliever performs wudu with intention, the same difference applies because the disbeliever's intention is void for acts requiring Islam. The author's mention of 'without intention' is for exaggeration, showing that wudu with intention is valid a fortiori. An objection is raised: if the intention is void, then wudu with and without intention are equal, so the a fortiori argument fails. The commentator responds by distinguishing between the person and the act: though intention is void for the disbeliever, the act of wudu itself is more perfect with intention, so the a fortiori reasoning holds. This concludes the discussion on the disbeliever's wudu.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intention in the heart to perform an act of worship. Here, its role in the validity of wudu.
لغو (laghw): Void or meaningless; here referring to the disbeliever's intention being invalid due to lack of eligibility to perform the intended act of worship.
أولوية (awlawiyyah): A fortiori reasoning; if a weaker case is valid, a stronger case is even more valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is a disbeliever's wudu without intention valid after embracing Islam?
A) Because intention is not a condition for the validity of wudu in Hanafi school.
B) Because the disbeliever's intention is always valid for any act.
C) Because wudu is only valid with intention for Muslims.
D) Because the disbeliever's wudu is never valid until Islam.

Key Takeaway
A disbeliever's wudu without intention is valid according to Hanafis because water purifies by itself; intention is not a condition for wudu.

Timing of Tayammum: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Ruling on timing of tayammum with inter-madhhab dispute and usul basis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on performing tayammum before the prayer time and explain the legal basis (khalaf mutlaq vs khalaf daruri) for the difference.

Core Idea
Tayammum before prayer time is valid for Hanafis because it is an absolute substitute; Shafi'is restrict it to necessity.

This passage from al-Hidayah's commentary (al-‘Inayah) addresses a classic inter-madhhab dispute: may tayammum be performed before the prayer time enters? The Hanafi school answers 'yes,' while al-Shafi‘i says 'no.' The difference stems from a deeper usul principle—whether tayammum is an 'absolute substitute' (khalaf mutlaq) for water, removing impurity entirely, or merely a 'necessary substitute' (khalaf ḍarūrī) that permits prayer without truly purifying. We will walk through the reasoning and the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
The matn states: 'It is valid in the time by agreement and before it contrary to al-Shafi‘i.' Note that both schools agree on validity during the time; the dispute is only about before the time.
2
Trace the disagreement to its usul root
The commentator explains that al-Shafi‘i views tayammum as a 'necessary substitute' (khalaf ḍarūrī): it exists only for the necessity of fulfilling the prayer obligation and does not remove the underlying impurity (hadath). Therefore, it cannot precede the need (the prayer time).
The analogy given is the purification of a mustahadah (woman with chronic bleeding)—her purification is only for the obligation, not genuine.
3
Identify the Hanafi principle
Hanafis consider tayammum an 'absolute substitute' (khalaf muṭlaq): it completely removes impurity (yarfa‘ al-ḥadath) just like wudu, until water is found. Hence it can be performed in advance, just as wudu may be done before the prayer time.
4
Understand the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
A Hanafi may make tayammum as soon as he knows he will not have water for the next prayer, even if hours remain before the time. A Shafi‘i must wait until the time enters.
5
Evaluate the author's choice of presentation
The commentator notes that the author deliberately included both the agreed and disputed points to be more comprehensive, even though it adds length. This reflects a pedagogical preference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويصح في الوقت اتفاقاً وقبله خلافاً للشافعي، فلا يجوز به الصلاة في أول الوقت عنده، هذا بناءً على ما عُرِفَ في أصول الفقه: أنَّ التراب خلف ضروري للماء عنده، وعندنا: خلف مطلق.
قوله: اتفاقاً؛ وهي بيننا وبين الشافعي، بل بين سائر العلماء. فإن قلت: لما كان هذا اتفاقيّاً فلا حاجة إلى ذكره فلو قال: ويصح قبل الوقت لكان أفيد وأوجز. قلت: نعم، ولهذا لم يذكره الشارح في «مختصره»، لكن المصنف نظر إلى أن ذكر المسألة الاتفاقية والاختلافيّة كليهما أفيد وأحسن من ذكر أحدهما، فلذا ذكرهما مرتباً؛ الاتفاقي أولاً، والاختلاف ثانياً.
قوله: وعندنا: خلف مطلق؛ توضيحه: أن صفة الخلفية عندنا مطلقة: كاملة، وعنده ضرورية، والخلف الضروري عبارة عما تثبت خلفيته للضرورة لا وهي ضرورة الحاجة إلى إسقاط الفرض عن الذمة مع قيام الحدث كما في طهارة المستحاضة. فعنده التيمم خلف عن الوضوء، وإن شئت قلت: التراب خلف بالماء، بمعنى أنه يحكم بالطهارة به لأداء الفرض، وليس برافع للحدث حقيقة، فلهذا لم يجوز تقديمه قبل الوقت؛ لعدم وجود الحاجة المحوجة إليه. وعندنا هو خلف مطلق بمعنى أنه يرتفع به الحدث إلى غاية وجود الماء فهو أيضاً طهور ورافع للحدث كأصله، فكما أن الوضوء جائز قبل الوقت يكون التيمم أيضاً.
(ينظر: «السعاية» (1: 536)، «المنهاج» (1: 105)، «النقاية» (1: 116).
And it is valid in the time by agreement and before it contrary to al-Shafi'i, so prayer with it is not permissible at the beginning of the time according to him. This is based on what is known in usul al-fiqh: that soil is a necessary substitute for water according to him, and according to us, it is an absolute substitute.
His saying: 'by agreement' – agreement between us and al-Shafi'i, indeed among all scholars. If you say: Since it is agreed upon, there is no need to mention it; if he said 'and valid before the time' it would be more beneficial and concise. I say: Yes, for this reason the commentator did not mention it in his Mukhtasar, but the author considered that mentioning both the agreed and disputed matters is more beneficial and better than mentioning one of them, so he mentioned them in order, the agreed first then the disputed.
His saying: 'and according to us: absolute substitute' – its explanation: that the attribute of substitution according to us is absolute and complete, and according to him necessary. The necessary substitute is that which is established as a substitute due to necessity, and it is the necessity of need to drop the obligation from the responsibility while the state of impurity persists, as in the purification of a mustahadah. According to him, tayammum is a substitute for wudu, or if you wish, soil is a substitute for water, meaning that purification is ruled by it for performing the obligation, but it does not truly remove the impurity. Therefore, he does not permit performing it before the time due to the absence of the need that necessitates it. According to us, it is an absolute substitute, meaning that impurity is removed by it until the existence of water, so it is also purifying and remover of impurity like its original. Just as wudu is permissible before the time, so too is tayammum.
(Refer to: al-Sa'aya 1:536, al-Minhaj 1:105, al-Nuqaya 1:116)
Source pages p. 434

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on the timing of tayammum, specifically whether it is valid before the prayer time enters. The matn states that tayammum is valid during the time by agreement, and before the time according to Hanafis but not according to Shafi'i. The commentator explains that the basis of this difference is the legal principle of substitution: Shafi'i considers tayammum a necessary substitute for water, meaning it only becomes valid when water is inaccessible at the time of prayer, and it does not truly remove impurity but only permits prayer. Hanafis consider tayammum an absolute substitute, meaning it is a full purification that removes the state of hadath until water is available. Therefore, just as wudu can be performed before the prayer time (since it is a form of purification in advance), tayammum can also be performed before the time. The commentator also addresses a potential objection: why mention the agreed-upon point? The author includes both to be thorough.

Key Terms
خلف ضروري (khalaf ḍarūrī): Necessary substitute: tayammum is only valid as a substitute for water when necessary (e.g., no water at prayer time), and it does not remove impurity but only permits prayer.
خلف مطلق (khalaf muṭlaq): Absolute substitute: tayammum is a complete substitute for water, removing the state of hadath until water is available.
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution with clean soil as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Tayammum is a necessary substitute (khalaf daruri) like the purification of a mustahadah.
B) Tayammum is an absolute substitute (khalaf mutlaq) that removes hadath until water is found.
C) Tayammum is not a substitute but a separate form of purification.
D) Tayammum is valid only when water is unavailable at the exact prayer time.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits tayammum before the prayer time because it considers tayammum an absolute substitute that removes impurity until water is found, analogous to wudu.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
6 min
Validity of Tayammum Before Prayer Time: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Explaining the Hanafi ruling on tayammum before prayer time and the usul al-fiqh basis for the dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits tayammum before the prayer time using the concept of khalaf mutlaq, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on khalaf daruri.

Core Idea
Tayammum before prayer time is valid for Hanafis because it is an absolute substitute that removes hadath, not a mere necessity license.

In this lesson, we explore a seminal dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: can one perform tayammum before the actual time of prayer? The disagreement stems from a deeper usul al-fiqh principle regarding the nature of tayammum as a substitute for water. By understanding the Hanafi concept of khalaf mutlaq (absolute substitute) versus the Shafi'i khalaf daruri (necessary substitute), you will grasp not only this ruling but also how madhhab positions are built on foundational usul commitments.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: tayammum is valid both during and before the prayer time. This is the point of agreement (during time) and disagreement (before time).
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The Shafi'i school holds that tayammum before time is invalid. Understand their reasoning: tayammum is only a necessary substitute (khalaf daruri) that does not remove hadath but merely permits prayer; necessity is absent before time.
3
Follow the Shafi'i proof
Examine the Shafi'i argument: because tayammum is a khalaf daruri, it cannot be performed when there is no immediate need. This is tied to the idea that tayammum does not truly purify but only allows the prayer to be valid under duress.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school rebuts with: (1) a hadith calling earth a 'purification' (طهور) indicating it removes hadath, and (2) the principle of khalaf mutlaq – an absolute substitute that shares all rulings of the original (wudu). Thus, just as wudu is allowed before time, so is tayammum.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
State the practical consequence: a Hanafi may perform tayammum before the prayer time, while a Shafi'i must wait until the time enters. This affects daily practice in situations of anticipated water scarcity.

This is based on what is known in usul al-fiqh: that earth is a necessary substitute for water according to him (al-Shafi'i), and according to us it is an absolute substitute. So just as wudu is permissible before the time, tayammum is also permissible before the time. If you wish to see the proofs of the two opinions, refer to al-Tawdih and al-Talwih and their glosses, and we have mentioned a considerable amount of it in al-Sa'ayah. And regarding two vessels, one pure and one impure, tayammum is permissible according to us, contrary to him. And his statement (the hadith): 'Pure earth is a purification for the Muslim even for ten pilgrimages' supports what we said. It is permissible before the time. [1] His saying: 'contrary to him' — he says tayammum is not permissible, rather he must do taharri (investigation); because he certainly has pure water, able to use it by a proof considered valid in the Shari'ah, which is taharri, so there is no necessity, so tayammum is not allowed. According to us, taharri is not allowed because earth is an absolute purifier when unable to find water, and inability has been realized by the contradiction leading to cancellation. That is as in al-Talwih, and in it also: 'It is not hidden that the invalidity of tayammum before taharri according to al-Shafi'i is based on the view that tayammum is not valid without inability to use water, whether it is a necessary or absolute substitute, and there is no inability with the possibility of taharri; so he allowed tayammum when one is confused. So the deduction of this issue on tayammum being a necessary substitute in the sense that it is only to the extent that necessity is repelled is not as it should be, and if he intended that it is necessary that it is only when there is the necessity of inability to use water, then this would not be a matter of dispute.' [2] His saying: 'earth...' — the author of al-Hidayah mentioned this hadith in this wording, and did not mention the hadiths' transmitters who narrated it with this wording. Indeed, Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, and Ahmad narrated: 'Pure earth is the wudu of a Muslim even for ten pilgrimages; when he finds water, let him touch his skin with water.' It was authenticated by Ibn al-Qattan, and it is from the hadith of Abu Dharr.
Source pages p. 434

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the permissibility of tayammum (dry ablution) before the entry of prayer time. The commentator begins by stating the Hanafi ruling: tayammum is valid both during the prayer time and before it. The point of agreement is that it is valid during the time; the point of disagreement is before the time. The Shafi'i school holds that tayammum is not valid before the time because it is a 'necessary substitute' (khalaf daruri) for water, meaning it only permits performance of the prayer but does not remove ritual impurity (hadath). It is only allowed when necessity (i.e., inability to use water) is present, which does not exist before the time. The Hanafi school, on the other hand, holds that tayammum is an 'absolute substitute' (khalaf mutlaq) that removes hadath just like water, so it can be performed before the time just like wudu. The commentator clarifies that this is built on the usul al-fiqh principle of the nature of tayammum as a substitute. He then addresses a subsidiary issue: if one has two vessels, one pure and one impure, the Hanafis permit tayammum without taharri (investigation) while the Shafi'is require investigation. The Hanafis argue that because earth is an absolute purifier and the contradiction between the two vessels cancels the certainty of pure water, tayammum is valid without investigation. The commentator also provides the hadith 'Pure earth is a purification for the Muslim even for ten pilgrimages' as supporting evidence for the Hanafi view, showing that tayammum is not limited to necessity but is a general purification. The passage thus presents the full Hanafi position, the opposing Shafi'i view, the underlying principle, and the Hanafi response.

Key Terms
خلف ضروري (khalaf ḍarūrī): A substitute that is established only due to necessity; it does not fully replace the original but permits the performance of an obligation under duress.
خلف مطلق (khalaf muṭlaq): An absolute substitute that completely takes the place of the original, sharing all its rulings and effects.
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution using pure earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as explained in the text, why is tayammum permissible before the prayer time?
A) Because it is a necessity-driven substitute (khalaf daruri).
B) Because it is an absolute substitute (khalaf mutlaq) that removes ritual impurity like water.
C) Because the Prophet performed tayammum before prayer time.
D) Because there is consensus (ijma) on this point.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits tayammum before prayer time because it treats tayammum as a khalaf mutlaq that removes hadath, unlike the Shafi'i view of khalaf daruri.

Tayammum with Two Vessels: Pure and Impure
Ruling on tayammum when two vessels exist, one pure one impure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tayammum when two vessels are present and explain why investigation is not required.

Core Idea
When certainty is negated by contradiction, tayammum becomes permissible without investigation.

This lesson addresses a classic dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding tayammum when a person has two water vessels—one pure, one impure—and cannot tell them apart. The Hanafi position permits tayammum without investigation, while the Shafi'i school requires investigation to find the pure water. Understanding the reasoning behind each view deepens your appreciation of how the Hanafi school defines 'inability to use water.'

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the two positions
Understand the basic case: a person has two vessels, one containing pure water and the other impure, and cannot distinguish them. The Hanafi school says tayammum is permissible; the Shafi'i school requires investigation.
2
Analyze the Shafi'i argument
The Shafi'i view holds that since pure water definitely exists, investigation (taharri) is a valid legal method to identify it, thus there is no inability to use water, and tayammum is invalid.
3
Understand the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school argues that the contradictory evidence (one vessel impure) negates the certainty of pure water. Water is effectively inaccessible, so the earth as a purifier (tahur) becomes applicable without investigation.
4
Examine the hadith proof
The hadith 'Al-turabu tuhuru al-muslimi wa law ila 'ashri hijaj' (The pure earth is a purifier for the Muslim even up to ten Hajj periods) supports the Hanafi view that earth is an absolute purifier, not a mere substitute of necessity.
5
Apply the mufta bihi ruling
In practice, a Hanafi follower may perform tayammum without any investigation and pray. The mufta bihi is that tayammum is permissible before the prayer time as well.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ففي إنائين طاهر ونجس ، يجوز [التيمم] عندنا خلافاً له ، وقوله [ﷺ] : «التُّرَابُ طَهُورُ المُسْلِمِ وَلَوْ إِلَى عَشْرِ حِجَجٍ) يؤيِّدُ ما قلنا. جائز قبل الوقت، وإن شئت الاطلاع على أدلة القولين فارجع إلى «التوضيح» و«التلويح» وحواشيه، وقد ذكرنا قدراً معتداً منه في «السعاية».[1] قوله : خلافاً له ؛ فإنّه يقول : لا يجوز التيمم ، بل يجب عليه التحري ؛ إذ معه ماء طاهر بيقين ، يقدر على استعماله بدليل معتبر في الشرع وهو التحري، فلا ضرورة حينئذ، فلا يباح التيمم. وعندنا لا يجوز التحري ؛ لأنّ التراب طهورٌ مطلق عند العجز عن الماء، وقد تحقق بالتعارض الموجب للتساقط. كذا في «التلويح ) ، وفيه أيضاً : «لا يخفى أنّ عدم صحة التيمم قبل التحري عند الشافعي مبني على أنه لا صحة للتيمم بدون العجز الماء، سواء كان خلفاً ضرورياً أو مطلقاً، ولا عجز مع إمكان التحري ؛ ولذا جوز عن التيمم فيما إذا تحيّر. فتفريع هذه المسألة على كون التيمم خلفاً ضرورياً بمعنى أنه إنما يكون بمقدار ما تندفع به الضرورة ليس كما ينبغي، وإن أراد بكونه ضرورياً أن لا يكون إلا عند ضرورة العجز عن استعمال الماء، فهذا مما لا يتصوّر النزاع فيه ))
So in two vessels, pure and impure, tayammum is permitted in our school, contrary to him. And his saying (peace be upon him): 'The pure earth is a purifier for the Muslim, even up to ten Hajj periods' supports what we said. It is permissible before the time [of prayer]. And if you wish to examine the proofs of the two views, refer to al-Tawdih and al-Talwih and their glosses, and we have mentioned a moderate amount of it in al-Sa'ayah. [1] His statement: 'contrary to him'; for he says: tayammum is not permitted, rather he must investigate (taharri), because he has certain pure water with him, he is able to use it by a proof considered in the law, which is investigation, so there is no necessity at that point, thus tayammum is not permissible. And in our school, investigation is not permitted, because the earth is an absolute purifier when one is unable to use water, and [the certainty of pure water] has been negated by the contradiction causing a drop [of certainty]. So it is in al-Talwih, and in it also: 'It is not hidden that the invalidity of tayammum before investigation according to al-Shafi'i is based on the fact that tayammum is not valid without inability to use water, whether it is a substitute of necessity or absolute; and there is no inability with the possibility of investigation; therefore he permitted tayammum only when one is confused. So deriving this issue from the fact that tayammum is a substitute of necessity meaning that it is only to the extent that the necessity is repelled is not as it should be. And if by 'necessary' he meant that it only occurs at the necessity of inability to use water, then there is no room for dispute.'
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school. The issue: a person has two vessels, one containing pure water and the other impure, and he cannot determine which is which. The Hanafi position is that he may perform tayammum without investigation (taharri). The opposing view, attributed to Imam al-Shafi'i, is that he must investigate to find the pure water, and only if that fails can he use tayammum. The commentator explains the reasoning: The Shafi'i argues that since pure water exists certainly, there is no necessity for tayammum. The Hanafi response is that the certainty of pure water is negated by the contradictory evidence of the impure vessel, so effectively water is inaccessible. The hadith 'The pure earth is a purifier for the Muslim, even up to ten Hajj periods' supports the Hanafi view, showing that earth itself is a purifying agent, not merely a substitute of necessity. The commentator also notes that tayammum is permissible even before the prayer time, contrary to some understandings.

Key Terms
التيمم (al-tayammum): Dry ablution using pure earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
التحري (al-taharri): Legal investigation to determine which of two or more uncertain items is lawful, here trying to identify the pure water vessel.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) He must combine both by using the water and then tayammum.
D) He cannot perform any prayer until he finds certainty.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits tayammum without investigation when contradictory evidence negates the certainty of pure water, based on the principle that earth is a purifier in itself.

The Hadith of al-Sa'id al-Tayyib: Earth as a Purifier
Textual analysis of the hadith about earth being a purifier

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that tayammum is a rafi' li-l-hadath (purifier) using the hadith evidence and distinguish it from the view that it is merely a khalaf daruri (substitute of necessity).

Core Idea
The earth is inherently purifying; tayammum raises ritual impurity, not just permits acts.

This lesson examines the key hadith used by the Hanafi school to establish the legal nature of tayammum. The commentator refines the wording from al-Hidayah by citing the original narrations, showing that the word 'tuhur' confirms tayammum is an actual purifier. Understanding this distinction is crucial for knowing when and how tayammum can be performed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith and its variant wordings
The author of al-Hidayah mentioned the hadith with one wording; the commentator supplies the actual narrations from Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, and Ahmad, which state: 'Indeed the pure earth is a purifier as long as he does not find water, even up to ten Hajj periods.'
This step ensures we work with the most authoritative version.
2
Analyze the operative word 'tuhur'
The word 'tuhur' (with fatha) is derived from the root t-h-r meaning purification. The commentator takes it to mean 'mutahhir' (a purifier), implying that the earth itself has the property of removing ritual impurity.
In Hanafi usul, the form fu'ul (like tuhur) often indicates an inherent quality.
3
Understand the refutation of 'khalaf daruri'
The commentator explicitly states that the hadith shows tayammum is not a substitute of necessity (khalaf daruri) but rather a rafi' li-l-hadath (raiser of impurity). This directly counters the Shafi'i view that tayammum is merely a temporary permit.
This is a key point of intra- and inter-madhhab debate.
4
Derive the Hanafi ruling from the hadith
Since the earth is inherently purifying, tayammum is valid for any act requiring purity (e.g., prayer, touching the Quran) as long as water is absent. The condition 'ma lam yajid al-ma' shows it is not time-limited but lasts until water is found.
This derivation supports the Hanafi position that tayammum has full purifying power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[2] قوله : التراب... الخ، ذكر هذا الحديث بهذا اللفظ صاحب «الهداية»، ولم يذكر مخرجوا أحاديثها من أخرجه بهذا اللفظ ، نعم روى أبو داود والترمذي وأحمد : «إن الصعيد الطيب طهور ما لم يجد الماء، ولو عشر حجج» والبزار بلفظ : «الصعيد وضوء المسلم، وإن لم يجد الماء عشر سنين». فهذه الروايات وأمثالها صريحة في أنّ التيمم ليس بخلف ضروري، بل هو رافع للحدث، وأن التراب طهور - بالفتح - أي مطهر، وفي المقام أبحاث سؤالاً وجواباً ذكرناها في «السعاية».
[2] His statement: 'al-turabu... etc.', the author of al-Hidayah mentioned this hadith with this wording, and did not mention the hadith scholars who narrated it with this wording. Yes, Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, and Ahmad narrated: 'Indeed the pure earth is a purifier as long as he does not find water, even up to ten Hajj periods.' And al-Bazzar narrated with the wording: 'The earth is the ablution of the Muslim, even if he does not find water for ten years.' So these narrations and their like are explicit that tayammum is not a substitute of necessity, but rather it is an actual raiser of ritual impurity, and that al-turab is tuhur (with fatha) i.e. a purifier, and in this regard there are investigations questions and answers we have mentioned in al-Sa'ayah.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage is a textual refinement regarding the hadith used as proof for tayammum. The commentator notes that al-Hidayah quoted the hadith in a particular wording, but the actual narrations vary. He cites three versions: from Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, and Ahmad with the wording 'the pure earth is a purifier as long as he does not find water, even up to ten Hajj periods', and from al-Bazzar with 'the earth is the ablution of the Muslim, even if he does not find water for ten years'. The commentator then emphasizes that these narrations explicitly show that tayammum is not merely a substitute of necessity (khalaf daruri) but is an actual raiser of ritual impurity (rafi' li-l-hadath), and that the word 'tuhur' (with fatha on the first letter) means a purifier (mutahhir). This defends the Hanafi position that tayammum has inherent purifying power, not limited to temporary necessity. The commentator refers to his own work al-Sa'ayah for further discussion.

Key Terms
طهور (tuhur): A purifier; something that purifies others. Here used to describe earth's property in tayammum.
خلف ضروري (khalaf daruri): A substitute of necessity; something allowed only due to dire need, with minimum scope.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum with pure earth is a purifier, not a substitute of necessity, as evidenced by the hadith using the word 'tuhur'.

Tayammum When a Companion Refuses Water: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on tayammum when a companion refuses water, with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on tayammum when a companion has water and identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) of the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
If a companion refuses water, tayammum is valid; but whether you must ask first divides Abu Hanifa from his two disciples.

This lesson examines a practical scenario: you are traveling with a companion who has water, but you suspect he may refuse. Do you need to ask before performing tayammum? The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement on this point. By understanding the positions and their proofs, you will grasp how intention and certainty of refusal affect the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the point of disagreement
The act is performing tayammum when a companion has water. The disagreement is whether a request for water is required before tayammum.
The dispute is among the founding imams of the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa vs. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and the Sahibayn's position
Abu Hanifa holds that tayammum is valid even without requesting. The Sahibayn hold that it is not valid without requesting because water is potentially available.
The text in al-Hidayah explicitly states 'jaza khilafan lahuma' (it is permissible contrary to the two), indicating Abu Hanifa's view.
3
Compare the underlying reasoning
The Sahibayn reason that since water can be obtained by request, inability is not established. Abu Hanifa considers that if refusal is expected, the request is not necessary; the key is actual or certain inability.
The commentary explains that 'companion' is mentioned customarily; the ruling applies to anyone with water.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If a person prays with tayammum without asking and later obtains water, under Abu Hanifa the prayer is valid and not repeated. Under the Sahibayn, the prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
The passage also discusses nullification: if water is given before prayer, tayammum breaks; if after, prayer stands but tayammum voided for the future.
5
Identify the mufta bihi (operative ruling) and its source
Al-Hidayah presents Abu Hanifa's view as correct. However, al-Mabsut holds the opposite. Later Hanafi fatwa often follows the Sahibayn for caution unless refusal is certain.
The student should recognize that both views are preserved and the mufta bihi may vary by context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبعد طلبه من رفيق له ماءً مَنَعَه وقبل طلبه جازَ خلافاً لهما (وبعد طلبه من رفيق له ماءً مَنَعَه حتى إذا صلّى بعد المنع ، ثمَّ أعطاه ينتقض به التيمم الآن، فلا يعيدُ ما قد صلّى ، وقبل طلبه جاز خلافاً لهما)، هكذا ذكر في «الهداية»). وذكر في «المبسوط» : أنه إذا لم يطلب منه وصلَّى لم يجز؛ لأنَّ الماء مبذول[1] قوله : من رفيق؛ ذكره جارٍ مجرى العادة ؛ فإنَّ كلَّ مَن حضر وقت الصلاة وعنده ماء، فإنّ حكمه كذلك رفيقاً كان أو غيره، والحاصل أنَّ فاقد الماء إذا وجد عند رجل ماءً طلبه منه ؛ لعدم المنع غالباً، فإن طلبه منه ومنعه يتيمم، وبعد ذلك لو أعطاه فإن أعطاه قبل الصلاة لا يجوز صلاته بذلك التيمم ؛ لانتقاضه بالقدرة على الماء، وإن بعد الصلاة تمت صلاته وبطل تيمّمه في هذا الوقت ؛ لوجود القدرة حينئذ. أعطاه .
And after his requesting from a companion who had water and he refused him, [tayammum is valid], and before his requesting it is permissible, contrary to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad]. (And after his requesting from a companion who had water and he refused him, such that when he prayed after the refusal, then [the companion] gave him [water], his tayammum is broken by that now, so he does not repeat what he has prayed. And before his requesting it is permissible, contrary to the two.) Thus it is mentioned in al-Hidayah. And it is mentioned in al-Mabsut: if he did not request from him and prayed, it is not valid, because the water is available. [1] His statement: 'from a companion'; he mentioned it as a customary matter, because everyone who is present at prayer time and has water, his ruling is the same, whether companion or other. The gist is that one who lacks water, if he finds water with a man, he requests it from him, because usually there is no refusal. If he requests and [the man] refuses, he performs tayammum. After that, if [the man] gives him [water] — if he gives before prayer, his prayer with that tayammum is not valid, because it is nullified by ability to use water; and if after prayer, his prayer is complete and his tayammum becomes void at that time, because ability exists then.

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about tayammum when a companion has water. The ruling from al-Hidayah: if a person asks a companion for water and is refused, then performs tayammum and prays, his prayer is valid even if the companion later gives water. If he does not ask before praying, the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it is not valid, but the text states 'jaza'(it is permissible) contrary to them', meaning the relied-upon view is that it is valid even without asking. However, al-Mabsut reports that if he does not ask and prays, it is not valid because water is available. The commentator clarifies that the mention of 'companion' is just customary; the same applies to any person. The essential rule: if a person finds water with someone, he should request it because typically it is given. If refused, tayammum is valid. If the water is given after prayer, the prayer stands but future tayammum is void.

Key Terms
رفيق (rafiq): A companion or fellow traveler; used customarily in the ruling, but the same rule applies to any person with water.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on whether requesting water is a prerequisite for tayammum when a companion has water; the practical difference lies in the validity of a prayer performed without asking.

Ruling on Asking for Water from a Companion Before Tayammum
Intra-Hanafi dispute on obligation to ask for water before tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on asking for water before tayammum, identify the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and apply the ruling to scenarios of water availability before or after prayer.

Core Idea
Before tayammum, you must ask for water from anyone who has it — or your prayer is invalid.

This lesson examines a key ruling from Al-Hidayah on the obligation to seek water before resorting to tayammum. The core issue is whether a person who has no water must request it from another who has it, or whether tayammum is permissible without asking. The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). We will explore the evidence and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the condition
The act under discussion is tayammum (dry ablution). Its permissibility depends on the condition that water is not available. The question is: does 'not available' include situations where water is present but held by another person?
2
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa)
Abu Hanifa holds that it is wajib (obligatory) to ask for water from a person who has it. If one fails to ask and performs tayammum and prays, the prayer is invalid. This is the mufta bihi (operative) position.
The text states 'خلافاً لهما' (contrary to them), referring to the Sahibayn.
3
Recognize the Sahibayn's disagreement
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that it is not necessary to ask. Tayammum is valid without asking, even if water is present with another. Their reasoning is that the water is not under one's control.
The text says 'وقبل طلبه جاز خلافاً لهما' – allowing tayammum before asking is contrary to them.
4
Apply the ruling to temporal scenarios
If a person asks and is refused, then prays, and after prayer the water is given: the prayer is valid, but tayammum is nullified for future acts. If the water is given before prayer, the tayammum is nullified and prayer is invalid. This applies only after asking.
The text: 'ثمَّ أعطاه ينتقض به التيمم الآن، فلا يعيدُ ما قد صلّى'
5
Understand the evidence
The Hadith 'إن الصعيد الطيب طهور ما لم يجد الماء' indicates that tayammum is valid as long as water is not found. Finding water here means actual possession or ability to obtain it by asking, per Abu Hanifa.
The text cites Al-Bazzar's narration to support that tayammum is not merely a substitute but a purification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبعد طلبه من رفيق له ماءً منعه وقبل طلبه جاز خلافاً لهما (وبعد طلبه من رفيق لـه مـاءٌ مَنَعَه حتى إذا صلّى بعد المنع، ثمَّ أعطاه ينتقض به التيمم الآن، فلا يعيدُ ما قد صلّى، وقبل طلبه جاز خلافاً لهما)، هكذا ذكر في «الهداية»). وذكر في «المبسوط»: أنه إذا لم يطلب منه وصلَّى لم يجز؛ لأنَّ الماء مبذول بلفظ: «إنّ الصعيد الطيب طهور ما لم يجد الماء، ولو عشر.، والبزار بلفظ: الصعيد وضوء المسلم، وإن لم يجد الماء عشر سنين». فهذه الروايات وأمثالها صريحة في أنّ التيمم ليس بخلف ضروري، بل هو رافع للحدث، وأن التراب طهور - بالفتح - أي مطهر، وفي المقام أبحاث سؤالاً وجواباً ذكرناها في «السعاية». قوله: من رفيق؛ ذكره جارٍ مجرى العادة؛ فإنَّ كلَّ مَن حضر وقت الصلاة وعنده ماء، فإنّ حكمه كذلك رفيقاً كان أو غيره، والحاصل أنَّ فاقد الماء إذا وجد عند رجل ماءً طلبه منه؛ لعدم المنع غالباً، فإن طلبه منه ومنعه يتيمم، وبعد ذلك لو أعطاه فإن أعطاه قبل الصلاة لا يجوز صلاته بذلك التيمم؛ لانتقاضه بالقدرة على الماء، وإن بعد الصلاة تمت صلاته وبطل تيمّمه في هذا الوقت؛ لوجود القدرة حينئذ.
And after he asks from a companion who has water and he prevents him, and before his asking it is permissible, contrary to them (the two). (And after he asks from a companion who has water and he prevents him, such that when he prays after the prevention, then he gives him, the tayammum is nullified by it now, so he does not repeat what he has prayed, and before his asking it is permissible, contrary to them.) Thus it is mentioned in al-Hidayah. And it is mentioned in al-Mabsut: that if he does not ask from him and prays, it is not permissible, because water is available. With the wording: 'Indeed, pure earth is a purification as long as he does not find water, even for ten years.' And al-Bazzar with the wording: 'Pure earth is the ablution of the Muslim, even if he does not find water for ten years.' So these narrations and their like are explicit that tayammum is not a necessary substitute, but rather it removes the state of impurity, and that earth is tahur (with fat-h) meaning purifier. And in this place there are investigations of questions and answers which we have mentioned in al-Si'aya. His saying: 'from a companion'; he mentioned it as is customary, for indeed everyone who is present at the time of prayer and has water, his ruling is likewise, whether a companion or other. The summary is that the one who lacks water, when he finds water with a man, he asks him for it, because she is generally not prevented. If he asks him and he prevents him, he performs tayammum. After that, if he gives him, then if he gives him before prayer, his prayer with that tayammum is not permissible, because it is nullified by ability to use water. And if after the prayer, his prayer is complete and his tayammum becomes void at this time, due to the existence of ability then.
Source pages p. 436

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from Al-Hidayah concerning the requirement of asking for water before performing tayammum when another person has water. The matn states that if one asks a companion for water and is refused, tayammum is valid. However, if he prays and then receives water before the prayer, his tayammum is nullified and the prayer is invalid; if he receives water after the prayer, the prayer is valid. The Sahibayn differ on whether asking is necessary; they allow tayammum without asking. The commentary then cites Al-Mabsut, which holds that if one does not ask at all, the prayer is invalid because water was available. The author supports this with hadiths indicating that tayammum is a valid purification and not merely a last resort. The commentary clarifies that the mention of 'companion' is just customary; the ruling applies to anyone who has water. The summary: a person without water must ask; if refused, he may do tayammum; if given before prayer, tayammum breaks; if after, prayer is valid.

Key Terms
رفيق (rafīq): A companion, specifically a travel companion in this context, but the ruling applies to any person who has water.
منع (mana'a): To prevent or refuse to give water when asked.
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution with earth as a purification when water is not available.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, if a person without water asks a companion for water, the companion refuses, and then the person performs tayammum and prays. After prayer, the companion gives him water. What is the ruling on his prayer?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid but tayammum is nullified and he must repeat.
C) The prayer is valid and tayammum remains valid.
D) The prayer is valid and tayammum is nullified but no repetition is required.

Key Takeaway
Before tayammum, you must request water from anyone who has it; failure to ask invalidates the prayer, but if you ask and are refused, your prayer is valid even if water appears later.

The Obligation to Ask for Water: Refuting the View of Hasan ibn Ziyad
Presents the view of Hasan ibn Ziyad that asking is humiliating and the response refuting it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on asking for water before tayammum and explain why the majority refutes Hasan ibn Ziyad's argument based on humiliation and hardship.

Core Idea
Asking for necessary water is not humiliation; it is an obligation because water is customarily shared.

This lesson examines a rare intra-Hanafi dispute: Hasan ibn Ziyad argued that asking a companion for water before tayammum involves humiliation (dhull) and hardship (haraj), and since tayammum was legislated to remove hardship, one may proceed without asking. The majority of Hanafi scholars, including Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, rejected this view. By studying the arguments, you will understand how the school uses custom ('urf) and prophetic practice to uphold the obligation of asking.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Position
Identify the ruling (hukm) that the majority holds. According to al-Mabsut, it is wajib to ask for water from a companion before tayammum. This is the position of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
The source explicitly says 'عليه أن يسأله' (he must ask him).
2
Identify the Opposing View and Its Basis
Hasan ibn Ziyad argues that asking entails humiliation (dhull) and hardship (haraj). Since tayammum was legislated to remove hardship, obligating asking would contradict the purpose of tayammum. He concludes that one may perform tayammum without asking.
Hasan's view is from the nawadir (rare transmissions) within the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the Opponent's Proof
The proof is a qiyas: asking causes hardship; tayammum is for removing hardship; therefore, asking cannot be obligatory. The minor premise is that any asking, especially for people of status, is inherently degrading.
The text mentions 'أرباب الوجاهة والمروءة' (people of dignity and manliness) to emphasize the perceived humiliation.
4
Examine the Hanafi Response
The response (لكنا نقول) rejects the claim that all asking is humiliating. Water for purification is customarily given freely (مبذول عادة), so asking for it is not degrading. Moreover, the Prophet himself asked for necessities, proving that asking for needs is not humiliating per se. Hardship only arises from excessive or unnecessary asking.
The text uses 'ماء الطهارة مبذول' (water for purification is given freely) and the prophetic example as counter-proofs.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf and Mufta Bihi
The practical consequence: if one does not ask and prays, the prayer is invalid according to the majority, but valid according to Hasan. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the majority view—obligation to ask.
This highlights that intra-madhhab differences can have real-world effects on validity of acts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي موضع آخر من «المبسوط»: إنه إن كان مع رفيقه ماءٌ فعليه أن يسأله إلا على قول حسن بن زياد له: فإِنَّهُ يقولُ السُّؤال ذل" وفيه بعض الحرج، ولم يشرع التيمم إلا لدفع الحرج. ولكنا نقول: ماء الطهارة مبذول عادة وليس في سؤال ما يُحتاج إليه مذلة، فقد قوله: السؤال ذل؛ حاصل دليل الحسن القائل بعدم وجوب طلب الماء من رفيقه، وجواز التيمم بدون الطلب أنّ السؤال من الغير لا يخلو عـن عيب وذلّة، لا سيما عند أرباب الوجاهة والمروءة. وفيه؛ أي في السؤال أو فى الذلّ اللازم منه بعض الحرج، فلو وجب للزم وجوب بعض أقسام الحرج، مع أنَّ التيمم لم يشرع إلا لدفع الحرج، كما يفيده قوله بعد ذكر التيمم: ﴿ مَا يُرِيدُ اللهُ لِيَجْعَلَ عَلَيْكُم مِّنْ حَرَج وَلَكِن يُرِيدُ لِيُطَهِّرَكُمْ ﴾ قوله: لكنا نقول؛ هذا جواب من قبل القائلين بوجوب الطلب عن دليل الحسن، وحاصله: أنّ ماء الطهارة مبذول فيما بين الناس عادة، فإنهم لا يستنكفون عن أخذه وإعطائه، وما يكون كذلك لا يكون في سؤاله ذل، وإنما هو في سؤال ما لا يكون كذلك. وأيضاً: كون مطلق السؤالِ باعثاً للذلّة والحرج ممنوع، فقد ثبت أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم سأل الحوائج الضرورية من غيره، وأي جاه أعظمُ من الجاهِ النبوي)، وإنما الحرجُ والذل في إكثار السؤال، وفي سؤال ما لا يحتاج إليه.
And in another place from al-Mabsut: that if his companion has water, then he must ask him, except according to the saying of Hasan ibn Ziyad: for he says that asking is humiliation and in it is some hardship, and tayammum was only legislated to remove hardship. But we say: water for purification is ordinarily given, and there is no degradation in asking for what is needed. (His saying: asking is humiliation; the summary of the proof of Hasan, who says that it is not obligatory to ask for water from his companion and that tayammum is permissible without asking, is that asking from others is not free from defect and humiliation, especially for people of dignity and manliness. And in it—meaning in the asking or the humiliation necessarily following from it—is some hardship. So if it were obligatory, it would necessitate obligating some type of hardship, while tayammum was only legislated to remove hardship, as is indicated by His saying after mentioning tayammum: 'Allah does not intend to make any hardship upon you, but He intends to purify you.' His saying: but we say; this is a response from those who hold the obligation of asking against the proof of Hasan. Its summary is that water for purification is ordinarily given among people, for they are not averse to taking and giving it, and what is like that has no humiliation in asking for it. Rather, humiliation is in asking for what is not like that. Also, that all asking causes degradation and hardship is denied, for it is established that the Prophet (peace be upon him) asked for necessary needs from others, and what status is greater than prophetic status? Rather, hardship and degradation are in excessive asking and in asking for what is not needed.
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This passage presents a further intra-Hanafi dispute from Al-Mabsut. It begins by stating the general rule: if one's companion has water, one must ask for it. However, Hasan ibn Ziyad holds an exceptional view: he argues that asking is humiliating and entails hardship, and since tayammum is meant to remove hardship, one may perform tayammum without asking. The commentary then expands on his argument: asking involves a defect and humiliation, especially for people of status and honor, and this hardship would contradict the purpose of tayammum. The text then provides the response: water for purification is commonly given and accepted without hesitation, so asking for it is not degrading. Moreover, the claim that all asking causes humiliation is false; the Prophet himself asked for necessary items, and his status is the highest. Hardship only arises from excessive asking or asking for unnecessary things. Therefore, the obligation to ask stands.

Key Terms
ذل (dhull): Humiliation or degradation, which Hasan ibn Ziyad claims is inherent in asking.
حرج (haraj): Hardship or difficulty, which tayammum was legislated to alleviate.
وجوب (wujūb): Obligation; the majority holds that asking for water is wajib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because water is cheap and easily available.
B) Because water for purification is ordinarily given without hesitation among people.
C) Because one must always ask for water before tayammum.
D) Because the Prophet asked for water.

Key Takeaway
The obligation to ask for water before tayammum stands because asking for necessary goods is not humiliating; hardship only comes from excessive or unnecessary requests.
