عمدة الرعاية على شرح الوقاية
وإن رأى في الصَّلاةِ فكما ذكر في «الزيادات».
[٢]
لكن يبقى صورتان :
أحدهما : أنه قطعَ الصَّلاةَ" فيما إذا ظنَّ المنع ، أو شك، فسأله فإن أعطي بطل تيممه ، وإن أبي فهو باق.
والأخرى : أنه إذا أتم الصلاة فيما إذا ظن أنه يعطى ، ثم سألَهُ فإن أعطى بطلت صلاته، وإن أبى تمت ؛ لأنه ظهرَ أنَّ ظنَّهُ كــان خـطـأ بخلاف مسألة التحري ؛ لأن القبلة حينئذ في جهةِ التَّحري أصالة، وهاهنا الحكم دائر على حقيقة القدرة والعجز، فأقيمَ غلبةُ الظَّن مقامَهُما تيسيراً ، فإذا ظهر خلافُهُ لم يبقَ قائماً مقامهما.
[١]قوله : فكما ذكر في «الزيادات»؛ أي الحكم على التفصيل المذكور، وهو أنه إن غلب على ظنه الإعطاء قطع الصلاة، وإلا لا. [٢]قوله : لكن يبقى صورتان ؛ يعني لا ذكر لهما في العبارات السابقة صريحاً، وإن كان قوله في «الزيادات»(۱) : (وإن أبى تمت صلاته»، يدلّ على حكمهما بإطلاقه وإشارته.
.
(۲)
[٣] قوله : إنه قطع الصلاة ؛ أي بجهله، وإن كان لا ينبغي له أن يفعل ذلك. [٤] قوله : إنه إذا أتم الصلاة ؛ أي بجهله أو بأمر آخر، وإن كان الواجب عليه في هذه الصورة القطع والسؤال ، و ما عرض للفاضل عصام الله أن القطع في هذه الصورة ليس بواجب، بل مندوب، فليس بصحيح، كما بيناه في «السعاية». [0] قوله : بخلاف...الخ ؛ جواب سؤال مقدر ، تقرير السؤال أنه لو اشتبهت على المصلّي جهة القبلة فتحرى إلى جهة وصلّى إليها ظانًا أنها جهة القبلة ، ثم ظهر بعد الفراغ أنّ الكعبة إلى جهة أخرى، فالحكم فيه على ما سيأتي في موضعه أنّ صلاته تامة، ولا تجب عليه الإعادة مع ظهور كون ظنّه خطأ، فما الفارق بين ما نحن فيه، حيث لم يعتبر الظن بعد ظهور الخطأ، وبين تلك المسألة؟
I say: If you want to encompass all the divisions: Know that if he sees water outside the prayer and prays and does not ask after the prayer to show inability or ability, then according to what is mentioned in al-Mabsut, it is not valid, whether he thinks it likely he will be given water, or not, or doubts both. And that is the issue of the matn. And if he sees during the prayer and does not ask after it, similarly. And if he sees outside the prayer and does not ask, and prays, then asks, if he is given, his prayer is invalid; if he is refused, his prayer is complete, whether he thought likely giving or refusal, or doubted both. [1] His saying: 'or doubted both' means in giving and not giving. That is because water is usually given, and there is no difficulty in asking for needs, so he must ask to show inability or ability, then pray with tayammum if refused, or with wudu if he finds water. And this is apparent in the case of doubt. And in the case of strong probability of giving, it is more apparent. As for the case of strong probability of not giving, there is consideration regarding the obligation of asking and the permissibility of tayammum without asking, because inability is then probable, and probability is considered in rulings, so tayammum should be permissible without asking. And that is what was mentioned in al-Dhakhirah from al-Jassas that this is the madhhab of Abu Hanifa, except that it may be said: The custom of giving water usually opposes it, so hesitation occurs and inability does not become apparent; rather, the probability of not giving is in the status of that which turns out to be wrong. [2] His saying: 'And that is the issue of the matn' means this form is the one mentioned in the matn. For if you say: This rules that the words of the matn and al-Mabsut agree, while his previous words rule contradiction. I say: They agree on the form of the issue, because each is set when he sees water outside prayer, and they differ in that the matn mentions the issue is disputed between Abu Hanifa and his two companions, while al-Mabsut mentions it is agreed upon among them. So the meaning of his saying 'and that is the issue of the matn' is that the subject of the mentioned issue is the subject of the one in al-Mabsut, although they differ in another respect. [3] His saying: 'his prayer' means that which he prayed with tayammum, because it appears that he had ability to water, and the shortcoming came from him where he did not ask. And if he sees during the prayer, then as mentioned in al-Ziyadat. [2] However, two cases remain: One: That he cuts the prayer when he thinks refusal or doubts, then asks; if he is given, his tayammum is invalid; if refused, it remains. The other: That he completes the prayer when he thinks he will be given, then asks; if he is given, his prayer is invalid; if refused, it is complete; because his assumption turned out to be wrong, unlike the case of qibla direction, because the qibla then is originally in the direction of ijtihad, and here the ruling revolves around the reality of ability and inability, so probability of assumption is put in their place for facilitation, and when its contrary appears, it no longer remains in their place. [1] His saying: 'as mentioned in al-Ziyadat' means the ruling on the detailed mention, that if he thinks likely giving, he cuts the prayer, otherwise not. [2] His saying: 'However, two cases remain' means they are not explicitly mentioned in the previous statements, although his words in al-Ziyadat: 'and if refused, his prayer is complete' indicates their ruling implicitly and by reference. [3] His saying: 'he cuts the prayer' means due to his ignorance, although he should not do that. [4] His saying: 'he completes the prayer' means due to his ignorance or another reason, although the obligation on him in this case is to cut and ask, and what al-Fadil Isam Allah presented that cutting in this case is not obligatory but recommended is not correct, as we explained in al-Si'ayah. [0] His saying: 'Unlike...' etc. is the answer to an implied question. The formulation of the question: If the direction of qibla is ambiguous for the worshipper, so he exerts ijtihad towards a direction and prays thinking it is the qibla, then after finishing it appears that the Ka'ba is in another direction, the ruling in that case, as will come in its place, is that his prayer is complete and he is not required to repeat despite his assumption being wrong. So what is the difference between our case, where the assumption is not considered after the error becomes apparent, and that case?
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah is a detailed commentary on a ruling regarding tayammum. It discusses the scenario where a person sees water after having performed prayer with tayammum. The central issue is whether he must ask for water after seeing it, and how his prayer is affected. The passage first clarifies that if he sees water outside prayer and prays without asking, then according to al-Mabsut, his prayer is invalid regardless of his assumption about being given water. The same applies if he sees water during prayer. However, if he sees water outside prayer, prays, then afterwards asks and is given water, the prayer is invalid; if refused, it is valid. The commentary explains that because water is customarily given, one must ask to determine actual ability or inability. In case of doubt or strong probability of being given, asking is obligatory; but if one strongly believes he will not be given, there is a debate: Abu Hanifa reportedly allows tayammum without asking because inability is probable, but this is countered by the custom of giving water, causing hesitation. The passage then reconciles al-Mabsut and the matn, noting they agree on the facts but differ on whether the ruling is disputed or agreed upon. Two additional cases are identified: (1) if he cuts the prayer when thinking refusal or doubting, then asks; (2) if he completes the prayer when thinking he will be given. In the latter, if his assumption proves wrong, his prayer is invalid because the assumption no longer holds. This is contrasted with qibla direction ijtihad, where the prayer remains valid even if wrong, because in qibla the ijtihad is original, whereas here the ruling depends on actual ability. The commentator also refutes a claim that cutting the prayer is not obligatory in the second case.

Key Terms
التيمم (al-tayammum): Dry ablution performed with clean earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
سؤال (su'al): Asking or requesting water from someone who is likely to give it, in the context of determining ability to use water.
غلبة الظن (ghalabat al-zann): Strong probability or dominant assumption about a matter, here about whether one will be given water.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a person sees water outside prayer, prays with tayammum without asking, and later asks and is given water, what is the ruling?
A) His prayer is valid because he already prayed.
B) His prayer is invalid because he did not ask first.
C) It depends on whether he thought he would be given water.
D) His tayammum is valid, so prayer is valid.

Key Takeaway
When water is seen after tayammum, the obligation to ask is central; the prayer's validity hinges on whether one asked and the actual outcome of asking.

Two Unmentioned Scenarios of Seeing Water During Prayer
Commentary expanding on two scenarios of seeing water during prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two scenarios of seeing water during prayer, apply the rule that predominant assumption is a temporary substitute for actual ability, and distinguish this from the qibla ijtihad case.

Core Idea
Predominant assumption about water substitutes for ability, but disappears when reality is known.

The commentator expands on a terse ruling from al-Ziyadat, clarifying two scenarios not spelled out previously. He then defends the ruling against a potential objection based on qibla ijtihad. Understanding these scenarios is key to knowing when prayer must be cut and when tayammum is invalidated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two cases: (a) cutting prayer when assuming denial or doubting, then asking; (b) completing prayer when assuming being given, then asking. For each, note the outcome based on whether water is actually given or denied.
Outcome determines validity of tayammum and prayer.
2
Determine the role of predominant assumption (ghalabat al-zann)
In both scenarios, the initial action is based on assumption, but the final ruling depends on actual outcome. Assumption is used as a proxy for ability only temporarily; when reality contradicts, the proxy falls away.
3
Contrast with qibla ijtihad
The commentator explains why, in qibla, the assumption is the basis of the obligation itself, so the prayer remains valid even if the direction is wrong. In tayammum, assumption is only a temporary stand-in for actual ability, so it is overridden when the truth emerges.
This is the key rational proof (dalil 'aqli) for the distinction.
4
Recognize the intra-madhhab dispute
Some scholars, such as al-Fadil 'Isam, held that cutting the prayer in the second scenario is only recommended (mandub), not obligatory. The commentator refutes this, affirming the mufta bihi as wajib.
The relied-upon position is that cutting is wajib when predominant assumption of being given water holds.
5
Apply to a new scenario
Given a specific case (e.g., a person on tayammum sees water during prayer and strongly assumes he will be given if he asks), determine the correct action and the post-asking ruling.
Use the two scenarios as models.

The summary of the answer: The qibla for the one to whom it is ambiguous is the direction of ijtihad; so the required act there is truly facing the direction of his ijtihad, and he did that, so the appearance of his assumption's error after finishing does not harm. Commentary
This passage is a commentary expanding on a brief ruling from al-Ziyadat about seeing water during prayer. The commentator, author of 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah, first notes that the earlier text only implied two scenarios, and he now makes them explicit. The first scenario: the person cuts his prayer out of ignorance (assuming he won't be given water or doubting), then asks. If water is given, his tayammum is invalidated; if refused, his tayammum remains valid. The second scenario: he completes his prayer assuming he will be given water, then asks. If he receives it, his prayer is invalidated; if refused, his prayer stands. The commentator then addresses a potential objection: why is the assumption not given weight after the error is discovered, unlike the case of qibla ijtihad where the prayer remains valid if the direction turns out wrong? The answer is that the qibla obligation is inherently based on ijtihad—the direction he faces is itself the wajib. But here the ruling depends on actual ability or inability to obtain water; predominant assumption was only a substitute for ease. Once the reality is known, the substitute falls away. The commentator also clarifies that cutting the prayer in the first scenario, though allowed, is not commendable if done ignorantly, and that one scholar's view that it is not obligatory is incorrect.

Key Terms
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution with dust as a substitute for wudu/ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
قطع الصلاة (qat' al-salah): To break or discontinue the prayer intentionally before completion.
غلبة الظن (ghalabat al-zann): Predominant assumption or strong probability, considered a valid basis for legal action in fiqh when certainty is unattainable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) In qibla, the direction of ijtihad is itself the wajib; in tayammum, the ruling is based on actual ability to get water.
C) Both cases are treated identically because both involve predominant assumption.
D) In tayammum, cutting is always required; in qibla, it is not.

Key Takeaway
Predominant assumption in tayammum is only a temporary proxy for actual ability; the ruling changes once reality is known, unlike qibla ijtihad where the assumption defines the obligation itself.

Multiple Prayers with One Tayammum: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Main ruling with refutation of Shafi'i view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on performing multiple prayers with one tayammum, identify the Shafi'i counter-argument, and evaluate the Hanafi response based on dalil naqli.

Core Idea
One tayammum suffices for unlimited prayers; the Shafi'i restriction is based on weak ahadith.

The question of how many prayers one can perform with a single tayammum arises in situations where water is unavailable. The Hanafi school holds that tayammum is a full substitute for wudu/ghusl and remains valid for any number of fard and nafl prayers until water is found. This lesson examines the proof for this position and the Shafi'i objection that tayammum should be limited to one fard.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling given in the matn: one tayammum suffices for both fard and nafl prayers without limit.
The Hanafi view is based on the general permission in the Quran.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position
Recognise that the Shafi'i school requires a separate tayammum for each fard prayer, though nafl prayers may be performed with the same tayammum as subordinate.
The Shafi'i justify this with a hadith from Ibn 'Abbas.
3
Follow the Shafi'i proof
Examine the Shafi'i evidence: the weak hadith narrated by al-Daraqutni and al-Bayhaqi, and the analogy that tayammum, as a substitute, should be limited like wudu.
The Hanafi response critiques the weakness of these ahadith.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand the Hanafi rebuttal: the Quranic verse (5:6) does not specify a limit; the ahadith cited are weak; Imam Muhammad's argument that seeking water does not invalidate tayammum.
The Hanafi rely on the clear, unqualified permission in the Quran.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Note the practical consequence: a Hanafi may pray all five daily prayers with one tayammum, while a Shafi'i must renew tayammum for each fard.
This difference affects travelers and those in water-scarce environments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويصلّي به ما شاء من فرض ونفل) خلافاً للشافعي [1]قوله : خلافاً للشافعي (۱) له ؛ فإنّ عنده يجب عليه أن يتيمم لكل فرض، ولا يصلي بتيمم واحد فرضين، نعم يصلّي به ما شاء من النوافل ؛ لأنها تابعة للفرائض، والحجة له كون التيمم خلفاً ضرورياً، وقد مرّ ما له وما عليه. وما أخرجه الدارقطني بسند ضعيف عن ابن عباس أنه قال : «من السنة أن لا يصلي بالتيمم أكثر من صلاة واحدة ) ، وما أخرجه البيهقي بسند ضعيف عن ابن عمر الله ، قال : «تيمم لكلّ صلاة ، فلا دلالة لهما على افتراض ذلك، وقد بسطنا الكلام فيه في «السعاية»(4). وفي كتاب «الحجج» للإمام محمد الله : «قال أهل المدينة : تيمم لكل صلاة، قال محمد : لأيّ شيءٍ قلتم أنه يتيمم لكل صلاة قالوا لأنّ عليه أن يبتغي ا الماء لكل صلاة، فلما ابتغى الماء ولم يجد يتيمم. قيل : وكيف وجب التيمم في ابتغاء الماء، ولم يوجد الماء، إنما يبتغي الماء ليجده فينتقض التيمم إذا وجد الماء وليس ينقضه ابتغاء الماء إذا لم يوجد ؛ لأنّ الله ل قال : فَلَمْ تَجِدُوا مَاءً فَتَيَمَّمُوا ) ، فرخص لمن لم يجد أن يتيمم، ولم يذكر ابتغاء الماء.
And he may pray with it as many fard and nafl as he wishes, contrary to al-Shafi'i. [1] His statement: 'contrary to al-Shafi'i' (1) because according to him he must perform tayammum for every fard, and he cannot pray two fard with one tayammum; yes, he may pray with it as many nafl as he wishes because they are subordinate to the fara'id. His argument is that tayammum is a necessary substitute, and what he has for and against has already passed. What al-Daraqutni narrated with a weak chain from Ibn 'Abbas that he said: 'It is from the sunnah not to pray with tayammum more than one prayer,' and what al-Bayhaqi narrated with a weak chain from Ibn 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) that he said: 'Perform tayammum for every prayer,' there is no indication from these two that it is obligatory. And we have discussed it extensively in al-Si'ayah (4). And in the book al-Hujaj of Imam Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him): 'The people of Madinah said: Perform tayammum for every prayer. Muhammad said: Why do you say that one should perform tayammum for every prayer? They said: Because he must seek water for every prayer, so when he seeks water and does not find it, he performs tayammum.' It was said: And how is tayammum obligated in seeking water when water is not found? He only seeks water to find it, so tayammum is invalidated when he finds water, and seeking water when it is not found does not invalidate it, because Allah said: '...and you find no water, then perform tayammum...' (5:6), so He permitted the one who does not find water to perform tayammum, and did not mention seeking water.
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute about whether one can perform multiple fard prayers with a single tayammum. The Hanafi position, stated in the matn, is that one may pray any number of fard and nafl prayers with one tayammum as long as the tayammum remains valid (i.e., until water is found or the excuse ends). The Shafi'i school holds that tayammum only suffices for one fard prayer; however, any number of nafl prayers may be prayed because nafl are subordinate to fard. The Shafi'i argument is that tayammum is a necessity substitute, so it should be restricted. The Hanafi response, elaborated by Imam Muhammad in his work al-Hujaj, refutes the Shafi'i claim: the ahadith cited by them (from Ibn 'Abbas and Ibn 'Umar) are weak, and the primary evidence from the Qur'an (5:6) only conditions the obligation of tayammum on not finding water, not on seeking water for each prayer. The obligation is to seek water only if one is certain water exists; otherwise, the tayammum remains valid for unlimited prayers. Imam Muhammad's rebuttal to the people of Madinah (Malikis) is also cited: seeking water does not invalidate tayammum; only finding water does.

Key Terms
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution with dust as a substitute for wudu/ghusl when water is unavailable.
فرض (fard): An obligatory religious duty, such as the five daily prayers.
نفل (nafl): Supererogatory or voluntary acts of worship beyond the obligatory ones.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary Hanafi evidence for performing multiple fard prayers with one tayammum?
A) A hadith from Ibn 'Abbas with a sound chain.
B) The Quranic verse (5:6) that does not limit tayammum to one prayer.
C) Consensus of the Companions.
D) The necessity of water for each prayer.

Key Takeaway
One tayammum is valid for multiple fard and nafl prayers until water is found, based on the Quranic permission and the weakness of restrictive ahadith.

Multiple Prayers with One Tayammum: Hanafi View
Hanafi ruling and inter-madhhab dispute on multiple prayers with one tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing multiple prayers with one tayammum and explain the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i objection.

Core Idea
One tayammum suffices for any number of prayers — it remains valid until nullified, just like wudu.

This lesson examines a key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the scope of a single tayammum. While the Shafi'i school requires a fresh tayammum for each obligatory prayer, the Hanafi school permits any number of obligatory and voluntary prayers with one tayammum. Understanding the reasoning behind each position is essential for appreciating how the Hanafi school applies analogy and weakens opposing evidence.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the core ruling: one tayammum suffices for any number of fard and nafl prayers. This is the mufta bihi position from Zahir al-Riwayah.
The matn clearly states 'ويصلّى به ما شاء من فرض ونفل'.
2
Identify the opposing school
Note that the passage explicitly says 'خلافاً للشافعي' (contrary to al-Shafi'i). The Shafi'i school requires a separate tayammum for each fard prayer, though multiple nafl are allowed.
The Shafi'i view is based on tayammum being a concession (rukhsah), not a full substitute.
3
Examine the Hanafi dalil
The Hanafi proof is Quran 5:6 (the permission for tayammum when no water is found) and analogy with wudu: tayammum is a substitute (khalaf) for wudu, so it remains valid until nullified.
The passage also draws an analogy with the qibla ruling: one's best effort suffices even if later found wrong.
4
Examine the Shafi'i dalil
The Shafi'i rely on weak hadith from Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar that one should not pray more than one prayer with tayammum.
The passage explicitly notes these hadith are weak (sahif) and do not prove obligation.
5
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response argues that the Quran does not limit tayammum, weak hadith cannot override the clear analogy with wudu, and the burden of proof for limitation lies on the opponent.
Imam Muhammad's 'al-Hujaj' also rebuts the Medinan view that one must seek water for each prayer.

كتاب الطهارة التيمم ويصلّى به ما شاء من فرض ونفل (ويصلّي به ما شاء من فرض ونفل) خلافاً للشافعي وحاصل الجواب : إنَّ القبلة في حق من اشتبهت عليه هي جهة التحري ، فالواجب هناك حقيقة هو الاستقبالُ إلى جهة تحريه ، وقد فعل فلا يضر ظهور خطأ ظنّه بعد الفراغ، وفيما نحن فيه الحكم دائرٌ على حقيقةِ القدرة والعجز عن الماء، وأقيمت غلبة الظن مقامهما للتيسير، فإذا بان خلافه لم يبقَ غلبة الظن قائماً مقامهما ، فلذلك لم تعتبر إذا ظهر خلاف ما ظنّه. قوله : خلافاً للشافعي له ؛ فإنّ عنده يجب عليه أن يتيمم لكل فرض، ولا يصلي بتيمم واحد فرضين، نعم يصلّي به ما شاء من النوافل ؛ لأنها تابعة للفرائض، والحجة له كون التيمم خلفاً ضرورياً، وقد مرّ ما له وما عليه. وما أخرجه الدارقطني بسند ضعيف عن ابن عباس أنه قال : «من السنة أن لا يصلي بالتيمم أكثر من صلاة واحدة ) ، وما أخرجه البيهقي بسند ضعيف عن ابن عمر الله ، قال : «تيمم لكلّ صلاة ، فلا دلالة لهما على افتراض ذلك، وقد بسطنا الكلام فيه في «السعاية». وفي كتاب «الحجج» للإمام محمد الله : «قال أهل المدينة : تيمم لكل صلاة، قال محمد : لأيّ شيءٍ قلتم أنه يتيمم لكل صلاة قالوا لأنّ عليه أن يبتغي الماء لكل صلاة، فلما ابتغى الماء ولم يجد يتيمم. قيل : وكيف وجب التيمم في ابتغاء الماء، ولم يوجد الماء، إنما يبتغي الماء ليجده فينتقض التيمم إذا وجد الماء وليس ينقضه ابتغاء الماء إذا لم يوجد ؛ لأنّ الله قال : فَلَمْ تَجِدُوا مَاءً فَتَيَمَّمُوا ) ، فرخص لمن لم يجد أن يتيمم، ولم يذكر ابتغاء الماء. ينظر: «مغني المحتاج»(۱ : ۹۸). في سنن الدارقطني (۲) : ۱۸۵) ، وغيره، قال ابن حجر في الدراية (١ : ٦٨) : «إسناده واه». في معرفة السنن والآثار (۱) : (۲۳)، قال ابن حجر في الدراية (١) : (٦٨) : رواه البيهقي بسند صحيح. (السعاية» (١) : ٥٤٦). المائدة : من الآية ٦ .
The book of purification: Tayammum. And one may pray with it whatever he wishes of obligatory and voluntary (prayers). (And one may pray with it whatever he wishes of obligatory and voluntary) contrary to al-Shafi'i. The summary of the answer: Indeed the qibla for one whom it is ambiguous is the direction of one's best effort (taharrī); so the obligation there is actually facing the direction of his best effort, and he has done it, so the appearance of error in his assumption after completion does not harm. In our case here, the ruling revolves around the reality of ability and inability to obtain water. Overwhelming probability (ghalabat al-ẓann) is established in their place for ease. So if the opposite becomes clear, overwhelming probability no longer stands in their place, therefore it is not considered if the opposite of what he assumed appears. His saying: 'contrary to al-Shafi'i' – for him (al-Shafi'i) indeed he holds that one must perform tayammum for every obligatory prayer, and may not pray two obligatory prayers with one tayammum. Yes, he may pray with it whatever he wishes of voluntary prayers because they are dependent on the obligatory. His proof is that tayammum is a substitute of necessity, and we have already mentioned its proofs and counter-proofs. And what al-Daraqutni narrated with a weak chain from Ibn 'Abbas that he said: 'It is from the sunna not to pray with tayammum more than one prayer', and what al-Bayhaqi narrated with a weak chain from Ibn 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with them) that he said: 'Perform tayammum for every prayer.' Both of these do not indicate the obligation of that. And we have expanded discussion on it in 'al-Si'aya'. And in the book 'al-Hujaj' of Imam Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him): 'The people of Medina said: Perform tayammum for every prayer. Muhammad said: For what reason do you say that one should perform tayammum for every prayer? They said: Because he must seek water for every prayer. So when he seeks water and does not find it, he performs tayammum.' It was said: 'How is tayammum obligated in seeking water when water is not found? He only seeks water to find it, so tayammum is nullified if he finds water. Seeking water does not nullify it when water is not found, because Allah said: 'And you do not find water, then perform tayammum' (Quran 5:6). So He granted permission to one who does not find to perform tayammum, and He did not mention seeking water.' Reference: Mughnī al-Muḥtāj (1:98). In Sunan al-Daraqutni (2:185) and others; Ibn Hajar in al-Dirāya (1:68) said: 'Its chain is weak.' In Ma'rifat al-Sunan wa al-Āthār (1:23); Ibn Hajar in al-Dirāya (1:68) said: 'Al-Bayhaqi narrated it with a sound chain.' Al-Si'āya (1:546). Al-Mā'ida verse 6.
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding the number of prayers that can be performed with a single tayammum. The matn (base text) states the Hanafi position: one may pray any number of fard and nafl prayers. The sharh (commentary) notes that this is contrary to al-Shafi'i, who requires a separate tayammum for each fard prayer, though he permits multiple nafl prayers. The hashiya (super-commentary) then provides the Hanafi response, first by drawing an analogy to the qibla: when the qibla is ambiguous, one prays according to his best judgment, and if he later discovers error, his prayer is still valid because the obligation was to face his direction of ijtihād. In tayammum, however, the ruling is based on actual ability or inability to find water; when the reality contradicts the assumption, the ruling changes. The Hanafis argue that tayammum is a substitute (khalaf) for wudu, and like wudu, it remains valid until nullified. The Shafi'i proof from weak hadith is rejected. The passage also includes a dialogue from Imam Muhammad's 'al-Hujaj' where he refutes the Medinan position that one must seek water for each prayer, showing that seeking water (as opposed to actual loss of water) does not nullify tayammum. The Quranic verse (5:6) only mentions 'finding no water' as the condition. Thus the Hanafi position is that a single tayammum suffices for any number of prayers.

Key Terms
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution with clean earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or cannot be used.
فرض (fard): A prayer that is obligatory by definitive evidence; the five daily prayers.
نفل (nafl): Voluntary, supererogatory prayers beyond the obligatory ones.
خلافاً للشافعي (khilāfan lil-Shāfi'ī): Contrary to the position of Imam al-Shafi'i, the founder of the Shafi'i school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Hanafi school's ruling on praying multiple prayers with one tayammum?
A) Only one fard prayer is allowed.
B) Any number of fard and nafl prayers.
C) Only nafl prayers, not fard.
D) Only one prayer in total.

Key Takeaway
A single tayammum suffices for any number of prayers, as it is a full substitute for wudu and remains valid until nullified.

Nullifiers of Tayammum: Qiyas and the Refinement of 'Ability'
Ruling on nullifiers of tayammum with proof and refinement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two nullifiers of tayammum, explain the qiyas basis for transferring wudu nullifiers, and distinguish lawful ability from mere sight of water.

Core Idea
Tayammum is nullified by wudu nullifiers and lawful water ability; sight alone is insufficient.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling on what breaks tayammum. The matn states two nullifiers, and the commentary refines the concept of 'ability' to mean lawful and sufficient water. We will explore the qiyas reasoning and the intra-Hanafi preference for 'qudra' over 'ru’ya'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two nullifiers
The matn lists two nullifiers: (1) anything that nullifies wudu, and (2) ability to obtain sufficient water for purification. Note that these are distinct categories: events and water availability.
The second includes both physical and legal ability.
2
Understand the qiyas argument
Tayammum is a substitute (khalaf) for wudu. The principle 'al-asl aqwa min al-khalaf' means what nullifies the stronger (wudu) also nullifies the weaker (tayammum) a fortiori.
This is a jaliyyah qiyas; the illa is substitution.
3
Analyze the second nullifier: ability vs. sight
The author prefers 'ability' (qudra) over 'sight of water' (ru’yat al-mā’) because ability covers all excuses (illness, cold) that, when removed, nullify tayammum. Sight is not the operative factor.
This is a critical refinement from al-Hidayah's wording.
4
Clarify legal ability
Legal ability (qudra shar‘iyya) means water that one may lawfully use. Finding usurped or deposited water does not count, because it is not permissible to use.
Physical ability alone is insufficient.
5
Apply the 'sufficient' condition
Water must be sufficient for the required purification. If one finds water but uses it extravagantly (e.g., washing twice when once suffices) and water runs out, tayammum may still be nullified on the preferred view because the complete purification was possible.
The example of a dry patch (lum‘a) shows that sufficiency is judged by the minimum needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وينقضُهُ : ناقض الوضوء، وقدرته على ماء كاف لطهره. (وينقضه : ناقض الوضوء ، وقدرته على ماء كاف لطهره) حتى إذا قدر على الماء ولم يتوضأ، ثم عدم أعاد التيمم. وإنما قال : كافٍ لطهره، حتى إذا اغتسل الجنب ولم يصل الماء إلى لُمْعَةِ ظهره، وفنى الماء وأحدث حدثاً يوجب الوضوء، فتيمم لهما : أرأيتم لو كان في موضع لا يطمع في الماء، وابتغى أينقض الابتغاء تيممه، إنما ينتقض التيمم بحدث يحدثه الرجل ، أو يجد الماء. انتهى. قوله : وينقضه ؛ إسناد النقض إلى القدرة مجازي ؛ لأنّ الناقض حقيقة هو الحدث السابق ، وزوال المبيح للتيمّم شرط لظهور عمله، وإلى ناقض الوضوء حقيقي. قوله : ناقض الوضوء ؛ لأنه خلف عن الوضوء، فيأخذ حكمه، وأيضاً الأصل أقوى من الخلف، فما كان ناقضاً للأقوى كان ناقضاً للخلف، إلا ضعف بالطريق الأولى. قوله : وقدرته ؛ هذا أولى من قول صاحب الهداية: «ورؤية الماء»؛ فإنّه لا يصدق إلا في التيمم ؛ لعدم الماء، مع أنّ كلّ عذر يباح به التيمم ينتقض بزواله، فإنّ المريض إذا تيمم للمرض ثم صح انتقض تيممه ، وكذا إذا تيمم للبردِ ثم زال البرد. والمراد بالقدرة القدرة الشرعيّة، فيخرج وجدان ماء الغصب والوديعة ؛ فإنّه لا يباح له استعماله، فلا ينتقض به التيمم. قوله : كاف؛ في إطلاقه إشارة إلى اعتبار الأدنى، فلو وجد ماء فغسل به كل عضو مرَّتين أو ثلاثاً فنقص عن إحدى رجليه مثلاً بطل تيممه على المختار؛ لأنه لو اقتصر على المرَّةِ الواحدة كفاه. كذا في خلاصة الفتاوى. قوله : لمعة...الخ ؛ بضم اللام القطعة اللامعة اليابسة في أي موضع كان ، فالتقييد بالظهر جار مجرى العادة، فإنّه كثيراً ما يبقى موضع يابس في جانب الخلف. (من الحجة على أهل المدينة (١ : ٤٨ - ٤٩). انتهى من الهداية (١) : ١٣٤). ينظر: البحر الرائق (۱) : (١٦٠) ، و رد المحتار (۱ : ۱۷۰).
And it is nullified by: the nullifier of wudu, and his ability to obtain water sufficient for his purification. (And it is nullified by: the nullifier of wudu, and his ability to obtain water sufficient for his purification) So that if he is able to obtain water but does not perform wudu, then loses the water, he repeats tayammum. And he only said: sufficient for his purification, such that if a junub bathes and water does not reach a dry patch on his back, and the water runs out, and he commits an event that requires wudu, then he performs tayammum for both. Do you not see that if he were in a place where he does not hope for water, and he seeks it, does seeking nullify his tayammum? Indeed, tayammum is only nullified by an event that the person commits, or by finding water. End. His saying: 'and it is nullified by' – attribution of nullification to ability is metaphorical, because the actual nullifier is the earlier event, and the expiration of the permission for tayammum is a condition for the effect of its operation; but attribution to the nullifier of wudu is real. His saying: 'nullifier of wudu' – because tayammum is a substitute for wudu, so it takes its ruling; also the original is stronger than the substitute, so what is a nullifier of the stronger is a nullifier of the substitute, a fortiori. His saying: 'and his ability' – this is preferable to the statement of the author of al-Hidayah: 'and the sight of water', because it is not realized except in tayammum due to lack of water; moreover, every excuse that permits tayammum is nullified by its removal. For example, if a sick person performs tayammum due to illness and then recovers, his tayammum is nullified; likewise if he performs tayammum due to cold and then the cold ceases. What is meant by ability is legal ability, so finding usurped water or a deposit is excluded, because it is not permissible for him to use it, so tayammum is not nullified by it. His saying: 'sufficient' – in its absolute form is an indication of considering the minimum. So if he finds water and washes each limb twice or thrice, and water falls short on one of his feet, for example, his tayammum is invalidated according to the preferred view, because if he had limited himself to one wash, it would have sufficed him. Thus in Khulāṣat al-Fatāwā. His saying: 'lumpat...' etc. – with damm on the lam, it means a shiny dry patch anywhere on the body. The restriction to the back is conventional, because often a dry spot remains on the side of the back. (From al-Ḥujja ʿalā Ahl al-Madīna 1:48-49. End from al-Hidāya 1:134. Refer to al-Baḥr al-Rāʾiq 1:160 and Radd al-Muḥtār 1:170.
Source pages p. 444

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on what nullifies tayammum. The matn states two nullifiers: (1) anything that breaks wudu, and (2) the ability to obtain water sufficient for purification. The sharh explains that if one acquires water but does not use it and then loses the water, he must repeat tayammum. The hashiya refines the wording: 'ability' (قدرته) is preferred over 'seeing water' (رؤية الماء) as found in al-Hidayah, because the ability is the key factor. The nullification is metaphorical regarding ability; the real nullifier is the event (like passing wind) or the acquisition of water. The principle is that tayammum is a substitute for wudu, so the original's nullifier also nullifies the substitute, and even more strongly. The hashiya also clarifies that legal ability means lawful ability; finding water that one cannot use legally (e.g., usurped or deposited water) does not nullify tayammum. The term 'sufficient' (كاف) indicates that only sufficient water counts; if one finds water but it is insufficient due to extravagance (e.g., washing twice when once suffices), he may still be responsible. The example of a dry patch (لمعة) is given to illustrate that sufficient water means enough to wash all required parts. The passage also includes a quote from Imam Muhammad's argument with the people of Medina, reiterating that seeking water does not nullify tayammum; only actually finding it does.

Key Terms
ناقض (nāqiḍ): Something that nullifies ritual purity (wudu or tayammum).
قدرة (qudra): Legal ability to obtain and use water lawfully; ability in a shar'i sense.
كاف (kāf): Sufficient quantity of water to perform purification (wudu or ghusl) properly.
لمعة (lum'a): A dry patch on the body that missed water during ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Passing wind
B) Finding water that one can lawfully use
C) Seeing water from a distance
D) Recovering from illness that was the excuse for tayammum

Key Takeaway
Tayammum is nullified by wudu nullifiers and by lawful ability to obtain sufficient water; mere sight or unlawful access have no effect.

Effect of Finding Water on Tayammum: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Repeating Tayammum for Minor Impurity
Ruling on tayammum for both impurities with intra-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differ on whether one must repeat tayammum for the minor impurity after using found water for janabah, and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
When water sufficient for each impurity individually but not both, using it for janabah triggers an intra-Hanafi dispute on tayammum for the minor impurity.

This passage from the commentary 'Umdat al-Ri'aya on Al-Wiqayah explores a nuanced scenario: after performing tayammum for both janabah and wudu, a person finds water sufficient for washing each impurity individually but not both. Since janabah is more severe, he uses the water to wash it. The question then arises: is his tayammum for the minor impurity still valid, or must he repeat it? The Hanafi masters Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani offer two views, and the commentator clarifies the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Water found is sufficient for washing janabah or wudu individually, but not both. The person uses the water for janabah because it is more severe.
This is the fifth scenario described in the text.
2
State the point of dispute
After washing janabah, is the tayammum for the minor impurity (hadath asghar) still valid, or must it be repeated?
3
Examine Abu Yusuf's reasoning
Abu Yusuf holds no repeat is needed because the water was obligated (wajib al-sarf) to be used for janabah. Thus, in a legal sense, the person never had access to sufficient water for wudu, so the tayammum for wudu remains valid.
Key principle: ability to access water is negated if the water must be used for a more important purpose.
4
Examine Muhammad al-Shaybani's reasoning
Muhammad holds that at the moment of finding, the person had physical access to water sufficient for wudu, so his tayammum for wudu was invalidated. After using the water for janabah, he must repeat tayammum for wudu.
Key principle: actual ability (even if temporary) invalidates tayammum.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Imam al-Atabi in Sharh al-Ziyadat declares Muhammad's view as the most correct (al-asahh). Thus, the relied-upon position is that he must repeat tayammum for the minor impurity.
The tarjih is based on the strength of Muhammad's dalil regarding actual ability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

للحدث الأصغر؟ فيه روايتان : إحداهما : عدم الإعادة، وهو قول أبي يوسف الله عليه ، بناءً على عدم قدرته على الماء الكافي لرفع الحدث، فلم يبطل تيمّمه في حقه، فلا حاجة إلى إعادته ؛ وذلك لأن القدرة على الماء الكافي إنّما تعتبر إذا لم يكن واجب الصرف إلى جهة أهم، كما سيأتي من الشارح تصريحه. وهذا الماء الذي وجده وإن كان كافياً لكلِّ منهما على حدة لكن صرفه إلى غسل اللمعة كان واجباً ، فلم يكن قادراً على الكافي لرفع الحدث بالمعنى المذكور. وآخراهما : الإعادة، وهو قول محمد الله ، بناءً على تحقق القدرة على الماء الكافي لطهره، وهذا هو الأصح ، صرح به العتابي له في «شرح الزيادات».  قوله : وإن تيمم أوّلاً ؛ أي للحدث الأصغر ظناً منه أنه قدر على ماءٍ كافٍ للوضوء فبطل تيممه.  قوله : روايتان أيضاً ؛ فعند أبي يوسف الله لا يعيد، بناءً على أن صرفه إلى اللمعة واجب، فهو معدوم في حق الحدث من الابتداء، فلا يبطل تيممه في حقه، فتيممه ثانياً عبث. وعند محمد ه يعيد ؛ لكونه قادراً على الكافي للوضوء، فما دام يبقى الماء لا يفيد تيممه، فإذا صرفه إلى اللمعة نظراً إلى أنه أهم وجبت عليه إعادة التيمم ؛ لعجزه حينئذ عن الماء الكافي.  قوله : أما إذا تيمم....الخ ؛ يعني تيمم للجنابة أولاً، بناء على فناء الماء وبقاء
Then if he finds water sufficient for both, his tayammum is invalidated in respect of each one. If it is not sufficient for either, both remain valid. If it is sufficient for one specifically, he washes that one, and tayammum remains for the other. If it is sufficient for each individually, he washes the major impurity (janabah), because janabah is more severe. If he washes the janabah, should he repeat tayammum for the minor impurity? There are two narrations. He said: His tayammum is invalidated because he has access to water sufficient for the purification for which he performed tayammum as a substitute. And ability to access sufficient water nullifies tayammum. He said: 'If it is not sufficient' – this is one form of the issue, that the water he found is not sufficient for either, such that it is little and cannot allow wudu or washing of the janabah. Its ruling is that his previous tayammum remains valid for both impurities due to his inability to access sufficient water. He said: 'If it is sufficient' – this is a third form comprising two scenarios: First, the water he found is sufficient for washing the janabah but not for wudu. Its ruling: his tayammum for the major impurity is invalidated because he can access sufficient water for the major purification, but his tayammum for the minor impurity is not invalidated due to inability to access water sufficient for wudu. Second, he finds water sufficient for wudu but not for washing the janabah – for water is little and the janabah extensive. Its ruling: his tayammum for wudu is invalidated, and his tayammum for ghusl remains. He said: 'He washes that one' – meaning he washes with the sufficient water what is needed from the janabah and the wudu limbs. He said: 'If it is sufficient for each individually' – this is a fifth scenario: the water he has access to is sufficient for each individually, not jointly, such that if he washes the janabah with it he can, but no water remains after that to perform wudu; if he washes the wudu limbs with it he can, but no water remains after that to wash the janabah. The ruling: he must wash the janabah with it because janabah is more severe than the minor impurity, so the focus on removing it is stronger. Then his janabah is removed and his tayammum for it is invalidated. He said: 'If he then washes' etc. – meaning in this scenario, if he washes the janabah with that water giving priority to the more important, should he repeat tayammum for the minor impurity? There are two narrations: One: not repeating – the statement of Abu Yusuf, based on his inability to access water sufficient for removing the minor impurity, so his tayammum for it did not become invalid, and there is no need to repeat it. This is because ability to access sufficient water is only considered if it is not obligated to be directed to a more important matter. This water he found, although sufficient for each individually, its use for washing the janabah was obligatory, so he was not able to access sufficient water for removing the minor impurity in the mentioned sense. The second: repeating – the statement of Muhammad, based on the realization of ability to access sufficient water for his purification, and this is the most correct, as stated by al-Atabi in his 'Sharh al-Ziyadat'. He said: 'If he first performed tayammum' – meaning for the minor impurity, thinking he had access to water sufficient for wudu, so his tayammum became invalid. He said: 'Two narrations as well' – according to Abu Yusuf, he does not repeat, based on the fact that directing it to the janabah was obligatory, so it is non-existent from the beginning in respect of the minor impurity, so his tayammum for it is not invalidated, and repeating his tayammum would be futile. According to Muhammad, he repeats because he had access to water sufficient for wudu, so as long as water remains, his tayammum is of no use; when he directs it to the janabah considering it more important, repeating tayammum becomes obligatory due to his subsequent inability to access sufficient water. He said: 'As for if he performed tayammum...' etc. – meaning he first performed tayammum for janabah based on the water being exhausted and (water) remaining...
Source pages p. 445

Commentary
This passage from the commentary expands on rulings concerning the effect of finding water after performing tayammum for both major and minor impurities. The author, al-Margainani, presents five scenarios. In the first, water sufficient for both invalidates tayammum for both. In the second, water insufficient for either leaves both tayammum valid. In the third, water sufficient for one specific impurity: he washes that impurity and retains tayammum for the other. The fourth scenario subdivides: if water is sufficient only for washing janabah, tayammum for janabah is invalidated but tayammum for wudu remains; if sufficient only for wudu, tayammum for wudu is invalidated and for janabah remains. The fifth scenario: water sufficient for each individually but not both. Since janabah is more severe, he must use the water to wash janabah. After washing janabah, a dispute arises between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani on whether he must repeat tayammum for the minor impurity. Abu Yusuf says no, because the water was obligated to be used for janabah, so he was not actually able to use it for wudu; Muhammad says yes, he had access to sufficient water for wudu at the outset, so tayammum for wudu was invalidated, and after using it for janabah he must repeat tayammum. The relied-upon position (al-mu'tamad) is Muhammad's view, as stated by al-Atabi. The passage also mentions a variation where he first performs tayammum thinking water is available, then finds it insufficient, with the same two narrations applying.

Key Terms
اللمعة (al-lum'ah): The state of major ritual impurity (janabah) requiring a full body wash (ghusl). In this text, 'غسل اللمعة' means washing off janabah.
تيمم (tayammum): Dry purification with clean earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
حدث أكبر (hadath akbar): Major ritual impurity necessitating ghusl, such as janabah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where a person finds water sufficient for washing janabah and wudu individually but not both, and uses the water for janabah, what is the mufta bihi ruling regarding his tayammum for wudu?
A) His tayammum for wudu remains valid (Abu Yusuf).
B) His tayammum for wudu is invalid and he must repeat it (Muhammad).
C) Both tayammums become invalid.
D) Only the tayammum for janabah is invalid, and he must repeat both.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, when water sufficient for each impurity individually is found, using it for the more severe impurity (janabah) does not preserve the tayammum for the minor impurity due to the prior ability to access water for it, necessitating a repeat tayammum.

Tayammum Repetition After Washing Lam'a: Abu Yusuf vs Muhammad
Intra-Hanafi ruling dispute on tayammum repetition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the reasoning of Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad on whether tayammum must be repeated after washing a lam'a, and state the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Tayammum validity depends on actual water access for the intended purification, not mere water existence.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute. A person performs tayammum for minor impurity, then finds sufficient water to wash both the minor impurity and a spot of janabah (lam'a). After washing the lam'a, does the tayammum stand or must it be repeated? The answer depends on how 'ability to use water' is defined when multiple obligations compete for the same water.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario and Core Question
A person has minor hadath (e.g., invalidated wudu) and a spot of janabah on his body. He performs tayammum for the minor hadath, then finds water sufficient to wash both the lam'a and for a full wudu. He washes the lam'a first. Does his original tayammum remain valid, or must he repeat it?
2
State Abu Yusuf's Position and Reasoning
Abu Yusuf holds that he does NOT repeat tayammum. Reasoning: The water was obligatory to use for the lam'a (janabah is more severe), so it was effectively unavailable for wudu from the beginning. Thus, at the time of tayammum, he lacked water for wudu, so tayammum was valid and remains so.
Key principle: obligation to divert water to a more important purpose (lam'a) negates ability to use it for wudu.
3
State Imam Muhammad's Position and Reasoning
Imam Muhammad holds that he MUST repeat tayammum. Reasoning: At the moment he found the water, he had sufficient water for wudu, which invalidated his tayammum. His decision to wash the lam'a first is his own choice; the initial ability to use water for wudu already voided the tayammum. After using the water for lam'a, he becomes unable, so he must perform a new tayammum.
Key principle: initial ability to obtain water for wudu invalidates tayammum, regardless of later diversion.
4
Determine the Mufta Bihi and Its Authority
The commentator states that Imam Muhammad's view is the most correct (asahh), as confirmed by al-Atabi in Sharh al-Ziyadat. Thus the operative fatwa is that tayammum must be repeated.
Authority: Zahir al-Riwayah; tarjih by al-Atabi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن تيمم أولاً ثم غسلَ اللَّمْعَة ففي إعادة التيم روايتان أيضاً. إحداهما: عدم الإعادة، وهو قول أبي يوسف الله عليه، بناءً على عدم قدرته على الماء الكافي لرفع الحدث، فلم يبطل تيمّمه في حقه، فلا حاجة إلى إعادته؛ وذلك لأن القدرة على الماء الكافي إنّما تعتبر إذا لم يكن واجب الصرف إلى جهة أهم، كما سيأتي من الشارح تصريحه. وهذا الماء الذي وجده وإن كان كافياً لكلِّ منهما على حدة لكن صرفه إلى غسل اللمعة كان واجباً، فلم يكن قادراً على الكافي لرفع الحدث بالمعنى المذكور. وآخرهما: الإعادة، وهو قول محمد الله، بناءً على تحقق القدرة على الماء الكافي لطهره، وهذا هو الأصح، صرح به العتابي له في «شرح الزيادات». 11 قوله: وإن تيمم أوّلاً؛ أي للحدث الأصغر ظناً منه أنه قدر على ماءٍ كافٍ للوضوء فبطل تيممه. قوله: روايتان أيضاً؛ فعند أبي يوسف الله لا يعيد، بناءً على أن صرفه إلى اللمعة واجب، فهو معدوم في حق الحدث من الابتداء، فلا يبطل تيممه في حقه، فتيممه ثانياً عبث. وعند محمد ه يعيد؛ لكونه قادراً على الكافي للوضوء، فما دام يبقى الماء لا يفيد تيممه، فإذا صرفه إلى اللمعة نظراً إلى أنه أهم وجبت عليه إعادة التيمم؛ لعجزه حينئذ عن الماء الكافي.
If he performs tayammum first, then washes the spot (of janabah), then concerning repetition of tayammum there are two narrations as well. One: not repeating, which is the view of Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him), based on his inability to obtain sufficient water for removing the impurity, so his tayammum is not invalidated in his regard, so there is no need to repeat it; because ability to obtain sufficient water is only considered when it is not obligatory to divert it to a more important purpose, as the commentator will explicitly state. This water he found, although sufficient for each individually, diverting it to washing the spot was obligatory, so he was not able to obtain sufficient water for removing the impurity in the aforementioned sense. The other: repeating, which is the view of Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him), based on his ability to obtain sufficient water for his purification, and this is the most correct, as stated by al-Atābi in his commentary on al-Ziyādāt. He said: 'And if he performs tayammum first,' meaning for the minor impurity, thinking that he has sufficient water for ablution, so his tayammum is invalidated. Then he said: 'Two narrations as well'; according to Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) he does not repeat, based on the fact that diverting the water to the spot is obligatory, so it is considered nonexistent with respect to the impurity from the beginning, so his tayammum is not invalidated in his regard, and his second tayammum is futile. According to Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) he repeats, because he is able to obtain sufficient water for ablution, and as long as water remains, his tayammum is ineffective, so when he diverts it to the spot considering it more important, he is obliged to repeat tayammum due to his inability to obtain sufficient water then.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a ruling from al-Wiqayah. It discusses a scenario: A person does tayammum for minor impurity (hadath asghar) thinking he has enough water for wudu, but then finds water sufficient for both wudu and washing a spot of janabah (lam'a) on his body. He washes the lam'a first. Now, does his original tayammum remain valid? There are two narrations (riwayatan) from the Hanafi school. Imam Abu Yusuf says he does not need to repeat tayammum because the water was obligatory to use for the lam'a (since janabah is more severe), so in effect he did not have water sufficient for wudu. His tayammum remains. Imam Muhammad says he must repeat tayammum because he had sufficient water for wudu when he found it; diverting it to lam'a was his choice, but later he becomes unable, so tayammum is needed. The commentator states that Muhammad's view is the most correct (asahh), as confirmed by al-Atabi in Sharh al-Ziyadat. The passage then further explains the reasoning in detail.

Key Terms
اللمعة (al-lam'a): A spot of janabah (major impurity) on the body that requires washing.
الحدث (al-hadath): State of ritual impurity; here specifically minor impurity (hadath asghar) that requires wudu.
التيمم (al-tayammum): Dry ablution with earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, why must tayammum be repeated in the scenario?
A) Because he had sufficient water for wudu at the time of finding it
B) Because washing the lam'a is obligatory
C) Because water is always preferred over tayammum
D) Because Abu Yusuf also agreed

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, tayammum is invalidated upon finding sufficient water for wudu, even if that water is later used for an obligatory purpose like washing janabah; the mufta bihi requires repeating tayammum.

Using Water for Hadath Invalidates Tayammum for Lam'a
Ruling on effect of using water for hadath on tayammum for lam'a

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a person who performed tayammum for both hadath and janaba uses available water for hadath, and explain the agreement of the two narrations (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad).

Core Idea
Using water for one impurity invalidates tayammum for the other if water was sufficient for both.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario in taharah: a person in a state of both major (janaba) and minor (hadath) impurity performs a single tayammum covering both. Later, he finds water but only enough for one purification. If he chooses to use the water for wudu (hadath), what happens to the tayammum for janaba? The matn delivers a clear ruling agreed upon by the two primary students of Abu Hanifa—Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A person had combined tayammum for both hadath and janaba, then finds water sufficient for only one purification.
This assumes water is available but not enough for both.
2
Apply the ruling
If he uses the water for hadath (wudu), his tayammum for the lam'a (janaba) is invalidated. The tayammum for hadath also becomes void because water was used for it, but the focus is on the lam'a.
The ruling is about the remaining impurity's tayammum.
3
Note the agreement
This ruling is agreed upon by both Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two narrations), unlike the previous scenario where they differed on using water for lam'a.
The agreement signals a clear operative position in the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن صرف إلى الحدثِ انتقض تيمُّمُهُ في حق اللمْعَةِ باتفاق الروايتين.
And if he diverts (the water) to the minor impurity, his tayammum is invalidated regarding the spot of janabah by agreement of the two narrations.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This is a clear ruling from the matn. It states that if a person who has done tayammum for both impurities (hadath and janabah) finds water sufficient for only one, and he uses it for the minor impurity (hadath) rather than the lam'a, then his tayammum is invalidated with respect to the lam'a. This is agreed upon by both Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, unlike the previous scenario where they differed. The reasoning is that by using water for hadath, he has shown that the water was available for that purpose, so the tayammum for the lam'a is no longer valid because he could have used the water for it but chose otherwise.

Key Terms
الحدث (al-hadath): Minor impurity requiring wudu.
اللمعة (al-lam'a): Spot of janabah (major impurity).
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution with earth as substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable.
الروايتين (al-riwayatayn): The two narrations: the transmissions from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It remains valid
B) It is invalidated by agreement
C) It is invalidated according to Abu Yusuf only
D) It is invalidated according to Muhammad only

Key Takeaway
Using water for hadath invalidates the combined tayammum for janaba, agreed by the two narrations, because water availability for one proves it was available for the other.

Tayammum for Janabah and Hadath: Rulings When Water is Found
Ruling on tayammum scenarios after finding water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings on tayammum for janabah and hadath when water of limited quantity is found, distinguishing between sufficiency for lam'a and wudu.

Core Idea
When water suffices for only one impurity, tayammum for the other remains valid.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah details the intricate scenarios following tayammum for major impurity (janabah) and then minor impurity (hadath). Understanding which tayammum is invalidated when water of varying sufficiency is found is essential for correctly applying the rules of purification. We will walk through each case methodically.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial states
Determine that the person performed tayammum for janabah, then had a minor hadath (and either did or did not perform tayammum for it), then found water.
The water quantity may be limited.
2
Classify water sufficiency
Assess whether the water found is sufficient for: both lam'a (spot of janabah) and wudu, only lam'a, only wudu, each individually, or neither.
Sufficiency means enough water to fulfill the obligation.
3
Apply the ruling for each case
Based on the classification, determine which tayammum(s) are invalidated and what actions are required: if sufficient for both, both invalid; if for neither, both valid; if for only one, that one's tayammum invalid and the other remains; if for each individually, priority to lam'a.
If water used for wudu instead of lam'a, janabah tayammum must be repeated.
4
Handle the dispute on order
In the case where one starts with tayammum for hadath then diverts water to lam'a, note the disagreement between al-Ziyadat (repeat tayammum) and al-Asl (no repeat).
The text does not resolve which is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما إذا تيمم للجنابة، ثم أحدث فتيم للحدث، ثم وجد الماء، فكذا في الوجوه المذكورة. وإن تيمم للجنابة ثم أحدث ولم يتيمم للحدث فوجد الماء، فإن كفى اللمعة والوضوء فظاهر. وإن لم يكف لأحدهما لا ينتقض تيممه، فيستعمل الماء في اللُّمْعة تقليلاً للجنابة، ويتيمم للحدث. وإن كفى اللُّمْعَةَ لا الوضوءَ انتقض تيممه، ويغسلُ اللمعة ويتيمم للحدث. وإن كفى للوضوء لا للمُعَةِ فتيممه باق وعليه الوضوء. وإن كفى لكلِّ واحدٍ منهما منفرداً يصرفه إلى اللمعة، ويتمم للحدث، فإن توضأ به جاز، ويعيدُ التّيمُّمَ للجنابة، ولو لم يتوضأ به، ولكن بدأ بالتّيمم للحدثِ ثمّ صرفَهُ إلى اللمعة، هل يعيد التيمم أم لا؟ ففي رواية «الزيادات» (۱) : يعيد. وفي رواية «الأصل» (۲) : لا. ثم قال: اللمعة، ثم أحدث حدثاً يوجب الوضوء فتيمم له ثانياً، ثم وجد الماء، فالحكم فيه كالحكم في الوجه الأول، وهو أنه إذا وجد من الماء ما يكفي للحدث والجنابة كليهما بطل تيممه في حق كل منهما، وإن لم يكف لأحدهما بقي في حقهما، وإن كفى لأحدهما بعينه بطل تيمّمه في حقه خاصة، وإن كفى لكل منهما منفرداً غسل اللمعة.
But if he performs tayammum for janabah, then has a minor impurity and performs tayammum for it, then finds water, the same applies to the aforementioned cases. If he performs tayammum for janabah, then has a minor impurity and does not perform tayammum for it, then finds water: if it suffices for both the lam'a and wudu, then it is apparent (that his tayammum is invalidated). If it does not suffice for either, his tayammum is not invalidated; he uses the water for the lam'a to reduce janabah, and performs tayammum for the minor impurity. If it suffices for the lam'a but not for wudu, his tayammum is invalidated, and he washes the lam'a and performs tayammum for the minor impurity. If it suffices for wudu but not for the lam'a, his tayammum remains valid and he must perform wudu. If it suffices for each individually, he diverts it to the lam'a, and completes tayammum for the minor impurity; if he performs wudu with it, it is permissible, and he repeats tayammum for janabah. And if he does not perform wudu with it, but begins with tayammum for the minor impurity then diverts it to the lam'a, does he repeat tayammum or not? In the narration of al-Ziyādāt: he repeats. In the narration of al-Asl: no. Then he said: the lam'a, then he has a minor impurity requiring wudu and performs tayammum for it a second time, then finds water: the ruling is the same as the first case, namely: if he finds water sufficient for both the minor impurity and janabah, his tayammum is invalidated with respect to both; if it does not suffice for either, it remains valid for both; if it suffices for one specifically, his tayammum is invalidated with respect to that one only; if it suffices for each individually, he washes the lam'a.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage details several scenarios of tayammum for janabah followed by minor impurity. The commentator first relates to the previous discussion about tayammum for both impurities. He then enumerates cases: (1) If water is sufficient for both lam'a and wudu, tayammum is invalidated. (2) If insufficient for either, tayammum remains. (3) If sufficient for lam'a only, tayammum for janabah is invalidated, but tayammum for hadath remains. (4) If sufficient for wudu only, tayammum for janabah remains, but wudu is needed. (5) If sufficient for each only individually, he must use water for lam'a (since janabah is more important), then perform tayammum for hadath. If he instead uses water for wudu, that is valid but he must repeat tayammum for janabah. There is a dispute between the two narrations (al-Ziyadat and al-Asl) on whether he must repeat tayammum if he first does tayammum for hadath then uses water for lam'a. The final summary reiterates the general principles.

Key Terms
الجنابة (al-janabah): Major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.
الحدث (al-hadath): Minor impurity requiring wudu.
اللمعة (al-lam'a): Spot of janabah on the body.
التيمم (al-tayammum): Dry ablution as substitute for wudu or ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a person performs tayammum for janabah, then has minor hadath (without performing tayammum for it), and finds water sufficient for lam'a only, what is the ruling?
A) His tayammum for janabah is invalidated and he must wash the lam'a and perform tayammum for hadath
B) His tayammum for janabah remains valid and he must perform tayammum for hadath
C) Both tayammums are invalidated
D) He must use the water for wudu and repeat tayammum for janabah

Key Takeaway
When water is found after tayammum, its sufficiency for specific impurities determines which tayammum remains valid; priority is given to removing janabah over hadath.

Tayammum Invalidation and the Riwayat Dispute on Water for Lum'a
Expansion on tayammum invalidation with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on tayammum invalidation when water is found after tayammum for janaba and hadath, and identify the dispute between Riwayat al-Asl and al-Ziyadat regarding the sequence of using water for lum'a.

Core Idea
When water is found after tayammum, invalidation depends on sufficiency for each impurity; a Hanafi dispute exists on whether prior tayammum for hadath affects the janaba tayammum.

This lesson examines a nuanced scenario in the Hanafi school: a person performs tayammum for janaba (major impurity), then experiences hadath (minor impurity) without renewing tayammum, and later finds water. The ruling on whether the tayammum remains valid depends on how much water is available and how it is used. The passage also presents a dispute within the school regarding the sequence of using limited water for washing a limb (lum'a) versus performing wudu, with two transmitted narrations from Imam Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base scenario
Start with the core case: a person performed tayammum for janaba, then had hadath (but did not perform tayammum for it), and then found water. The ruling depends on the sufficiency of that water.
This is the scenario from the first line of the passage.
2
Analyze the water sufficiency scenarios
The text lists four possibilities: water suffices for both lum'a and wudu (clear invalidation), for neither (tayammum remains), for lum'a only (tayammum invalidated for janaba), for wudu only (tayammum valid for janaba, wudu required).
Focus on the 'apparent' ruling of the first scenario.
3
Examine the disputed scenario
The key dispute arises when water suffices for each impurity individually (but not both together). The text states the default: water should be used for lum'a, then tayammum for hadath. But if someone first performs tayammum for hadath (thinking water unavailable for it) then uses water for lum'a, does the janaba tayammum require repetition?
This is the expansion probe.
4
Contrast the two narrations
Riwayat al-Ziyadat holds that the janaba tayammum must be repeated because the water was effectively available for janaba after the tayammum for hadath. Riwayat al-Asl holds it is not repeated because the water was used for lum'a after the hadath tayammum was already done.
Both narrations are from Imam Muhammad; no tarjih is given here.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf is whether the person must perform a new tayammum for janaba or not. According to al-Ziyadat, he would need to; according to al-Asl, his original tayammum suffices.
This difference affects the validity of subsequent prayers if water is later found.

اللمعة، ثم أحدث حدثاً يوجب الوضوء فتيمم له ثانياً، ثم وجد الماء، فالحكم فيه كالحكم في الوجه الأول، وهو أنه إذا وجد من الماء ما يكفي للحدث والجنابة كليهما بطل تيممه في حق كل منهما، وإن لم يكف لأحدهما بقي في حقهما، وإن كفى لأحدهما بعينه بطل تيمّمه في حقه خاصة، وإن كفى لكل منهما منفرداً غسل اللمعة. For the hadath, then he found water, so it is similar in the mentioned aspects. If he performed tayammum for janaba then caused hadath and did not perform tayammum for the hadath, then found water: if it suffices for the lum'a and wudu, it is apparent. If it does not suffice for either, his tayammum is not invalidated; he uses the water for the lum'a to minimize the janaba, and performs tayammum for the hadath. If it suffices for the lum'a but not for wudu, his tayammum is invalidated, and he washes the lum'a and performs tayammum for the hadath. If it suffices for wudu but not for the lum'a, his tayammum remains valid and he must perform wudu. In the narration of al-Asl: no. : The lum'a, then he caused hadath requiring wudu and performed tayammum a second time, then found water. [2] His saying: 'he uses' is not obligatory but a priority, as the commentator indicated earlier in the beginning of the chapter. (3) His saying: 'his tayammum is invalidated' means regarding janaba, due to his ability to use water sufficient for washing his lum'a. [4] His saying: 'but he began with tayammum' thinking that he would divert the water to the lum'a, as if it were nonexistent for the hadath.

Commentary
This passage belongs to the commentary on the rulings of tayammum, specifically the case of a person who performed tayammum for janaba, then had a minor impurity, and then found water. The commentary presents several scenarios based on the sufficiency of water. It begins by stating the general principle: if water is sufficient for both washing the lum'a (to partially remove janaba) and wudu, the tayammum is invalidated entirely. If it suffices for neither, the tayammum remains valid. If it suffices for one specifically, then only the tayammum for that impurity is invalidated. The next scenario is when water suffices for each impurity individually but not both together. In that case, the water should be used for the lum'a first, then tayammum for hadath. There is a dispute regarding the sequence: if the person first performs tayammum for hadath (thinking the water is unavailable for hadath) and then uses water for the lum'a, does he need to repeat the tayammum for janaba? According to al-Ziyadat, yes; according to al-Asl, no. The commentary then summarizes the rule for a similar case. The hashiya (super-commentary) clarifies that the initial ruling is apparent, and the use of water for the lum'a is not obligatory but recommended. The invalidation is due to the ability to use water. The final note explains that the person's thinking affects the ruling.

Key Terms
اللمعة (al-lum'a): A small part of the body (e.g., a limb) that is washed to reduce the state of janaba partially.
الحدث (al-hadath): Minor impurity that necessitates wudu.
الجنابة (al-janaba): Major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.
التيمم (al-tayammum): Dry ablution with pure earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or cannot be used.
