Defining Qudra (Ability) for Water in Tayammum
Definition of qudra and its two types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi definition of qudra (ability) for water in tayammum, identify its condition, and distinguish between ibaha and tamlik.

Core Idea
Ability to use water is legal, not just physical: water needed for najasa is absent; ability exists via ownership or permission.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya defines the legal concept of qudra (ability) specifically for tayammum. It establishes that water must be available for purification without conflicting with more important Shari'ah purposes. The commentary unpacks two ways ability is recognized—ownership and permission—and illustrates with a scenario where a group is granted permission to use water.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary condition for qudra
The passage begins by stating that ability is only established if the water is not required for a more important purpose. Identify this condition and understand that if water is obligated for something else, it is considered non-existent for tayammum.
The key Arabic phrase: 'إنَّما تثبت القدرة إذا لم يكن مصروفاً إلى جهة أهم'.
2
Recognize the example of a more important purpose
The commentary explains that removing physical najasa (impurity) from the body or clothing that would prevent salah is a more important purpose. This diverts the water from use for purification, making tayammum permissible.
Najasa that is excused (ma'fu) does not require diversion.
3
Differentiate between the two types of qudra
Ability is established by two means: ibaha (permission to use without ownership) and tamlik (ownership). Understand the juristic difference: the owner has full disposal rights; the one with ibaha only has the right to use.
Ibahah is sufficient to invalidate tayammum; ownership is not required.
4
Apply the scenario to solidify understanding
The passage gives a case: an owner tells a group each may use water, but it suffices for one. Analyze why each person's tayammum is invalidated (ability established individually) and why the rest must repeat tayammum after one uses it (inability becomes apparent).
The ruling is based on the existence of ability, not actual usage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثمَّ إنَّما تثبت القدرة إذا لم يكن مصروفاً إلى جهة أهم، حتى إذا كان على بدنه أو ثوبه نجاسة يصرفُهُ إلى النَّجاسة، ثمَّ القدرة تثبت: بطريق الإباحة، وبطريق التمليك".
فإن قال صاحب الماءِ الجماعة من المتيممين : ليتوضأ بهذا الماء أيكم شاء ، والماء يكفي لكلّ واحدٍ منفرداً ، ينتقض تيمم كلُّ واحد، فإذا توضاً بهِ واحد يعيدُ الباقون تيممهم ؛ لثبوتِ القدرة لكلِّ واحدٍ على الانفراد.
[0]
[ 1 ] قوله : ثم...الخ ؛ يريد أنّ المراد بالقدرة على الماء الكافي لطهره القدرة المعتبرة شرعاً، وهي إنما تكون إذا لم يكن الماءُ واجب الصرفِ شرعاً إلى جهة أهم من طهره : كإزالة النجاسةِ الحقيقيَّة من بدنِهِ أو ثوبه المانعة من أداء الصلاة، فإن كان كذلك فوجوده بمنزلة عدمِهِ فيباح له التيمم. [٢]قوله : نجاسة ؛ أي بقدر ما يمنع عن الصلاة، فإن كانت بقدر ما عفا الشارع عنه على ما سيأتي تفصيلُهُ إن شاء الله تعالى لم يلزمه صرفه إليها. [٣] قوله : بطريق الإباحة وبطريق التمليك ؛ يعني أنّ القدرة على الماء لا تنحصر في ملكه بأن يدخل الماء في ملكه بقبول الهبة أو الصدقة أو بالشراء أو غيرها من أسباب التمليك، بل تعم القدرة على سبيل الإباحة أيضاً.
والفرق بينهما أن المملك له يدخلُ في ملكه ذلك الشيء، وتترتب عليه آثاره ، فيقدر على بيعه وهبته وسائر الانتقالاتِ وغير ذلك مما يجوز للإنسان أن يفعله في ملكه، وأما المباح له فلا يملك إلا الانتفاع بذلك الشيء الذي أبيح له، ولا يملك التصرف فيه ، كتصرف الرجل في ملكه.
[٤] قوله : منفرداً ؛ فإن كان الماء كثيراً كافياً لكلِّ واحدٍ واحد مجتمعاً ، فانتقاض تيممهم أظهر.
[0] قوله : لثبوت ؛ متعلق بقوله : «يعيد» أو بقوله : «ينتقض»؛ فإنّ ثبوت القدرةِ على الماء لكل واحد ، ولو على سبيل الإباحة علة لانتقاض التيمم، وهو علة لإعادته حين عدم الماء، يتوضؤ واحد منهم لظهور عجز الباقين.
Then, ability is only established if water is not required for a more important purpose, such that if there is najasa on his body or clothes, he diverts water to the najasa. Then ability is established in two ways: by permission (ibaha) and by ownership (tamlik). If the owner of water says to the group of those performing tayammum: 'Let any of you perform wudu with this water,' and the water suffices for each individually, the tayammum of each is invalidated. Then if one performs wudu with it, the rest repeat their tayammum because ability is established for each individually. [1] His saying: 'then...etc.'; he intends that the meaning of ability regarding water sufficient for his purification is the ability recognized by the Shari'ah, which is only when the water is not obligated by the Shari'ah to be diverted to a purpose more important than his purification, such as removing physical najasa from his body or clothing that prevents performing prayer. If it is so, its existence is like its non-existence, so tayammum is permissible for him. [2] His saying: 'najasa' means an amount that prevents prayer; if it is an amount that the Lawgiver has excused, as will be detailed later if Allah wills, he is not obliged to divert water to it. [3] His saying: 'by way of ibaha and by way of tamlik'; he means that ability regarding water is not limited to ownership by which water enters his ownership through accepting a gift, charity, purchase, or other means of ownership, but rather includes ability by way of ibaha as well. The difference between them is that the owner has that thing enter his ownership, and its effects follow, so he is able to sell it, gift it, and all other transfers and things that a person is allowed to do with his property. As for the one given permission, he only owns the usufruct of that thing which is permitted to him, and he does not own the right to dispose of it like a person's disposal in his property. [4] His saying: 'individually'; if the water is abundant sufficient for each one collectively, then the invalidation of their tayammum is more apparent. [0] His saying: 'due to the establishment'; it is related to his saying 'he repeats' or his saying 'it invalidates'; because the establishment of ability to water for each, even by way of ibaha, is the cause for the invalidation of tayammum, and it is the cause for its repetition when water is absent, one of them performing wudu because of the apparent inability of the rest.
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This passage defines the concept of 'qudra' (legal ability to use water) for tayammum purposes. It begins by stating that ability is only recognized if the water is not required by the Shari'ah for a more important purpose. The primary example is the removal of physical najasa (impurity) from the body or clothing that would prevent salah; in such a case, the water must be used for that, so it is considered absent for tayammum. Then, the passage explains that ability can be established in two ways: ibaha (permission to use without ownership) and tamlik (ownership). The commentary clarifies that ability is not limited to ownership; even if one is given permission to use water, that establishes ability. The difference is that an owner has full rights of disposal (sell, gift, etc.), while a person with ibaha only has the right to use. Finally, the passage presents a scenario: the owner tells a group of people who need wudu that any one of them may use the water, and the water suffices for each individually. In this case, each person's tayammum is invalidated because each has the ability (even though only one can actually use it). If one performs wudu, the others must repeat their tayammum because the ability was established. The commentary adds that the invalidation is due to the establishment of ability, and the repetition is due to the subsequent inability after one has used the water.

Key Terms
القدرة (al-qudra): Ability/access to water as recognized by the Shari'ah, established either by ownership or by permission.
الإباحة (al-ibaha): Permission to use water without owning it.
التمليك (al-tamlik): Ownership of water, including the right to sell, gift, or otherwise dispose of it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) He must use water for both najasa and tayammum.

Key Takeaway
Legal ability to use water for tayammum exists only when water is not required for a more important Shari'ah purpose, and it can be established by ownership or permission.

Establishment of Qudra over Water: Ibaha and Tamlik
Definition and examples of qudra for tayammum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define qudra (ability) over water for tayammum, distinguish between ibaha and tamlik, and apply the condition of water priority to determine the validity of tayammum.

Core Idea
Ability over water invalidates tayammum—whether by ownership or permissibility to use.

This lesson unpacks a key principle from the Hanafi school regarding tayammum: the legal ability (qudra) to use water is not limited to ownership. Even if you are merely permitted to use water (ibaha), your tayammum becomes invalid. However, this ability is only established if the water is not required for a more urgent purpose, such as removing impurity that prevents prayer. Through the example of a group granted permission to use a water source, we will see how the school applies this rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two ways ability is established
Locate in the passage how qudra is defined: it is established either through ownership (tamlik) or through permissibility (ibaha). Note that ownership gives full dispositive power, while ibaha only grants the right to use.
The passage explicitly states: 'ثمَّ القدرة تثبت: بطريق الإباحة، وبطريق التمليك.'
2
Understand the priority condition
The passage first mentions that ability is not established if the water must be used for a more important purpose, like removing najasah that prevents salah. In such a case, the water is considered as if absent, and tayammum remains valid.
Commentary [1] clarifies this: 'المراد بالقدرة على الماء الكافي لطهره القدرة المعتبرة شرعاً، وهي إنما تكون إذا لم يكن الماءُ واجب الصرفِ شرعاً إلى جهة أهم من طهره.'
3
Analyze the group example
Consider the scenario: an owner tells a group, 'Whoever wishes may do wudu with this water.' If the water suffices for each individually, everyone's tayammum is invalidated. If one uses it, the rest lose ability and must repeat tayammum.
The invalidation is due to established ability via ibaha. The phrase 'li-thubut' in the last line confirms this causality.
4
Distinguish ibaha and tamlik
The commentary [3] provides a clear distinction: tamlik grants full ownership rights (sale, gift, etc.), while ibaha only permits use without ownership. Both, however, establish qudra for the purpose of invalidating tayammum.
This is a key Hanafi position: ibaha suffices for qudra.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثمَّ إنَّما تثبت القدرة إذا لم يكن مصروفاً إلى جهة أهم، حتى إذا كان على بدنه أو ثوبه نجاسة يصرفُهُ إلى النَّجاسة، ثمَّ القدرة تثبت: بطريق الإباحة، وبطريق التمليك. فإن قال صاحب الماءِ الجماعة من المتيممين : ليتوضأ بهذا الماء أيكم شاء ، والماء يكفي لكلّ واحدٍ منفرداً ، ينتقض تيمم كلُّ واحد، فإذا توضاً بهِ واحد يعيدُ الباقون تيممهم ؛ لثبوتِ القدرة لكلِّ واحدٍ على الانفراد.
[ 1 ] قوله : ثم...الخ ؛ يريد أنّ المراد بالقدرة على الماء الكافي لطهره القدرة المعتبرة شرعاً، وهي إنما تكون إذا لم يكن الماءُ واجب الصرفِ شرعاً إلى جهة أهم من طهره : كإزالة النجاسةِ الحقيقيَّة من بدنِهِ أو ثوبه المانعة من أداء الصلاة، فإن كان كذلك فوجوده بمنزلة عدمِهِ فيباح له التيمم. [٢]قوله : نجاسة ؛ أي بقدر ما يمنع عن الصلاة، فإن كانت بقدر ما عفا الشارع عنه على ما سيأتي تفصيلُهُ إن شاء الله تعالى لم يلزمه صرفه إليها. [٣] قوله : بطريق الإباحة وبطريق التمليك ؛ يعني أنّ القدرة على الماء لا تنحصر في ملكه بأن يدخل الماء في ملكه بقبول الهبة أو الصدقة أو بالشراء أو غيرها من أسباب التمليك، بل تعم القدرة على سبيل الإباحة أيضاً. والفرق بينهما أن المملك له يدخلُ في ملكه ذلك الشيء، وتترتب عليه آثاره ، فيقدر على بيعه وهبته وسائر الانتقالاتِ وغير ذلك مما يجوز للإنسان أن يفعله في ملكه، وأما المباح له فلا يملك إلا الانتفاع بذلك الشيء الذي أبيح له، ولا يملك التصرف فيه ، كتصرف الرجل في ملكه. [٤] قوله : منفرداً ؛ فإن كان الماء كثيراً كافياً لكلِّ واحدٍ واحد مجتمعاً ، فانتقاض تيممهم أظهر. 
[0] قوله : لثبوت ؛ متعلق بقوله : «يعيد» أو بقوله : «ينتقض»؛ فإنّ ثبوت القدرةِ على الماء لكل واحد ، ولو على سبيل الإباحة علة لانتقاض التيمم، وهو علة لإعادته حين عدم الماء، يتوضؤ واحد منهم لظهور عجز الباقين.
Then, ability is only established when (the water) is not directed to a more important matter, such that if there is impurity on his body or clothing, he directs it to the impurity. Then ability is established by way of permissibility (ibaha) and by way of ownership (tamlik). If the owner of the water says to a group of those performing tayammum: 'Let whoever of you wishes perform wudu with this water,' and the water is sufficient for each one individually, the tayammum of each one is invalidated. Then if one of them performs wudu with it, the rest repeat their tayammum, because ability is established for each one individually.
[1] His statement: 'Then...etc.' means that what is intended by ability over water sufficient for his purification is the ability considered legally (shar'an), which is only when the water is not legally obligated to be directed to a matter more important than his purification, such as removing actual impurity from his body or clothing that prevents prayer. If that is the case, its existence is like non-existence, so tayammum is permissible for him. [2] His statement: 'impurity' means to the extent that prevents prayer; if it is to the extent that the Lawgiver has pardoned, as will be detailed later, he is not obligated to direct water to it. [3] His statement: 'by way of ibaha and by way of tamlik' means that ability over water is not restricted to ownership, such that water enters his ownership by accepting a gift, charity, purchase, or other means of ownership, but rather covers ability by way of permissibility as well. The difference between them is that the one who is given ownership enters that thing into his ownership and its effects attach to it, so he has power to sell it, gift it, and other transfers, and other things that a person is permitted to do with his property. As for the one who is permitted (mubah), he owns only the benefit of that thing which was permitted to him, and does not own disposition over it like the disposition of a man over his property. [4] His statement: 'individually' means if the water is abundant, sufficient for each one collectively, then invalidation of their tayammum is more apparent.
[0] His statement: 'because of the establishment' is connected to his statement: 'he repeats' or to his statement: 'is invalidated'; because the establishment of ability over water for each one, even by way of ibaha, is the cause for invalidation of tayammum, and it is the cause for repeating it when water is absent, when one of them performs wudu, due to the manifest inability of the rest.
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with explanation from the commentary on Al-Wiqaya. It defines the legal concept of 'qudra' (ability) over water for the validity of tayammum. The key principle is that tayammum is valid only when a person lacks the ability to use water, and this ability is legally recognized even if the water is not owned. The passage establishes two essential conditions: First, the water must not be required for a more important purpose, such as removing najasah (ritual impurity) that would prevent salah. If the water is needed to remove such impurity, it is not considered available for wudu, so tayammum remains valid. Second, ability can be established in two ways: (a) ownership (tamlik), where the person owns the water and can dispose of it fully, and (b) permissibility (ibaha), where the person is permitted to use the water without owning it. The example given illustrates this: if the water owner says to a group 'whoever wishes may do wudu,' this grants ibaha, and each person thereby has ability, so their tayammum is invalidated. If one uses the water, the rest lose their ability (since the water is consumed) and must repeat their tayammum. The commentary further clarifies that even if the water is abundant and sufficient for all collectively, the invalidation is even more apparent. The phrase 'li-thubut' links the establishment of ability as the cause for invalidation and the need to repeat tayammum when water is later absent.

Key Terms
القدرة (al-qudra): Legally recognized ability to utilize water, either through ownership or permissibility, sufficient for purification.
الإباحة (al-ibaha): The state where a person is legally permitted to use water without owning it, e.g., through permission from the owner.
التمليك (al-tamlik): Making something owned by a person, such as through gift, purchase, or inheritance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does the existence of water NOT establish qudra (ability) for the purpose of invalidating tayammum?
A) When the water is owned by another person.
B) When the water is needed to remove najasah that prevents salah.
C) When the water is insufficient for full wudu.
D) When the person does not have permission to use it.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, legal ability (qudra) over water is established both by ownership (tamlik) and by permissibility (ibaha), and if such ability exists—unless the water is needed for a more urgent purpose—tayammum becomes invalid.

Hibah al-Musha' and its Effect on Tayammum
Intra-Hanafi dispute on donation of undivided water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on hibah al-musha' concerning tayammum and explain why tayammum remains valid under both Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Gifted shared water does not invalidate tayammum—whether the gift fails (Abu Hanifa) or yields insufficient shares (Sahibayn).

This passage examines a subtle intra-Hanafi dispute about the effect of gifting undivided water (hibah al-musha') on a person's tayammum. The scenario involves a donor saying 'This water is for you' to a group of mutayammimeen, who then take possession. While both Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn agree that tayammum is not invalidated, they reach this conclusion through different legal reasoning. Understanding their rationales deepens your grasp of the conditions for invalidating tayammum and the rules of gift ownership.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and initial ruling
Read the passage: water is gifted to a group without dividing it, they take possession. The immediate ruling is that their tayammum is not invalidated.
The ruling is unanimous among the three imams, but the justifications differ.
2
Understand the condition for invalidating tayammum
Tayammum is invalidated only when the person has sufficient water for wudu. The key is 'qudra'—ability to use enough water. If ownership or possession does not give enough water for each, tayammum remains valid.
Ability must be actual, not merely potential.
3
Trace Abu Hanifa's reasoning
Abu Hanifa holds that hibah al-musha' of a partitionable thing (like water) is invalid unless the property is first divided and shares segregated. Since the gift is invalid, ownership does not transfer to the recipients; the water remains the donor's property. Thus, the mutayammimeen have no ability over water, and tayammum is valid.
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) follows Abu Hanifa's view.
4
Trace the Sahibayn's reasoning
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that hibah al-musha' is valid and confers ownership, but ownership is shared among all recipients. Each person owns an undivided portion, and since the total water is sufficient for each individually but not collectively, each person's share is insufficient for full wudu. Hence, no ability to invalidate tayammum.
Both imams agree on the result, but the Sahibayn treat the gift as effective yet yielding insufficient water.
5
Identify the mufta bihi and note additional transmission
The commentator marks 'al-asahh' (more correct) as Abu Hanifa's view. Additionally, 'Isam ibn Yusuf reported that hibah al-musha' is fasid (defective) and confers ownership with possession, but the apparent narration is that it does not confer ownership.
This extra layer shows further nuance within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما إذا قال : هذا الماء لكم، وقبضوا ، لا ينتقض تيممهم ، أما عندهما ، فلأنَّ هبة المشاع يوجب الملك على سبيل الاشتراك ، فيملك كلُّ واحدٍ مقداراً لا يكفيه، وأما عند أبي حنيفة له ، فالأصح (٤) أنه يبقى على ملك الواهب [١] قوله : هذا الماء لكم ؛ أي بلام التمليك، وكذا إذا صرح بلفظ دال على الهبة. [٢]قوله : وقبضوا ؛ أي المتيممون ذلك الماء، قيَّد بذلك لأنَّ الهبة لا تفيد الملك عندنا بدون القبض كما هو مفصل في (كتاب الهبة). [٣] قوله : أما عندهما ؛ تفصيله أنّ هبة المشاع : أي الشيء المشترك الشائع الغير يقسم ؛ أي يكون بحيث لو قسم لا يبقى منتفعا به ؛ كالرحى المنقسم إن كان ذلك مما لا والحمام والبيت الصغير جائزة اتفاقاً. وإن كان ذلك الشيء مما يقسم فهبته غير نافذة عند أبي حنيفة له ما لم يقسم، وتفرز حصة كل واحد، ويقبضها صاحبها. وعند أبي يوسف ومحمد الله: هذه أيضاً نافذة ومفيدة للملك، ففي ما إذا وهب الماء الكافي لكلّ واحدٍ من المتيممين انفراداً لا اجتماعاً من غير تقسيم وإفراز حصة كل منهم لا ينتقض تيممهم. أما عنده فظاهر ؛ لأنّ مثل هذه الهبة عنده ليست بنافذة، ولا مفيدة للملك ؛ فيبقى الماء على ملك الواهب، فلم تثبت قدرتهم على الماء مطلقاً. وأما عندهما ؛ فلأنّ هبة المشاع وإن كانت تفيد الملك لكنها تفيده اشتراكاً، فيملك كل واحد منهم في الصورة المذكورة شيئاً منه، وهو غير كاف لطهره ، فلم تثبت القدرة الناقضة للتيمم. (٤) قوله : فالأصح ؛ إشارة إلى وقوع الخلاف فيه، فإن عصام بن يوسف له روى أن هبة المشاع فاسدة، والفاسدة تفيد الملك بالقبض، وبه أخذ بعض المشايخ ، وظاهر الرواية أنّها لا تفيده، حتى لا ينفذ تصرّفه فيه. كذا في «الفتاوى الخيريّة)) (۱) ، (۲)، وغيرها. و«الحامدية»
But if he says: 'This water is for you,' and they take possession (qabd), their tayammum is not invalidated. As for according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), because the gift of an undivided share (hibah al-musha') necessitates ownership on a shared basis, so each one owns an amount insufficient for him. As for according to Abu Hanifa, the more correct (al-asahh) is that it remains the property of the donor. [1] His statement: 'This water is for you' means with the lam of ownership, and likewise if he explicitly uses a word indicating gift. [2] His statement: 'and they take possession' means the mutayammimeen take possession of that water. He restricted it with that because the gift does not effect ownership in our school without possession, as detailed in the book of Hibah. [3] His statement: 'As for according to the two' – its detail is that hibah al-musha' means the common, undivided, non-partitionable thing; that is, such that if it were divided, no benefit would remain from it, like the partitioned mill and the bathhouse and the small house – these are valid by agreement. But if that thing is partitionable, then its gift is not effective according to Abu Hanifa until it is divided, and the share of each is segregated and taken possession of by its owner. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, this too is effective and confers ownership. Thus in the case where one gifts water sufficient for each of the mutayammimeen individually (not collectively) without division and segregation of each one's share, their tayammum is not invalidated. As for according to him (Abu Hanifa), it is apparent because such a gift is not effective in his view, nor does it confer ownership, so the water remains the property of the donor, and thus their ability over water is not established at all. As for according to the two, because hibah al-musha', although it confers ownership, it confers it on a shared basis, so each one in the mentioned scenario owns a part of it, but it is insufficient for his purification, so the ability that invalidates tayammum is not established. (4) His statement: 'the more correct' indicates the existence of difference therein. For 'Isam ibn Yusuf narrated that hibah al-musha' is invalid (fasid), and the invalid confers ownership with possession, and some mashayikh adopted this. The apparent of the narration is that it does not confer ownership, such that his disposition in it is not effective. This is in al-Fatawa al-Khayriyyah and others, and al-Hamidiyyah.
Source pages p. 449

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of a gift of undivided water (hibah al-musha') on the validity of tayammum. The scenario: the water owner says 'This water is for you' (using tamlik wording) to a group of mutayammimeen, and they take possession (qabd). According to Abu Hanifa, such a gift of an undivided share in a partitionable thing (like water) is not effective without prior division and segregation of each share. Therefore, the water remains the donor's property, and the mutayammimeen do not have the ability to use it for wudu, so their tayammum remains valid. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), hibah al-musha' is effective and confers shared ownership. However, each person only owns an undivided, insufficient portion of the water; since the total water is sufficient for each individually but not collectively, each person's share is less than what is needed for purification. Therefore, the ability that would invalidate tayammum is not established, and the tayammum also remains valid. Thus, both positions agree that tayammum is not invalidated in this case, but for different reasons. The commentary also notes an additional transmission from 'Isam ibn Yusuf that hibah al-musha' is fasid and confers ownership with possession, which some scholars adopted, but the apparent narration is that it does not confer ownership. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the school is that hibah al-musha' of a partitionable thing is invalid and does not confer ownership, which aligns with Abu Hanifa's view.

Key Terms
هبة المشاع (hibah al-musha'): A gift of an undivided, shared portion of a property that is not yet partitioned.
القبض (al-qabd): Taking physical possession of the gifted item, required in Hanafi law for the gift to confer ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi) in the passage, if the owner of water says 'This water is for you' to three mutayammimeen and they take possession, what is the ruling on their tayammum?
A) Tayammum is invalid because they own the water.
B) Tayammum is valid because the gift is invalid and they do not own the water.
C) Tayammum is valid only if they are relatives of the donor.
D) Tayammum is invalid because the water is sufficient for each individually.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum remains valid when gifted water is undivided, regardless of whether the gift is considered invalid (Abu Hanifa) or yields insufficient shares (Sahibayn).

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
10 min
Hibah al-Musha' and Its Effect on Tayammum
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the effect of hibah al-musha' on tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that tayammum remains valid after receiving a gift of undivided water, and distinguish the reasoning of Abu Hanifa from that of the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Receiving undivided water as a gift does not break tayammum because each recipient lacks sufficient water.

When water is given as a gift to a group who have performed tayammum, does the availability of that water nullify their tayammum? The Hanafi school unanimously says no, but the reasoning splits between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples. This passage unpacks that legal nuance, showing how differences in the law of gifts (hibah) lead to the same practical outcome in purification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and legal question
The case: a donor gives a container of water to a group who have performed tayammum, but the water is not divided among them. Does this gift give them the ability to use water such that their tayammum is invalidated?
The key is whether the recipients legally 'own' enough water for purification.
2
State the agreed Hanafi ruling
All Hanafi authorities agree: tayammum is not invalidated. The practical ruling (mufta bihi) is that the tayammum remains valid.
The disagreement is only over the legal basis (ta'lil), not the outcome.
3
Follow Abu Hanifa's reasoning
Abu Hanifa holds that a gift of an undivided share (hibah al-musha') does not transfer ownership until the property is partitioned and each recipient takes possession. Since the water is not divided, it remains the property of the donor; the recipients never owned it, so they lack the ability to use water.
Zahir al-riwayah supports this view.
4
Follow the Sahibayn's reasoning
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad argue that hibah al-musha' does confer ownership, but shared ownership. Each recipient owns a fraction of the whole, but that fraction is insufficient for full purification (wudu or ghusl). Thus, the condition of having sufficient water is not met.
Both companions agree on the outcome, diverging only on why the gift is ineffective.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence is identical: tayammum stands. However, the difference surfaces in edge cases, e.g., if the donors later give explicit permission (ibahah) to a specific person, the Sahibayn would invalidate that person's tayammum (because they own a share), while Abu Hanifa would not (because they never owned anything).
This shows how a difference in usul al-fiqh can create branching rulings in subsidiary cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما إذا قال : هذا الماء لكم، وقبضوا ، لا ينتقض تيممهم ، أما عندهما ، فلأنَّ هبة المشاع يوجب الملك على سبيل الاشتراك ، فيملك كلُّ واحدٍ مقداراً لا يكفيه، وأما عند أبي حنيفة له ، فالأصح (٤) أنه يبقى على ملك الواهب [١] قوله : هذا الماء لكم ؛ أي بلام التمليك، وكذا إذا صرح بلفظ دال على الهبة. [٢]قوله : وقبضوا ؛ أي المتيممون ذلك الماء، قيَّد بذلك لأنَّ الهبة لا تفيد الملك عندنا بدون القبض كما هو مفصل في (كتاب الهبة). [٣] قوله : أما عندهما ؛ تفصيله أنّ هبة المشاع : أي الشيء المشترك الشائع الغير يقسم ؛ أي يكون بحيث لو قسم لا يبقى منتفعا به ؛ كالرحى المنقسم إن كان ذلك مما لا والحمام والبيت الصغير جائزة اتفاقاً. وإن كان ذلك الشيء مما يقسم فهبته غير نافذة عند أبي حنيفة له ما لم يقسم، وتفرز حصة كل واحد، ويقبضها صاحبها. وعند أبي يوسف ومحمد الله: هذه أيضاً نافذة ومفيدة للملك، ففي ما إذا وهب الماء الكافي لكلّ واحدٍ من المتيممين انفراداً لا اجتماعاً من غير تقسيم وإفراز حصة كل منهم لا ينتقض تيممهم. أما عنده فظاهر ؛ لأنّ مثل هذه الهبة عنده ليست بنافذة، ولا مفيدة للملك ؛ فيبقى الماء على ملك الواهب، فلم تثبت قدرتهم على الماء مطلقاً. وأما عندهما ؛ فلأنّ هبة المشاع وإن كانت تفيد الملك لكنها تفيده اشتراكاً، فيملك كل واحد منهم في الصورة المذكورة شيئاً منه، وهو غير كاف لطهره ، فلم تثبت القدرة الناقضة للتيمم. (٤) قوله : فالأصح ؛ إشارة إلى وقوع الخلاف فيه، فإن عصام بن يوسف له روى أن هبة المشاع فاسدة، والفاسدة تفيد الملك بالقبض، وبه أخذ بعض المشايخ ، وظاهر الرواية أنّها لا تفيده، حتى لا ينفذ تصرّفه فيه. كذا في «الفتاوى الخيريّة)) (۱) ، (۲)، وغيرها. و«الحامدية» (تنقيح الفتاوى الحامدية»(٢ : ٨٥). ولم تثبت الإباحة ؛ لأنه لَمّا بطل الهبةُ بطل ما في ضمنه من الإباحة، ثمَّ إن أباحوا واحداً بعينه ينتقض تيمُّمُهُ عندهما لا عنده ؛ لأَنَّهُ لما لم يملكُوهُ لا يصح إباحتهم.
And if he says: 'This water is for you,' and they take it, their tayammum is not invalidated. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), because a gift of an undivided share causes ownership on the basis of sharing, so each one owns an amount insufficient for him. According to Abu Hanifa, the correct view is that it remains the property of the donor. [1] His statement: 'This water is for you' means with the letter of ownership, and likewise if he explicitly uses a word indicating a gift. [2] His statement: 'and they take it' means the people performing tayammum take that water; this is conditioned because a gift does not confer ownership in our school without possession, as detailed in the Book of Gifts. [3] His statement: 'according to the two' – its detail is that a gift of an undivided share means a shared thing that is not divided; it is such that if divided it would no longer be beneficial, like a millstone, a bathhouse, or a small house – this is permissible by agreement. If the thing is divisible, its gift is not effective according to Abu Hanifa unless it is divided and each one's portion is separated and taken. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, this is also effective and confers ownership. So in the case where he gave water sufficient for each of those performing tayammum individually but not collectively, without division and allocation of each one's share, their tayammum is not invalidated. According to him (Abu Hanifa) it is obvious, because such a gift in his view is not effective and does not confer ownership, so the water remains the property of the donor, and thus their ability to use water is not established absolutely. According to the two, even though the gift of an undivided share confers ownership, it does so jointly, so each of them owns something from it in the mentioned situation, which is insufficient for his purification, so the ability that invalidates tayammum is not established. (4) His statement: 'the correct view' indicates that there is disagreement about it. Indeed, 'Isam ibn Yusuf narrated that a gift of an undivided share is invalid, and an invalid gift confers ownership by possession, and some mashayikh adopted this. The apparent transmission (zahir al-riwayah) is that it does not confer ownership, so that his disposal of it is not effective. This is mentioned in al-Fatawa al-Khayriyya and others, and al-Hamidiyya (Tanqih al-Fatawa al-Hamidiyya 2:85). And the permission (ibahah) is not established; because when the gift became void, what was included in it of permission also became void. Then if they permit one specific person, his tayammum is invalidated according to the two but not according to him (Abu Hanifa), because they do not own it, their permission is not valid.
Source pages p. 449

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of a gift of undivided water on the validity of tayammum. The issue arises when a person gives water to a group of people who have performed tayammum. The question is: does their ability to use this water break their tayammum? The ruling is that tayammum is not broken, but the reasoning differs between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples. According to Abu Hanifa, a gift of an undivided share (hibah al-musha') in a divisible item is not legally effective and does not transfer ownership. Therefore, the recipients do not actually own the water, and thus they lack the ability to use water for purification, so tayammum remains valid. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, such a gift does transfer ownership, but it gives each recipient a share of the whole, not exclusive ownership of a sufficient quantity. Since no one gets enough water for complete purification, the condition of having sufficient water is not met, and tayammum is not invalidated. The commentary further discusses the case where the gift is declared invalid (fasid); in that case, any implied permission to use the water also falls away, and if permission is given to a specific person, his tayammum is broken according to the disciples but not Abu Hanifa, because they lack ownership. The passage also notes a minority view from 'Isam ibn Yusuf that an invalid gift does confer ownership by possession, but the relied-upon transmission (zahir al-riwayah) is that it does not.

Key Terms
هبة المشاع (hibah al-musha'): A gift of an undivided share in a property that is not yet partitioned.
التيمم (al-tayammum): Dry ablution with clean earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person gives a container of water as a gift to a group who have performed tayammum, and the water is not divided, what happens to their tayammum?
A) It is invalidated because they now own water.
B) It remains valid because they do not have sufficient water individually.
C) It is invalidated only according to Abu Hanifa.
D) It remains valid only according to the Sahibayn.

Key Takeaway
The ruling that tayammum is not invalidated by a gift of undivided water is unanimous among the Hanafi masters, though the legal reasoning differs.

Apostasy Does Not Invalidate Tayammum
Intra-Hanafi dispute on apostasy and tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that apostasy does not invalidate tayammum, explain the rational proof (dalīl ʿaqlī) distinguishing between the act and its legal effect, and evaluate Zufar's opposing argument.

Core Idea
Apostasy nullifies reward, not legal purity: tayammum remains valid after return to Islam.

Does leaving Islam erase your purification? The Hanafi school makes a crucial distinction between the act of worship and its legal effect. In this lesson, we examine the ruling that apostasy does not break tayammum, and we see how Imam Zufar's contrary view is answered by a sharp analytical distinction between reward (thawāb) and legal state (ḥukm).

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Extract the precise ḥukm: tayammum remains valid after apostasy and reversion, provided no other nullifier occurred. Note the act (tayammum), the interruption (riddah), and the resumption (return to Islam).
The ruling applies to the state of ṭahārah, not the act of tayammum itself.
2
State Zufar's opposing position and his proof
Zufar holds that apostasy invalidates tayammum. His reasoning: tayammum is a rukhsah (concession) contrary to qiyās, so disbelief (kufr) contradicts it, just as it contradicts other acts of worship. Identify the principle: 'disbeliever is not qualified for worship.'
Zufar's argument is based on the nature of tayammum as an exceptional purification.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response distinguishes between the concluded act of tayammum and its remaining effect (waṣf al-ṭahārah). Apostasy cannot remove a completed act; it only affects ongoing or future acts. The legal purity (ṭahārah) is like that from wuḍūʾ – it remains despite apostasy.
This is a qiyās with wuḍūʾ: apostasy does not break wuḍūʾ, so it should not break tayammum.
4
Address the objection from verses on ḥubūṭ al-ʿamal
The opponent cites that apostasy nullifies all deeds. The Hanafi answer: nullification applies only to reward (thawāb), not to legal effects (aḥkām). The state of purity is a legal effect, not a deed whose reward is lost.
This distinction is critical: the same act can have both spiritual reward and legal consequences.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilāf)
If a person apostatises after tayammum and returns, the majority view (Abū Ḥanīfa, Abū Yūsuf, Muḥammad) allows prayer with that tayammum. Zufar would require a new tayammum. The muftā bihī is the majority position.
This difference directly affects the validity of acts performed after return.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا ردته
[٢] قوله : لا ردته ؛ بكسر الراء المهملة، وتشديد الدال المهملة ؛ أي لا ينقضُ التيمم ارتداد المتيمم ، فإذا تيمم المسلم ثم ارتد ثمّ أسلم ولم يوجد شيء من النواقض السابقة يبقى تيممه، فيصح أداء الصلاة به. وفيه خلاف زفر الله ، فإنّه يقولُ ببطلانه باعتراض الردة معللاً بأن الكفر ينافي التيمم : لأنه شرع مطهراً على خلاف القياس فينافيه الكفر كسائر العبادات ؛ لعدم أهلية الكافر لها. والجواب عنه : إن الباقي بعد التيمم ليس نفس التيمم ليرتفع بورودِ الكفر، بل الباقي هو وصف كونه طاهراً، واعتراض الكفر عليه لا ينافيه : كاعتراض الكفر على الوضوء، حيث لا تبطل الطهارة الحاصلة. فإن قلت : قد دلت الآيات والأحاديث على أنّ الردّة تحبط العمل، فكيف يبقى تيمم المرتد ووضوؤه. قلت : الردة إنما تحبط ثواب الأعمال لا حكماً آخر ثابتاً بها : كوصف الطهارة.
Apostasy does not invalidate (tayammum). [2] His statement: 'apostasy does not invalidate' – with kasra on the ra, and tashdid on the dal – means that the apostasy of the one performing tayammum does not invalidate the tayammum. So if a Muslim performs tayammum, then apostatizes (may Allah protect us from that), then becomes Muslim, and none of the previous nullifiers have occurred, his tayammum remains, and his prayer with it is valid. There is a disagreement with Zufar, for he says that it is invalidated by the occurrence of apostasy, reasoning that disbelief contradicts tayammum because it is a purification legislated contrary to analogy (as a concession), so disbelief contradicts it like other acts of worship, since the disbeliever is not qualified for them. The answer to him is: what remains after tayammum is not the tayammum itself to be removed by the arrival of disbelief, but rather what remains is the description of being pure (taharah), and the occurrence of disbelief does not contradict it, just as the occurrence of disbelief does not invalidate wudu[ where the purity obtained remains. If you say: verses and hadiths indicate that apostasy nullifies deeds, so how does the tayammum and wudu of an apostate remain? I say: apostasy only nullifies the reward of deeds, not another legal effect established by them, like the description of purity.
Source pages p. 450

Commentary
This passage addresses the effect of apostasy (riddah) on the validity of tayammum. The ruling is clear: apostasy does not break tayammum. If a Muslim performs tayammum, then leaves Islam, and later returns to Islam without having encountered any of the standard nullifiers of tayammum (like finding water, hadath, etc.), his tayammum remains valid and he can pray with it. Imam Zufar disagreed, arguing that disbelief (kufr) is incompatible with tayammum because tayammum is a form of purification that is a concession (rukhsah) contrary to analogy; thus, like other acts of worship, it is nullified by apostasy since the disbeliever lacks the capacity for worship. The Hanafi response distinguishes between the act of tayammum itself, which is concluded, and its effect (hukm), which is the state of purity (taharah). Apostasy does not remove this state, just as it does not remove the purity from wudu. The passage then addresses a potential objection: if apostasy nullifies all deeds, how can purity remain? The answer is that nullification (ihbat) only applies to the reward (thawab), not to the legal effects (ahkam) like purity. Thus, the taharah remains valid for future acts after return to Islam.

Key Terms
الردة (al-riddah): Apostasy from Islam; leaving the religion of Islam.
حبوط العمل (hubut al-‘amal): Nullification of deeds; the reward for good deeds is lost due to apostasy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, if a Muslim performs tayammum, then apostatizes, then returns to Islam, what is the ruling on his tayammum?
A) It is invalidated because apostasy nullifies all deeds.
B) It remains valid because apostasy only nullifies reward, not purity.
C) It is invalidated only according to Abu Hanifa.
D) It becomes valid only after he repeats tayammum.

Key Takeaway
Apostasy nullifies the reward of tayammum but not its legal effect of purity, so the tayammum remains valid upon return to Islam.

Apostasy Does Not Nullify Tayammum: Hanafi Ruling and Proof
Explaining that apostasy does not invalidate tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the effect of apostasy on tayammum and explain the reasoning (qiyas) used to derive it.

Core Idea
Apostasy does not nullify tayammum because it nullifies reward, not the legal state of purity.

You may wonder: if a Muslim performs tayammum, then apostatizes, and later returns to Islam, is his tayammum still valid? The Hanafi school answers with a clear position, supported by a subtle distinction between the act of purification and the resulting state of purity. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof through analogy with wudu, and the disagreement of Imam Zufar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is tayammum performed by a Muslim who then apostatizes and returns. The ruling is that the tayammum remains valid and the person may pray with it.
2
Locate the dalil
The Hanafi proof is qiyas (analogy) with wudu: just as wudu's purity is not nullified by apostasy, so too tayammum.
This is an analogical argument from an established ruling.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The common factor (illa) is that both wudu and tayammum produce a legal state of taharah (purity) that is a legal effect (hukm), not an act of worship. Apostasy nullifies reward, not legal states.
The illa is extracted by tanqih al-manat.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam Zufar disagrees, arguing that tayammum is an exceptional worship, so kufr nullifies it. He relies on the exceptional nature of tayammum.
This is an intra-Hanafi disagreement.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) is relied upon. The response distinguishes the act from the resulting state; apostasy only nullifies reward.
The mufta bihi is the majority view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا ردته
[1]
ولم تثبت الإباحة؛ لأنه لَمّا بطل الهبةُ بطل ما في ضمنه من الإباحة، ثمَّ إن أباحوا واحداً بعينه ينتقض تيمُّمُهُ عندهما لا عنده؛ لأَنَّهُ لما لم يملكُوهُ لا يصح إباحتهم.
(لا ردته) " حتى إذا تيمَّمَ المسلمُ ثم ارتد، نعوذ بالله تعالى منه، ثم أسلم تصح صلاته بذلك التيمم. [١] قوله : ولم يثبت؛ دفعُ دخل مقدر تقرير الدخل: أن الهبة تفيد أمرين: وإباحة الانتفاع، وبطلان ثبوت الملك بسبب كون الهبة هبة مشاع لا يستلزم بطلان الإباحة؛ لكونها تصح في مشاع، فينبغي في الصورة المذكورة أن تبقى الإباحة الملك، وينتقض التيمم. وتحرير الدفع: أن الإباحة في هذه الصورة لم تكن على سبيل الاستقلال، بل كانت في ضمن الهبة، فلما بطلت الهبة لم يثبت ما يتبعها أيضاً، لما تقرر في موضعه أنّ الشيء إذا بطل بطل ما في ضمنه، وأنَّ المبني على الفاسد فاسد.
[٢]قوله: لا ردته؛ بكسر الراء المهملة، وتشديد الدال المهملة؛ أي لا ينقضُ التيمم ارتداد المتيمم، فإذا تيمم المسلم ثم ارتد ثمّ أسلم ولم يوجد شيء من النواقض السابقة يبقى تيممه، فيصح أداء الصلاة به.
وفيه خلاف زفر الله، فإنّه يقولُ ببطلانه باعتراض الردة معللاً بأن الكفر ينا في التيمم: لأنه شرع مطهراً على خلاف القياس فينافيه الكفر كسائر العبادات؛ لعدم أهلية الكافر لها.
والجواب عنه: إن الباقي بعد التيمم ليس نفس التيمم ليرتفع بورودِ الكفر، بل الباقي هو وصف كونه طاهراً، واعتراض الكفر عليه لا ينافيه: كاعتراض الكفر على الوضوء، حيث لا تبطل الطهارة الحاصلة.
فإن قلت: قد دلت الآيات والأحاديث على أنّ الردّة تحبط العمل، فكيف يبقى تيمم المرتد ووضوؤه.
قلت: الردة إنما تحبط ثواب الأعمال لا حكماً آخر ثابتاً بها: كوصف الطهارة.
"Apostasy does not nullify (tayammum)." ... and the permission (to use the water) was not established; because when the gift (hibah) became void, what was implied in it of permission also became void. Then if they (the owners) permitted a specific (individual) his tayammum is nullified according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) but not according to him (Abu Hanifa) because since they did not own it (the water) their permission is invalid. (The phrase "no apostasy"): meaning when a Muslim performs tayammum then apostatizes (may Allah protect us) then returns to Islam, his prayer with that tayammum is valid. [1] His saying "and it was not established" is a rebuttal of an anticipated objection. The objection: hibah conveys two things: ownership and permission to benefit. The invalidity of hibah due to being shared (musha') does not necessitate the invalidity of permission because permission is valid in shared property. So in the mentioned scenario permission should remain and tayammum should be invalidated. The rebuttal: In this scenario permission was not independent but within hibah. When hibah becomes void, what follows it also becomes void, as established that when a thing becomes void, what is within it also becomes void, and what is built on corrupt is corrupt. [2] His saying "no apostasy" (with kasra on ra' and tashdid on dal): i.e., apostasy of the one who performed tayammum does not nullify tayammum. So if a Muslim performs tayammum then apostatizes then returns to Islam and none of the previous nullifiers occurred, his tayammum remains and he may validly perform prayer with it. There is a disagreement with Zufar (may Allah have mercy on him) who holds that it is nullified because apostasy intervenes, reasoning that kufr opposes tayammum since tayammum is legislated as a purifier contrary to analogy, so kufr contradicts it like other acts of worship because the disbeliever is not qualified for them. The response: What remains after tayammum is not the tayammum itself to be lifted by the occurrence of kufr, but rather the quality of being pure (taharah). The intervention of kufr does not contradict it, just as kufr does not nullify wudu's purification. If you say: Verses and hadith indicate that apostasy nullifies deeds, so how does the tayammum and wudu of an apostate remain? I say: Apostasy only nullifies the reward of deeds, not other rulings established by them, like the quality of purity.
Source pages p. 450

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Al-Wiqayah. The matn states "لا ردته" meaning apostasy does not nullify tayammum. The commentator explains that if a Muslim performs tayammum, then apostatizes, then returns to Islam, his tayammum remains valid and he can pray with it. He first addresses a potential objection about permission (ibahah) when water is a gift, clarifying that since the gift was invalid, the permission is also invalid. Then he explains the phrase "no apostasy" directly. He then discusses a disagreement with Imam Zufar, who holds that apostasy invalidates tayammum because kufr contradicts the nature of tayammum as an exceptional purifier. The Hanafi response distinguishes between the act of tayammum (which is no longer present after the time passes) and the legal state of taharah (purity) that remains, similar to wudu. Finally, an objection is raised that apostasy nullifies all deeds based on Quran and Sunnah. The response is that nullification applies to reward (thawab), not to legal effects like the state of purity. Thus, the relied-upon Hanafi position is that tayammum is not nullified by apostasy.

Key Terms
ردة (riddah): Apostasy from Islam; leaving the Islamic faith.
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution with clean earth or dust as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
طهارة (taharah): Legal purity, either physical (from impurity) or ritual (from hadath). Here it means the state of being pure for prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Apostasy does not nullify tayammum because it affects the reward of deeds, not the legal state of purity.

Delaying Prayer and Seeking Water: Recommendations and Obligations
Ruling on delaying prayer and obligating search for water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on delaying prayer when hoping for water and on seeking water, and distinguish between recommended and obligatory actions with their conditions.

Core Idea
Delaying prayer for water is recommended, not obligatory; seeking water becomes obligatory when water is thought to be near, especially in inhabited areas.

In this passage, the commentator expands on two interrelated rulings for the one who lacks water: when to delay prayer and when to actively seek water. Understanding the distinction between recommended (nadb) and obligatory (wajib) actions, and the role of conjecture (zann), is essential for correct practice. The hadith of the Prophet ﷺ provides the evidence for the recommended nature of delaying, while the obligation of seeking depends on location and presumption.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings in the matn
The matn states: (1) It is recommended for one who hopes for water to delay his prayer until the end of the time. (2) It is obligatory to seek water within a ghalwah if he thinks it near.
These are separate but related: the first pertains to the timing of prayer, the second to the prerequisite of seeking water.
2
Understand the proof for delaying prayer
The commentator cites a hadith from Abu Sa'id Al-Khudri where two travelers prayed with tayammum and then found water. The Prophet praised the one who did not repeat as 'following the Sunnah', indicating delaying is Sunnah, not wajib.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is clear (qati al-dalalah) regarding the recommendation.
3
Distinguish the conditions for seeking water
The passage details that in inhabited areas (umranat) seeking is wajib by consensus due to presumption of existence. In the desert, it is wajib only when one thinks (zann) water is near within a ghalwah; otherwise it is merely recommended (mustahabb).
'Ghalwah' is defined as 300-400 cubits (approx 150-200 meters).
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on repetition
If one fails to seek when wajib and prays with tayammum, then later seeks and does not find water, repetition (i'adah) is wajib according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the two), but Abu Yusuf disagrees. The relied-upon position is that of the two.
This difference highlights that the obligation of seeking is connected to the validity of the prayer in the view of the majority.
5
Apply the rulings to a practical scenario
Consider a traveler in a desert who strongly believes water is within a ghalwah. He should delay his prayer to the end of the time and actively search. If he finds water, he performs wudu and prays. If not, his tayammum prayer is valid and he does not need to repeat (if he searched). If he did not search, repetition is required.
The scenario integrates all elements: hope, zann, location, and the consequence of omission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ندب لراجيه أن يؤخّر صلاته إلى آخر الوقت ويجب طلبه قدر غلوة، لو ظنَّهُ قريباً وإلا فلا
[۱]-
وندب لراجيه) أي لراجي (۱) الماء، أن يؤخّر صلاته إلى آخر الوقت)، فلو صلّى بالتيمم في أول الوقت، ثمَّ وجدَ الماء والوقت باق لا يعيدُ الصَّلاة". ( ويجبُ طَلَبُهُ قدر غلوة، لو ظنَّهُ " قريباً وإلا فلا) ، الغَلُوةُ ) : مقدار ثلاثمئة ذراع إلى أربعمئة. [١]قوله : وندب؛ أي يستحب لمن كان يرجو إدراك الماء والقدرة عليه إن أخر صلاته من أول الوقت أن يؤخّرها لإحراز أكمل الطهارتين، وليس ذلك بواجب لثبوتِ العجز في الحال، وتخيير المصلّي شرعاً في أدائه أوّل الوقت أو أوسطه أو آخره.
[٢]قوله : لا يعيد الصلاة؛ لما أخرجه أبو داود والحاكم عن أبي سعيد الخدري له قال: «خرج رجلان في سفر فحضرت الصلاة وليس معهما ماء، فتيمما فصليا ثم وجدا الماء في الوقت، فأعاد أحدهما ولم يعد الآخر، ثم أتيا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وذكرا ذلك له، فقال للذي لم يعد: أصبت السنة وأجزأ لك صلاتك، وقال للذي أعاد: لك الأجر مرتين (۳) [٣] قوله : لو ظنه... الخ؛ تفصيله على ما في «البحر» وغيره: إن فاقد الماء إن كان في العمرانات فالطلب واجب اتِّفاقاً؛ لأنَّ غلبة وجود الماء في العمرانات دليل ظاهر على وجوده، فلا بد من الطلب ليظهر عدمه، فيتحقق عجزه وإن كان في الصحراء فإن لم يظنّه قريباً لا يجب عليه الطلب، بل يستحب إذا كان على طمع من وجود الماء، وإن ظنه قريباً يجب عليه الطلب؛ لكون الظن معتبراً شرعاً، فلو لم يطلب وصلّى بالتيمم ثم طلبه فلم يجده وجبت عليه الإعادة عندهما، خلافاً لأبي يوسف، ذكره في «السراج الوهاج».
It is recommended for one who hopes (to find water) to delay his prayer until the end of the time, and it is obligatory for him to seek it (water) the distance of a bowshot (ghalwah), if he thinks it is near, otherwise not. [1] His saying: "and it is recommended for one who hopes" i.e., one who hopes for water, to delay his prayer until the end of the time. So if he prays with tayammum at the beginning of the time, then finds water while time remains, he does not repeat the prayer. "And it is obligatory to seek it the distance of a bowshot, if he thinks it is near, otherwise not." Al-Ghalwah: the amount of three hundred to four hundred cubits. [1] His saying: "recommended" (nadb) i.e., it is mustahabb for the one who hopes to obtain water and is able to do so if he delays his prayer from the beginning of the time to delay it in order to attain the more complete of the two purifications. That is not obligatory because inability is established at the moment, and the worshipper is legally given the choice to pray at the beginning, middle, or end of the time. [2] His saying: "he does not repeat the prayer" is based on what Abu Dawud and Al-Hakim narrated from Abu Sa'id Al-Khudri (may Allah be pleased with him) that he said: "Two men set out on a journey, and the time for prayer came while they had no water. They performed tayammum and prayed, then they found water within the time. One of them repeated the prayer and the other did not. Then they came to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and mentioned that to him. He said to the one who did not repeat: 'You have followed the Sunnah and your prayer suffices you.' And he said to the one who repeated: 'You have the reward twice.'" [3] His saying: "if he thinks..." etc., its detail according to Al-Bahr and others: One who lacks water if he is in inhabited areas, seeking is obligatory by agreement because the prevalence of water in inhabited areas is a clear indication of its existence, so seeking is necessary to establish its absence and thus realize his inability. If he is in the desert, and he does not think it near, seeking is not obligatory, rather it is recommended if he has hope of finding water. If he thinks it near, seeking becomes obligatory because conjecture (zann) is legally considered. If he does not seek and prays with tayammum, then seeks and does not find it, repetition (i'adah) is obligatory according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), contrary to Abu Yusuf, as mentioned in Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj.
Source pages p. 451

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of Al-Wiqayah concerning two issues: (1) delaying prayer for one who hopes to find water, and (2) the obligation of seeking water. The commentator explains that it is recommended (nadb/mustahabb) for a person who is hopeful or has a strong expectation of finding water to delay his prayer until the end of the time in order to perform ablution with water (the more complete purification). This is not obligatory because at the present moment he is unable to use water, and the shari'ah allows prayer at any time within the window. If he prays with tayammum at the beginning and then finds water within the same time, he does not need to repeat the prayer; a hadith from Abu Hurayrah (correctly Abu Sa'id Al-Khudri) is cited as proof. The second ruling is about seeking water. The matn states it is obligatory to seek water within a distance of a ghalwah (approx. 300-400 cubits) if one thinks water is near. The commentary elaborates: if in inhabited areas, seeking is obligatory by consensus because water is likely present. If in the desert, it depends on one's estimation: if he thinks water is nearby, seeking becomes obligatory because legal conjecture is legally valid; otherwise it is merely recommended. If he fails to seek and prays with tayammum, then later seeks and does not find water, he must repeat his prayer according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), but Abu Yusuf disagrees, holding that repetition is not required. The relied-upon position is that of the majority (the two).

Key Terms
ندب (nadb): Recommendation; an action that is encouraged but not obligatory, synonymous with mustahabb.
غلوة (ghalwah): A distance measure, approximately 300 to 400 cubits (about 150-200 meters).
عمرانات (umranat): Inhabited areas, populated places like villages or towns where water is expected to be available.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person is in an inhabited area and has no water, what is the ruling on seeking water before performing tayammum?
A) Seeking is recommended (sunnah).
B) Seeking is obligatory (wajib).
C) Seeking is not required because water is not expected.
D) Seeking is obligatory only if one is a resident, not a traveller.

Key Takeaway
Delaying prayer for water is Sunnah; seeking water is Wajib in inhabited areas or when strong presumption of nearness exists; omission of wajib seeking necessitates repetition of prayer.

Taharah — Purification
beginner

Delaying Prayer for Tayammum: A Recommended Act
States and comments on delaying prayer and searching for water in tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that delaying prayer for tayammum is recommended (mustahabb) not obligatory, and cite the hadith proof that finding water later does not require repetition.

Core Idea
Delaying prayer for tayammum is recommended to seek complete purity; finding water later does not require repetition.

When a traveler has no water but hopes to find it later, should he delay his prayer until the end of the time? This passage clarifies that it is recommended, not mandatory. We also learn that if he prays with tayammum early and finds water later, his prayer is valid—contrary to a common misconception.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling: delaying is mustahabb
The text says 'وندب' (it is recommended). Understand the difference between wajib and mustahabb in this context.
Recommended acts are rewarded but not required; omitting them does not incur sin.
2
Understand the rationale
The reason is to attain the more complete purification (water over tayammum). The worshipper has a choice of when to pray within the time.
3
Examine the dalil
The hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri about two travelers. Identify the part that supports non-repetition: the Prophet said 'أصبت السنة وأجزأ لك صلاتك' to the one who did not repeat.
The hadith is narrated by Abu Dawud and al-Hakim.
4
Apply the ruling
If one prays with tayammum early, then finds water within the time, he does not repeat. The Prophet's approval indicates validity.
This applies even if water is found within the same prayer time.
5
Distinguish from other schools
Some schools may require repetition; but Hanafi relies on this hadith and the principle that tayammum purifies sufficiently.
The text notes that the one who repeated got double reward, but it was not obligatory.

كتاب الطهارة التيمم
٤٥٣
وندب لراجيه أن يؤخّر صلاته إلى آخر الوقت ويجب طلبه قدر غلوة، لو ظنَّهُ قريباً
وإلا فلا
[۱]- وندب لراجيه) أي لراجي (۱) الماء ، أن يؤخّر صلاته إلى آخر الوقت)، فلو صلّى بالتيمم في أول الوقت ، ثمَّ وجدَ الماء والوقت باق لا يعيدُ الصَّلاة". ( ويجبُ طَلَبُهُ قدر غلوة ، لو ظنَّهُ " قريباً وإلا فلا) ، الغَلُوةُ ) : مقدار ثلاثمئة ذراع إلى أربعمئة. [١]قوله : وندب ؛ أي يستحب لمن كان يرجو إدراك الماء والقدرة عليه إن أخر صلاته من أول الوقت أن يؤخّرها لإحراز أكمل الطهارتين، وليس ذلك بواجب لثبوتِ العجز في الحال، وتخيير المصلّي شرعاً في أدائه أوّل الوقت أو أوسطه أو آخره.
[٢]قوله : لا يعيد الصلاة ؛ لما أخرجه أبو داود والحاكم عن أبي سعيد الخدري له قال : «خرج رجلان في سفر فحضرت الصلاة وليس معهما ماء، فتيمما فصليا ثم وجدا الماء في الوقت ، فأعاد أحدهما ولم يعد الآخر ، ثم أتيا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وذكرا ذلك له ، فقال للذي لم يعد : أصبت السنة وأجزأ لك صلاتك، وقال للذي أعاد : لك الأجر مرتين (۳) [٣] قوله : لو ظنه... الخ ؛ تفصيله على ما في «البحر» وغيره : إن فاقد الماء إن كان في العمرانات فالطلب واجب اتِّفاقاً ؛ لأنَّ غلبة وجود الماء في العمرانات دليل ظاهر على وجوده، فلا بد من الطلب ليظهر عدمه، فيتحقق عجزه
وإن كان في الصحراء فإن لم يظنّه قريباً لا يجب عليه الطلب، بل يستحب إذا كان على طمع من وجود الماء، وإن ظنه قريباً يجب عليه الطلب ؛ لكون الظن معتبراً شرعاً، فلو لم يطلب وصلّى بالتيمم ثم طلبه فلم يجده وجبت عليه الإعادة عندهما، خلافاً لأبي يوسف ، ذكره في «السراج الوهاج».
(۱) المراد بالرجاء غلبة الظن فإن كان لا يرجوه لا يؤخر الصلاة عن أول الوقت ؛ لأن فائدة الانتظار احتمال وجدان الماء، فيؤديها بأكمل الطهارتين. ينظر : «البحر» (١: ١٦٣ - ١٦٤).
(۲) الغَلوة : الغاية مقدار رمية. ينظر : «الصحاح»(۲ : ۲۰۸).
(۳) في «المستدرك»(١ : ٢٨٦)، وصححه، وسنن الدارمي (۱) : (۲۰۷) ، و(سنن البيهقي الكبير»
(۱ : ۲۳۱)، و(سنن أبي داود » (۱) : (۹۳) ، و«المجتبى»(۱ : ۲۱۳)، وغيرها.
(٤) (البحر الرائق (۱ : ١٦٩).
وعن أبي يوسف : أنه إذا كان الماء بحيث لو ذهب إليه وتوضأ تذهب القافلة وتغيب عن بصره، وكان بعيداً جاز له التّيمم، قال صاحب «المحيط»: هذا حسن جدا (۱۱)
Book of Purification: Tayammum. 453. And it is recommended for one who hopes for water to delay his prayer to the end of the time, and it is obligatory for him to search for it the distance of a stone's throw if he thinks it is near, otherwise no. [1] (And it is recommended for one who hopes) i.e., one who hopes for water, to delay his prayer to the end of the time, so if he prayed with tayammum at the beginning of the time then found water while the time remains, he does not repeat the prayer. (And it is obligatory for him to search for it the distance of a stone's throw if he thinks it is near, otherwise no), the stone's throw is three hundred cubits to four hundred cubits. [1] His statement: 'and it is recommended' i.e., it is mustahabb for one who hopes to obtain water and has the ability to do so if he delays his prayer from the beginning of the time to delay it in order to attain the more complete of the two purifications, and that is not obligatory due to the establishment of inability at the present moment, and the legal choice of the worshipper to perform it at the beginning, middle, or end of the time. [2] His statement: 'he does not repeat the prayer' because of what Abu Dawud and al-Hakim narrated from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: 'Two men set out on a journey, and the time for prayer came while they had no water. They performed tayammum and prayed, then they found water within the time. One of them repeated and the other did not. Then they came to the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and mentioned that to him. He said to the one who did not repeat: 'You have followed the Sunnah and your prayer is sufficient for you.' And he said to the one who repeated: 'For you is the reward twice.' [3] His statement: 'if he thinks... etc.'; its detail according to what is in 'al-Bahr' and others: The one who lacks water if he is in inhabited areas, then search is obligatory by consensus, because the prevalent existence of water in inhabited areas is a clear indication of its presence, so search is necessary to manifest its absence, thereby establishing his inability. If he is in the desert, then if he does not think it is near, search is not obligatory, but it is recommended if he is hopeful of the existence of water. If he thinks it is near, search is obligatory, because assumption is legally considered. So if he did not search and prayed with tayammum, then searched and did not find it, repetition is obligatory according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), contrary to Abu Yusuf, as mentioned in 'al-Siraj al-Wahhaj'. (1) What is meant by 'hope' is predominant assumption; if he does not have such hope, he should not delay the prayer from the beginning of the time, because the benefit of waiting is the possibility of finding water, so he performs it with the more complete of the two purifications. See: 'al-Bahr' (1:163-164). (2) 'al-Ghalwah': the distance of an arrow shot. See: 'al-Sihah' (2:208). (3) In 'al-Mustadrak' (1:286), and he declared it authentic, and Sunan al-Darimi (1:207), and Sunan al-Bayhaqi al-Kabir (1:231), and Sunan Abi Dawud (1:93), and al-Mujtaba (1:213), and others. (4) al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (1:169). And from Abu Yusuf: that if the water is such that if he goes to it and performs wudu, the caravan will leave and disappear from his sight, and it is distant, then tayammum is permissible for him. The author of 'al-Muhit' said: This is very good (11).
Source pages p. 451

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on Tayammum deals with two rulings: (1) it is recommended (mustahabb) for one who has hope of finding water to delay his prayer until the end of the prayer time, so that he may perform wudu if he finds it. This is not obligatory because he is currently unable to use water and because Islamic law gives the worshipper the choice to pray at any time during the period. (2) It is obligatory for him to search for water if he thinks it is near, within a distance of a stone's throw (ghalwah: 300-400 cubits). The commentator then explains that if he prayed with tayammum at the beginning of the time and then found water while the time remains, his prayer is valid and he does not need to repeat it. This is proven by the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, where the Prophet approved of the man who did not repeat. The detail: if the person is in inhabited areas, searching is obligatory by consensus because water is prevalent. In the desert, if he does not think water is near, searching is not obligatory but recommended if he has hope. If he thinks it is near, searching becomes obligatory because shar' considers assumption. If he fails to search in that case and prays, then searches and does not find water, he must repeat according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but Abu Yusuf disagrees. The commentator also brings a quote from Abu Yusuf about a scenario where fetching water would cause the caravan to leave him behind; in such a case, tayammum is permissible. The author of 'al-Muhit' considers this ruling very good.

Key Terms
التيمم (al-tayammum): Dry ablution with clean earth as a substitute for wudu when water is unavailable or harmful.
الرجاء (al-raja'): Hope or predominant assumption of finding water; it is not mere wish but a strong likelihood.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, when is it obligatory to search for water for tayammum?
A) Always, regardless of location or assumption.
B) Only when one is in inhabited areas.
C) When one thinks water is near (within a ghalwah distance).
D) Only at the end of the prayer time.

Key Takeaway
Delaying prayer for tayammum is recommended if you hope for water; your tayammum prayer is valid even if you find water later.

Searching for Water: Obligation and Repetition
States and comments on delaying prayer and searching for water in tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which searching for water becomes obligatory in the Hanafi school, and explain the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding repetition when search is neglected.

Core Idea
Searching for water is obligatory only if you think it is near; neglecting search when obliged requires repeating the prayer.

The obligation to search for water before tayammum is not absolute. This passage details the conditions: if you are in inhabited areas, search is always obligatory; in the desert, it depends on your assumption. Furthermore, if you fail to search when you should have, your prayer is deficient and must be repeated according to the majority of Hanafi imams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of locations
The text distinguishes two scenarios: being in inhabited areas ('amranat) and being in the desert. The ruling varies.
2
Rule for inhabited areas
In inhabited areas, searching is wajib by consensus because water is prevalent. The person must search to confirm absence before resorting to tayammum.
This is agreed upon among Hanafis.
3
Rule for the desert
In the desert, search is not obligatory if you do not think water is near. But if you have a predominant assumption (ghalabat al-dhann) that water is within a stone's throw (ghalwah), then search becomes wajib.
The distance is 300-400 cubits.
4
Consequence of neglecting search
If you were obligated to search but did not, then prayed with tayammum, and later found no water, you must repeat the prayer according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf disagrees in cases of hardship.
The intra-Hanafi dispute is noted.
5
Evaluate Abu Yusuf's exception
Abu Yusuf holds that if fetching water would cause the caravan to leave you behind, tayammum is permissible and no repetition is required. The author of al-Muhit considers this 'very good' (hasan jiddan).
This is a practical concession for travelers.

Source Text

And it is recommended for one who hopes for water to delay his prayer to the end of the time, and it is obligatory for him to search for it the distance of a stone's throw if he thinks it is near, otherwise no. They performed tayammum and prayed, then they found water within the time. One of them repeated and the other did not. Then they came to the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and mentioned that to him. He said to the one who did not repeat: 'You have followed the Sunnah and your prayer is sufficient for you.' And he said to the one who repeated: 'For you is the reward twice.' [3] His statement: 'if he thinks... etc.'; its detail according to what is in 'al-Bahr' and others: The one who lacks water if he is in inhabited areas, then search is obligatory by consensus, because the prevalent existence of water in inhabited areas is a clear indication of its presence, so search is necessary to manifest its absence, thereby establishing his inability. If he is in the desert, then if he does not think it is near, search is not obligatory, but it is recommended if he is hopeful of the existence of water. If he thinks it is near, search is obligatory, because assumption is legally considered. So if he did not search and prayed with tayammum, then searched and did not find it, repetition is obligatory according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), contrary to Abu Yusuf, as mentioned in 'al-Siraj al-Wahhaj'. (1) What is meant by 'hope' is predominant assumption; if he does not have such hope, he should not delay the prayer from the beginning of the time, because the benefit of waiting is the possibility of finding water, so he performs it with the more complete of the two purifications. See: 'al-Bahr' (1:163-164). (2) 'al-Ghalwah': the distance of an arrow shot. See: 'al-Sihah' (2:208). (3) In 'al-Mustadrak' (1:286), and he declared it authentic, and Sunan al-Darimi (1:207), and Sunan al-Bayhaqi al-Kabir (1:231), and Sunan Abi Dawud (1:93), and al-Mujtaba (1:213), and others. (4) al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (1:169). And from Abu Yusuf: that if the water is such that if he goes to it and performs wudu, the caravan will leave and disappear from his sight, and it is distant, then tayammum is permissible for him. The author of 'al-Muhit' said: This is very good (11).
Source pages p. 451

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on Tayammum deals with two rulings: (1) it is recommended (mustahabb) for one who has hope of finding water to delay his prayer until the end of the prayer time, so that he may perform wudu if he finds it. This is not obligatory because he is currently unable to use water and because Islamic law gives the worshipper the choice to pray at any time during the period. (2) It is obligatory for him to search for water if he thinks it is near, within a distance of a stone's throw (ghalwah: 300-400 cubits). The commentator then explains that if he prayed with tayammum at the beginning of the time and then found water while the time remains, his prayer is valid and he does not need to repeat it. This is proven by the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, where the Prophet approved of the man who did not repeat. The detail: if the person is in inhabited areas, searching is obligatory by consensus because water is prevalent. In the desert, if he does not think water is near, searching is not obligatory but recommended if he has hope. If he thinks it is near, searching becomes obligatory because shar' considers assumption. If he fails to search in that case and prays, then searches and does not find water, he must repeat according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but Abu Yusuf disagrees. The commentator also brings a quote from Abu Yusuf about a scenario where fetching water would cause the caravan to leave him behind; in such a case, tayammum is permissible. The author of 'al-Muhit' considers this ruling very good.

Key Terms
التيمم (al-tayammum): Dry ablution with clean earth as a substitute for wudu when water is unavailable or harmful.
الغلوة (al-ghalua): A measure of distance, approximately 300-400 cubits (about 150-200 meters).
الرجاء (al-raja'): Hope or predominant assumption of finding water; it is not mere wish but a strong likelihood.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, when is it obligatory to search for water for tayammum?
A) Always, regardless of location or assumption.
B) Only when one is in inhabited areas.
C) When one thinks water is near (within a ghalwah distance).
D) Only at the end of the prayer time.

Key Takeaway
Searching for water is obligatory if you think it is near; neglecting this obligation requires repeating the prayer per the majority Hanafi opinion.

Forgetting Water and Tayammum: The Excuse of Forgetfulness
States and comments on forgetting water in saddlebag

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a person forgets water in his baggage and prays with tayammum, and distinguish it from cases of doubt or assumption.

Core Idea
Forgetfulness that water is available excuses the tayammum prayer; doubt or assumption that water is gone requires repetition.

This passage deals with a common travel scenario: you forget water in your bag, pray with tayammum, then remember. Do you repeat? The Hanafi school says no, due to the excuse of forgetfulness. However, the ruling hinges on the exact mental state—forgetfulness versus doubt—and on when you remember. Let's dissect the conditions and scope of this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal classification
The act is performing tayammum prayer while having water available but forgotten. The hukm: prayer is valid (sahih) and no repetition is required.
This is the core ruling from the matn al-Wiqayah.
2
Distinguish forgetfulness from doubt
Forgetfulness (nisyan) is a valid excuse. Doubt (shakk) or assumption (zann) that water is gone is not—if water is found later, repetition is required by consensus.
The commentary emphasizes this distinction to avoid confusion.
3
Determine the scope of the ruling
The ruling applies to both traveler and resident; the mention of 'traveler' is incidental. Also, it applies whether remembrance is within the prayer time or after—but if remembered during the prayer, the prayer must be cut and repeated.
The phrase 'within the time' is not to restrict but to highlight the during-pregnancy exception.
4
Understand the term 'rahl' (saddlebag)
'Rahl' means the usual place where water is stored, whether a camel saddle, a home, or baggage. This broadens the application.
The commentators preferred this practical interpretation.
5
Note the Abu Yusuf scenario
If water is distant and fetching it would cause hardship (caravan leaves), tayammum is permissible even without forgetfulness. This ruling is endorsed as 'very good' because it relieves hardship.
This is a separate but related ruling included in the passage.
