454. 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah 'ala Sharh al-Wiqayah. And if a traveler forgets it (water) in his saddlebag, and he prays with tayammum, then remembers it within the time. [And from Abu Yusuf: that if the water is such that if he goes to it and performs wudu, the caravan will leave and disappear from his sight, and it is distant, then tayammum is permissible for him. The author of 'al-Muhit' said: This is very good (11).] [4] [0] (And if a traveler forgets it in his saddlebag, and prays with tayammum, then remembers it within the time (0) [1] His statement: 'This is very good' – with kasra of the jim and tashdid of the dal – i.e., definitely or much, and that because it is more convenient and repels hardship; for the traveler remaining alone or the caravan disappearing from his sight is hardship, especially in fearful deserts and especially for the weak. [2] His statement: 'and if he forgets it' – i.e., the water – specifying forgetfulness is to avoid the case where he doubts or thinks that the water has been used up, then prays with tayammum and then finds it, for then he repeats by consensus. Thus in 'al-Siraj al-Wahhaj'. [3] His statement: 'traveler' – this is an incidental restriction, for the ruling applies also to a resident, as Qadi Khan stated in his Fatawa. Also, [41] His statement: 'in his saddlebag' – with fatha, for a camel like a saddle for a riding beast, and it is said for a person's home and dwelling, and that is what is meant here, indicated in 'al-Mughrib' (2), and the author of 'al-Bahr' (3) chose that the meaning here is the first (camel saddle) based on their saying: 'if the water was in the back part of the saddle'... and the author of 'al-Nahr' held that what is meant here is what water is usually placed in, whether a home or a camel saddle. [0] His statement: 'within the time' – the purpose is not to avoid the case of remembering after the time, for it is stated in 'al-Hidayah' and others that the ruling is the same in both cases, rather the purpose is to indicate that this ruling only applies if he remembers after the prayer; if he remembers during the prayer, he must cut it and repeat the prayer, as stated in 'al-Siraj al-Wahhaj'.
Source pages p. 452

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific scenario: a traveler forgets water in his saddlebag (or home), prays with tayammum, then remembers that water was available during the prayer time. The ruling, as clarified by the commentary, is that he does not need to repeat the prayer. The commentator highlights that this is specific to forgetfulness; if he had doubt or thought the water was finished and then found it, he must repeat by consensus. The restriction 'traveler' is incidental—the same ruling applies to a resident. The term 'rahl' is explained: it can mean a camel saddle or a place of residence; the preferable interpretation here is the place where water is usually kept. The phrase 'within the time' is not to distinguish from remembering after the time (since the ruling is the same), but to clarify that if he remembers during the prayer, he must break the prayer and repeat it. A separate note from Abu Yusuf is included: if going to fetch water would cause the caravan to leave him behind and it is distant, tayammum is permissible, and this ruling is considered very good (hasan jiddan) by the author of al-Muhit because it relieves hardship.

Key Terms
النسيان (al-nisyan): Forgetfulness, distinguished from doubt or assumption that water is gone; only forgetfulness excuses non-repetition.
الرحل (al-rahil): A camel saddle or, by extension, a place where water is stored, such as a home or baggage.
الوقت (al-waqt): The time of prayer; used here to indicate that the ruling applies whether remembrance is within the time or after, but if during the prayer, the prayer must be cut.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) In forgetfulness, no repetition; in doubt, repetition required.
B) Both require repetition.
C) Neither requires repetition.
D) Doubt requires no repetition, forgetfulness does.

Key Takeaway
A tayammum prayer performed due to genuine forgetfulness of available water is valid and need not be repeated, unlike cases of doubt or assumption.

Tayammum Due to Human Constraint: Obligation to Repeat Prayer
Stating ruling on tayammum due to human constraint and obligation to repeat prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tayammum when the impediment is from human beings and explain why repetition (i‘adah) is required.

Core Idea
Human-caused impediments permit tayammum but do not lift the obligation to use water.

Not all excuses for tayammum are equal. The Hanafi school distinguishes between excuses from Allah (illness, cold) and excuses from human beings (captivity, threats). In the latter case, tayammum is valid for immediate prayer, but the prayer must be repeated once the human constraint is removed. This lesson clarifies that distinction and the underlying legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of excuses
The text divides excuses into two types: from Allah (min jihah Allah) and from human beings (min jihah al-‘ibad). Understand each category and their examples.
Examples from Allah: illness, extreme cold, fear of thirst. Examples from humans: captivity, imprisonment, death threats.
2
State the ruling for each category
For Allah-caused excuses: tayammum is valid and no i‘adah is required. For human-caused excuses: tayammum is valid but i‘adah is wajib.
The text states: 'في هذه الصورة يجوز له التيمم وأداء الصلاة به في الحال، لكن تجب عليه الإعادة بعد زوال ذلك المانع.'
3
Explain the rationale
The human impediment is temporary and does not change the original obligation to use water; tayammum is a concession for necessity. Once the impediment is removed, the original obligation returns.
In contrast, excuses from Allah lift the obligation entirely because the inability is intrinsic to the person.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi disagreement
The author refutes a contrary view from Dhakhirat al-Uqba that claimed no repetition. The authors maintains that i‘adah is required, as shown in al-Si‘ayah.
This disagreement highlights the importance of the distinction.
5
Apply the ruling
Consider scenarios: a captive prevented by disbelievers, a prisoner with no water access, a person threatened with death. Determine the ruling for each.
In all these cases, the prayer performed with tayammum must be repeated after the constraint ends.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجب أن يُعلم أنَّ المانع عن الوضوء إذا كان من جهة العبادِ كأسير ينعُهُ الكفار عن الوضوء أو محبوس في السجن، والذي قيل له : إن توضأت قتلتك يجوز له التيمم لكن إذا زالَ المانع فينبغي أن يعيدَ الصَّلاة، كذا في «الذخيرة»). والحق أن الإشارة به إلى صدر كلامه فقط ، فاحفظ هذا ولا تصغ إلى التوجيه المذكور في ذخيرة العقبى» (۲) فقد بينا بطلانه في «السعاية»(۳). [١]قوله : ويجب أن يعلم ... الخ ؛ اعلم أنّ العذر المبيح للتيمم قد يكو من جهة الله ل كالمرض والبرد وخوف العطش ونحوها ، وحينئذ يجوز له التيمم، واع الإعادة عند القدرة على الماء. وقد يكون من جهة العبادِ كأسير في أيدي الكفَّارِ يمنعونه عن الوضوء، وكالمحبوس في السجن لا يجد ماء، وكالذي قيل له : إن توضأت قتلتك ونحو ذلك ، ففي هذه الصورة يجوز له التيمم وأداء الصلاة به في الحال، لكن تجب عليه الإعادة بعد زوال ذلك المانع.
And it is necessary to know that the prevention from ablution, if it is from the side of the servants, like a captive whom the disbelievers prevent from ablution, or an imprisoned person in prison, and one who was told: if you perform ablution, I will kill you, tayammum is permissible for him, but when the prevention ceases, he ought to repeat the prayer. Thus in 'al-Dhakhira'. And the truth is that the reference is only to the beginning of his statement, so remember this and do not listen to the direction mentioned in 'Dhakhirat al-Uqba', for we have shown its falsehood in 'al-Si'ayah'. [1] His statement: 'And it is necessary to know...' etc.; know that the excuse permitting tayammum may be from the side of Allah, like illness, cold, fear of thirst, and the like, and then tayammum is permissible for him, and there is no repetition when able to find water. And it may be from the side of the servants, like a captive in the hands of the disbelievers who prevent him from ablution, and like an imprisoned person in prison who finds no water, and like one who was told: if you perform ablution I will kill you, and the like. In this case, tayammum is permissible for him and he may perform prayer with it immediately, but he must repeat (the prayer) after that prevention ceases.
Source pages p. 454

Commentary
This passage from Umdat al-Ri'ayah deals with the ruling of tayammum when the impediment to using water is caused by human beings (min jihah al-‘ibad). The author first states the general principle: if someone is prevented from performing wudu by others—such as a captive held by disbelievers, a prisoner, or someone threatened with death if they perform wudu—they may perform tayammum. However, when the impediment is removed, they must repeat the prayer (i‘adah). The author then refutes a contrary opinion found in Dhakhirat al-Uqba, asserting that their argument is false as shown in al-Si‘ayah. The commentary then distinguishes two categories of excuses that permit tayammum: (1) from Allah (min jihah Allah)—such as illness, severe cold, fear of thirst—in which case tayammum is valid and no repetition is required upon finding water; (2) from human beings (min jihah al-‘ibad)—such as those mentioned—where tayammum is valid for immediate prayer but repetition is obligatory after the impediment disappears. This distinction is crucial in Hanafi fiqh: the excuse from Allah lifts the obligation of using water entirely, while the excuse from humans only temporarily permits tayammum, and the prayer must be repeated once the human constraint ends.

Key Terms
المَانِع (al-mani‘): The prevention from using water for wudu. Here it is divided into prevention from Allah (illness, cold, fear of thirst) and prevention from human beings (captivity, imprisonment, threats).
الإعَادَة (al-i‘adah): The obligation to repeat the prayer after the human impediment is removed, because the original prayer was performed with tayammum which is a temporary allowance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Tayammum is invalid; he must delay prayer until he finds water.
B) Tayammum is valid and no repetition is required.
C) Tayammum is valid, but he must repeat the prayer when the impediment is removed.
D) Tayammum is valid only if he fears death.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, tayammum due to human constraint is valid for immediate prayer, but the prayer must be repeated when the constraint ends.

Wiping over Khuffs: Permissibility and Proof from the Sunnah
Commentary opening the chapter on wiping over khuffs, explaining permissibility, conditions for obligation, and the Sunnah proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping over khuffs, identify the conditions that make it obligatory, and explain why the proof is from the Sunnah rather than the Qur'an.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuffs is a permissible Sunnah-based substitute for washing feet, not a Qur'anic obligation.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah opens the chapter on wiping over khuffs. The commentator clarifies that the default ruling is permissibility — the wearer may wipe or wash normally. However, specific circumstances elevate wiping to an obligation. The evidence for this practice comes from the Sunnah (prophetic words, actions, and approvals), not from the Qur'anic verse on wudu. Understanding this ruling requires careful attention to the nuance between permissibility and obligation, and the hierarchy of evidence in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
The commentator uses the word 'jaza' (permissible). This indicates that wiping is not obligatory; the wearer may choose to remove the khuffs and wash the feet. The default is washing, and wiping is a concession (rukhsah).
The term 'jaza' is deliberately chosen to avoid implying obligation.
2
Recognize exceptions that make wiping obligatory
If there is a cause that would make washing harmful or cause loss, wiping becomes wajib. Examples: insufficient water for washing (only enough for wiping), fear of missing the prayer time, fear of missing standing at 'Arafah, etc.
These are cases where the concession becomes duty to avoid hardship.
3
Understand the preference for washing
Even though wiping is valid, washing the feet (after removing khuffs) is considered superior (afdal) because it is more difficult and avoids the area of scholarly disagreement.
This shows that the ruling is not absolute; preference is given to the original act.
4
Analyze the evidence: Sunnah vs. Qur'an
The commentator says 'bi al-sunnah' to refute those who claim the proof is from the Qur'anic verse with the jar reading ('wa-arjulikum' to the ankles). Wiping is not limited to the ankles by consensus; thus the verse does not prove wiping. The practice is established by multiple forms of Sunnah.
The refutation targets a specific qira'a used by some to argue for wiping.
5
Differentiate 'Sunnah' from 'hadith'
The commentator prefers 'sunnah' because it encompasses the Prophet's words, actions, and tacit approvals, while 'hadith' often refers only to speech. This emphasizes the breadth of evidence.
Sunnah is a broader category, strengthening the proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب المسح على الخفين جاز بالسنة [1]. قوله: باب؛ أي هذا باب في أحكام مسح الخفين، وإنما ذكره عقيب التيمم لتناسبهما في كون كل منهما خلفاً، وبدلاً ، ومؤقتاً، ومقيداً بشرائط إلى غير ذلك من وجوه التناسب، كما بسطناها في «السعاية» (١) ، ولما كان ثبوت التيمم بالقرآن، وثبوت المسح بالسنة ناسب تقديم التيمم. [١]قوله : جاز؛ عبر بالجواز إشارة إلى أنّ المسح على الخفين غير واجب ؛ فإنّ للا بسهما أن ينزعهما ويغسل رجليهما، نعم لو غسل بدون نزعهما أثم ، وإن أجزاء الغُسل صرَّح به في «الدرر شرح الغُرر»(۳). وهذا إذا لم يوجد مقتض للوجوب، وإلا فيجب كمن ليس معه من الماء إلا ما يكفي المسح ، أو خافَ فوت وقت، أو وقوف عرفة، أو نحو ذلك إن اشتغل بالغُسل ، فحينئذ يجب عليه المسح ، صرح به في «البحر». وإلى أن الغسل أفضلُ من المسح ؛ لأنه أشقّ ، ولكونه أبعد عن مظنة الخلاف. [٢] قوله : بالسنّة ؛ فيه إشارة إلى الردّ على من قال بثبوته بقوله : وَأَرْجُلَكُمْ ﴾ (٤) بالجرّ ، فإنّ قوله : إلى الكعبين ما ينافيه، فإنّ المسح ليس محدوداً بهذا إجماعاً. واختار لفظ السنة على الحديث ؛ لأنَّ الحديث كثيراً ما يختص بقول الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم وأصحابه ، والسنة تعمّ القول والفعل والتقرير ، فأشار إلى أن ثبوتِ المسح بكل قسم من أقسام السنة.
Chapter on wiping over the khuffs: It is permissible by the Sunnah. [1] His statement: 'Chapter'; that is, this is a chapter concerning the rulings of wiping over the khuffs. He only mentioned it after tayammum because of their similarity in that each of them is a substitute, a replacement, time-bound, and restricted by conditions, among other aspects of similarity, as we have detailed in 'al-Si'ayah'. And since the establishment of tayammum is by the Qur'an, and the establishment of wiping is by the Sunnah, it was appropriate to place tayammum first. [1] His statement: 'Permissible'; he expressed permissibility to indicate that wiping over the khuffs is not obligatory; indeed, the wearer may remove them and wash his feet. However, if he washes without removing them, he sins, although the washing is valid. This is stated in 'al-Durar Sharh al-Ghurar'. This is when there is no requirement for obligation; otherwise, it becomes obligatory, such as one who has only enough water for wiping, or fears missing the time, or standing at 'Arafah, or the like if he engages in washing, then he must wipe. This is stated in 'al-Bahr'. And it indicates that washing is better than wiping because it is more difficult and because it is farther from the suspicion of disagreement. [2] His statement: 'By the Sunnah'; in it is a refutation of those who say it is established by His statement (interpretation of the meaning) 'and your feet' with a kasrah (in the recitation), for His statement 'to the ankles' contradicts it, because wiping is not limited by that according to consensus. And he chose the term Sunnah over hadith because hadith is often specific to the speech of the Messenger ﷺ and his Companions, while Sunnah includes speech, action, and tacit approval, so he indicated that the establishment of wiping is by every category of Sunnah.
Source pages p. 455

Commentary
This passage from Umdat al-Ri'ayah opens the chapter on wiping over khuffs (mash 'ala al-khuffayn). The author first explains why this chapter is placed after tayammum: both are substitutes (khalaf/badal), time-bound (muwaqqat), and restricted by conditions. Also, tayammum is proven by the Qur'an, while wiping over khuffs is proven by the Sunnah, so tayammum is given priority. The word 'jaza' (permissible) is deliberately used to indicate that wiping is not obligatory (wajib); the wearer may choose to remove the khuffs and wash the feet normally. However, if he washes his feet without removing the khuffs, the washing is valid but he sins (according to some texts, because he is neglecting the Sunnah). Washing is considered superior (afdal) to wiping because it is more difficult and avoids the area of disagreement (mazinnat al-khilaf). But if there is a reason for obligation—such as insufficient water for washing, fear of missing the prayer time or standing at 'Arafah—then wiping becomes obligatory. The phrase 'bi al-sunnah' refutes those who claim that the Qur'anic verse (al-Ma'idah 5:6) with the jar reading (wa-arjulikum) proves wiping. The author argues that the phrase 'ila al-ka'bayn' (to the ankles) contradicts that, as wiping is not limited to the ankles by consensus. He also explains why the term 'sunnah' is preferred over 'hadith': hadith often refers to the Prophet's speech, whereas sunnah encompasses his words, actions, and tacit approvals, thus providing stronger evidence for the practice of wiping over khuffs.

Key Terms
الخُفّ (al-khuff): Leather socks that cover the feet and ankles, worn with tahaarah. Wiping over them is a substitute for washing the feet in wudu.
السُنَّة (al-sunnah): The prophetic practice, comprising sayings (qawl), actions (fi‘l), and tacit approvals (taqrīr), used as the primary evidence for wiping over khuffs.
الجواز (al-jawaz): Permissibility; a legal ruling indicating that an act is allowed without being obligatory or forbidden.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does wiping over khuffs become obligatory (wajib)?
A) When water is available for both wiping and washing.
B) When one has only enough water for wiping and fears missing the prayer time.
C) When one is in a state of janabah.
D) When one is traveling more than 80 km.

Key Takeaway
Wiping over khuffs is a valid Sunnah-based dispensation; its default ruling is permissibility, not obligation, and it becomes obligatory only when washing is impractical.

Wiping Over Khuffs: Proof from the Mashhur Hadith
Commentary defending the ruling with mashhur hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping over khuffs and explain how the mashhur hadith justifies the addition to the Qur'anic command.

Core Idea
A mashhur hadith can add to the Qur'an's ruling; wiping over khuffs is for minor impurity only.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya defends the Hanafi ruling that wiping over khuffs is permissible only for those in minor impurity (muhdith), not for those requiring ghusl. The commentator addresses the apparent conflict with the Qur'an's command to wash the feet, explaining that a widely transmitted (mashhur) hadith can add to the Qur'an. Let's explore the reasoning and the proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Matn Ruling
Read the ruling: wiping over khuffs is for the muhdith, not for the one upon whom ghusl is obligatory. Understand what is being claimed.
The matn is the first line of the arabic.
2
Understand the Objection
The Qur'an (5:6) commands washing the feet. How can wiping be allowed? This is the key objection the commentator addresses.
The objection arises from the apparent contradiction between Qur'an and hadith.
3
Define the Mashhur Hadith
Learn the definition of al-sunnah al-mashhurah: a hadith that starts as ahad in the first generation but becomes widely transmitted later, making collusion on falsehood impossible.
This category is stronger than mere ahad but less than mutawatir.
4
See How it Adds to the Qur'an
The commentator explains that addition to the Qur'an (ziyadah 'ala al-kitab) is permitted by a mashhur or mutawatir hadith, even though a mere ahad hadith cannot. The hadith of Safwan provides this addition.
The principle is established in usul al-fiqh.
5
Apply the Exception
The hadith says 'except due to janabah'. Hence, those in major impurity (junub, ha'id, nufasa') cannot wipe; they must wash their feet.
The exception is clear and binding.

(٢) قوله : قيل : صورته ؛ إنما احتيج فيه إلى التصوير ؛ لاستبعاد تحقق المسح في حالة الغُسلِ ، فإنّ المغتسل إن صب من رأسه الماءِ ووصل ذلك إلى رجليه، وقد ذكروا هاهنا صوراً منها ما في «العناية» (۲) و«الكفاية» (۳) وغيرهما : أنه إذا توضأ ولبس خفيه أجنب ليس له أن يشدّ خُفِّيه فوق الكعبين ، ثم يغتسل ويمسح ، أو يغتسل قاعداً واضعاً رجليه على شيء مرتفع ثم يمسح. ومنها : أن المسافر إذا توضأ ولبس خفيه ثم أجنب وعنده ماء يكفي للوضوء، فإنه يتوضأ ويغسل رجليه ولا يمسح ؛ لأنَّ الجنابة حلت القدم. ومنها : ما ذكره الشارحُ ومعناه حمل دونَ مَن عليه الغُسل على معنى الاستثناء، فصار الحاصل أن المسح جائز للمحدثِ الذي ليس عليه غسل، وأما المحدث الذي عليه الغُسل فلا يجوز له المسح ، ولا يخفى ما فيه من التكلّف، وليطلب تفصيلُ هذا البحثِ من «السعاية»
Wiping over the khuffs: For the one with minor impurity, not for the one upon whom ghusl is obligatory. That is, by the well-known sunnah. By it, addition to the Book is permitted, because its requirement is washing the feet for the one with minor impurity, not for the one upon whom ghusl is obligatory. [1] His statement: 'by the well-known sunnah' – it is that which has individual origin: that is, it is narrated in the era of the Companions by a number not reaching the level of tawatur, then it is transmitted by the people of the second era and beyond by a group whose agreement upon falsehood is customarily impossible. If it is like that in the first era as well, then it is mutawatir. If the number of tawatur is not reached in a given era, then it is khabar al-wahid. The narrations of the hadith of wiping over the khuffs have reached a level of abundance, such that al-Suyuti counted it among the mutawatir hadiths in his treatise 'al-Azhar al-Mutanathira', and al-Ayni mentioned in 'al-Binaya' and 'Sharh Sharh Ma'ani al-Athar' that it was narrated by more than fifty Companions, and its narrators have remained many in every era. We have expanded all that in 'al-Si'aya'. [2] His statement: 'it is permitted' – he indicated by it to repelling the objection that the Qur'an rules the obligatory nature of washing the feet in wudu absolutely, so how is addition to it by hadith permitted? Its summary is that addition to the Book and abrogation of its absoluteness is not permitted by ahad hadiths, but by the well-known hadith, and also mutawatir, it is permitted as established in books of usul. [3] His statement: 'so that' etc. – the fa is not for causation, but to explain what is necessitated by the text, and it is possible that it is for causation of what is understood from the word 'addition'. [4] His statement: 'not for the one upon whom' – upon him is ghusl, meaning the menstruating woman, the woman in postpartum bleeding, and the one in a state of major impurity (junub). Based on the hadith of Safwan: 'The Messenger of Allah ﷺ used to order us, when we were traveling, not to remove our khuffs for three days and their nights except due to janabah.' It was said: its scenario: a junub did tayammum, then had minor impurity, and with him was enough water for wudu, so he performed wudu and put on his khuffs, then came upon water sufficient for ghusl, but he did not perform ghusl, then he found water for wudu, so he performed tayammum a second time for janabah. This was narrated by al-Tirmidhi, al-Nasa'i, Ibn Majah, and others. The point is that janabah does not customarily repeat, so there is no hardship in removing (the khuffs), unlike minor impurity, which repeats, so wiping was legislated for it in order to remove hardship. [1] His statement: 'upon him is ghusl' – it would have been better to say 'not for the one performing ghusl' to include the ghusl of Friday, the two Eids, and the like which are not obligatory, because wiping is not legislated in any ghusl at all. (2) His statement: 'its scenario was said' – the need for depiction here is due to the improbability of actually wiping while in a state of ghusl, because if the one performing ghusl pours water from his head and it reaches his feet... They have mentioned scenarios here, including what is in 'al-Inayah' and 'al-Kifayah' and others: that if he performed wudu and put on his khuffs and then became junub, he must not tighten his khuffs above the ankles, then perform ghusl and wipe, or perform ghusl while sitting with his feet on something elevated then wipe. Among them: that a traveler, if he performed wudu and put on his khuffs and then became junub, and he has enough water for wudu, then he performs wudu and washes his feet and does not wipe, because janabah encompassed the foot. Among them: that which the commentator mentioned, and its meaning is to interpret 'others than the one upon whom ghusl is obligatory' in the sense of exception, so the outcome is that wiping is permissible for the one in minor impurity who does not have ghusl upon him, but as for the one in minor impurity who has ghusl upon him, wiping is not permissible for him. The affectation in this is not hidden, and the detail of this discussion should be sought from 'al-Si'aya'.
Source pages p. 456

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya on the matn of Al-Wiqaya regarding the ruling of wiping over khuffs (leather socks) in wudu. The matn states: 'Wiping over the khuffs is for the one with minor impurity (muhdith), not for the one upon whom ghusl is obligatory (man wajaba 'alayhi al-ghusl).' The commentator first clarifies that the proof for this ruling is the 'well-known sunnah' (al-sunnah al-mashhurah). He then defines the mashhur hadith: it is a hadith that starts as khabar al-wahid (narrated by a limited number in the first generation) but later becomes widely transmitted such that it is impossible for the narrators to have agreed upon a lie. This is distinct from mutawatir, which is abundantly narrated from the first generation itself. The mashhur hadith is authoritative enough to add to the Qur'anic ruling, whereas a mere ahad hadith cannot. He cites al-Suyuti and al-'Ayni to show that the hadith on wiping over khuffs is narrated by over fifty Companions and is considered mutawatir (or at least mashhur). The commentator then addresses a potential objection: the Qur'an commands washing the feet in wudu (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:6), so how can wiping be allowed? He explains that addition to the Qur'an is permitted through a mashhur or mutawatir hadith, as established in usul al-fiqh. The word 'fa' in the matn ('fayajuz' = 'so it is permitted') indicates the conclusion of this argument. Next, the commentator explains the exception 'dun man wajaba 'alayhi al-ghusl' (not for the one upon whom ghusl is obligatory). This refers to women in menstruation and postpartum bleeding, and to men in a state of major ritual impurity (janabah). He narrates the hadith of Safwan that the Prophet ﷺ allowed wiping for three days and nights in travel except in case of janabah. The commentator then discusses a hypothetical scenario to illustrate that wiping is not valid for those who require ghusl. The scenario: a person in janabah performs tayammum, then has minor impurity, performs wudu with available water, puts on khuffs, then finds enough water for ghusl but does not perform it, then later finds only water for wudu and performs tayammum again for janabah. This scenario is narrated in hadith collections. The reason for the ruling is that janabah does not occur frequently, so there is no hardship in removing the khuffs for ghusl, whereas minor impurity occurs repeatedly, so wiping is legislated to remove hardship. The commentator also notes that the matn's phrase 'man wajaba 'alayhi al-ghusl' would be better expressed as 'dun al-mughtasil' (not for the one performing ghusl) to include non-obligatory ghusls like that of Friday and Eids, for which wiping is also not permissible. The commentator adds that several scenarios have been mentioned in other works about cases where wiping might be attempted during ghusl, but all confirm that wiping is not valid for anyone in a state of major impurity.

Key Terms
السنة المشهورة (al-sunnah al-mashhurah): A hadith that starts as ahad (individual) in the first generation but then becomes widely transmitted in subsequent generations to the point where it is impossible for the narrators to have agreed on a lie.
الخبر المشهور (al-khabar al-mashhur): Synonymous with al-sunnah al-mashhurah; a hadith widely transmitted but not reaching mutawatir in the first generation.
الزيادة على الكتاب (al-ziyadah 'ala al-kitab): Adding a ruling beyond what is stated in the Qur'an, such as allowing wiping over khuffs despite the Qur'an commanding washing the feet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, for whom is wiping over khuffs NOT permissible?
A) Someone with minor impurity (muhdith)
B) Someone who has worn khuffs in a state of wudu
C) Someone who requires ghusl (junub, ha'id, nufasa')
D) Someone who is traveling

Key Takeaway
Wiping over khuffs is a valid substitution for washing feet only when one has minor impurity; those requiring ghusl must wash their feet, established by the mashhur hadith of Safwan.

Wiping Over Khuffs: Exception for Janabah and Sunna Method
Commentary on the exception of janabah from wiping and the sunna method

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping over khuffs for a person in janabah and identify the sunna method of wiping including the dispute about the toes.

Core Idea
For janabah, khuffs must be removed; wiping is not allowed. Sunna: spread fingers from toes to shin.

This lesson clarifies a common confusion: can one wipe over khuffs while in a state of janabah? The text clearly states that wiping is not permitted forjanabah, even if the khuffs were put on after complete purity. It also details the sunna method of wiping, including the recommended spreading of fingers and the debated inclusion of the toes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling exception
Locate the statement that wiping over khuffs is not permissible for one upon whom ghusl is obligatory (janabah and any ghusl).
The commentator prefers 'except the one required to perform ghusl' to cover all types of ghusl.
2
Understand the scenario when wiping is invalid
Follow the hypothetical scenario: a junub person who performed tayammum, later had water for wudu but not for ghusl, then later found water for ghusl. The key point: when ghusl becomes obligatory, the hadath settles on the foot, so wiping is not enough.
3
Recognize the sunna method
Note the description: wiping with spread fingers, making lines, starting from the toes and extending to the shin. Understand what is obligatory vs sunna.
The obligatory minimum is the length of the tie of the shoelace (joint in middle of foot).
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute on toes
The text mentions a difference: most matns imply the toes are part of the wiped area, but fatwas (especially al-Khaniya) exclude them. The mufta bihi is that toes are not included.
This affects the validity if one wipes only the toes without the top of the foot.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : عليه الغسل؛ الأولى أن يقول: دون المغتسل؛ ليشمل غسل الجمعة والعيدين ونحوه مما ليس بفرض؛ فإن المسح غير مشروع في الغسل مطلقاً. قيل: صورته: جنب تيمم، ثم أحدث، ومعه من الماء ما يتوضأ، فتوضأ به ولبس خفيه، ثم مر على ماء يكفي للاغتسال، ولم يغتسل، ثم وجد من الماء ما يتوضأ به، فتيمم ثانياً للجنابة، فإن أحدث بعد ذلك توضأ ونزع خفيه غسل رجليه؛ لأن الجنابة حلت الرجل بمروره على الماء. وهذا تصوير لقول المصنف «دون من عليه الغسل»، إلا أن يقال: معنى قوله: «دون من عليه الغسل»، دون من عليه غسل الرجلين، ولا تخفى سخافته بل بطلانه. والأوضح أن يقال: إذا لبس الخف على طهارة كاملة ثم أجنب وتيمم للجنابة، ثم أحدث فوجد ما يكفي للوضوء، فعليه أن ينزع الخفين ويتوضأ، ولا يجوز له المسح؛ لأنه حين وجب عليه الغسل حل الحدث بالرجل فلا بد من دفع ذلك بالغسل.  وقوله: خطوطاً بأصابع مفرجة، يبدأ من أصابع الرجل إلى الساق. هذا صفة المسح على الوجه المسنون، فلو لم يفرج الأصابع لكن مسح مقدار الواجب جاز، وإن مسح بأصبع واحدة، ثم بلها ومسح ثانياً، ثم هكذا جاز أيضاً إن مسح كل مرة غير ما مسح قبل ذلك، وإن مسح بالإبهام والمسبحة منفرجتين، جاز أيضا؛ لأن ما بينهما مقدار أصبع أخرى. قوله: خطوطاً؛ تمييز من فاعل جاز، ويحتمل أن يكون حالاً منه. قوله: يبدأ؛ بصيغة المعروف؛ وضميره إلى المحدث أو الماسح، أو بصيغة المجهول المؤنث، والضمير إلى الخطوط، وهذه جملة مستأنفة بياناً لكيفية المسح والخطوط. قوله: من أصابع الرجل؛ ظاهره أن الأصابع لها دخل في محل المسح، حتى لو مسح عليه إن حصل قدر الفرض صح، وهو مفاد أكثر المتون، وظاهر الفتاوى أنه لا يجوز؛ فإنهم قالوا: تفسير المسح أن يمسح على ظهر قدميه ما بين أطراف الأصابع، فهذا يفيد أن الأصابع غير داخلة في المحلية، وبه صرح في الخانية. كذا في البحر. قوله: إلى الساق؛ هذا حد المسح المسنون، وأما محل الفرض فحده معقد الشراك، وهو المفصل الذي في وسط القدم.
His saying: 'upon him is ghusl' - the better expression would be 'except the one required to perform ghusl' to include Friday ghusl, two Eid ghusl, and similar optional ones, for wiping is not legislated in any ghusl. It was said: its scenario: a junub person performed tayammum, then had a minor hadath, and with him was enough water for wudu, so he performed wudu and wore his khuffs, then passed by water sufficient for ghusl but did not perform ghusl, then found water for wudu and performed tayammum a second time for janabah; then if he had a hadath after that, he performed wudu and removed his khuffs and washed his feet, because janabah had settled on the foot by his passing over water. This is a depiction of the author's saying 'except the one upon whom ghusl is obligatory' unless it is said: the meaning of his saying 'except the one upon whom ghusl is obligatory' is except the one upon whom ghusl of the feet is obligatory, and its absurdity, rather its falsehood, is not hidden. The clearest is to say: if he wore khuffs upon complete purity, then became junub and performed tayammum for janabah, then had a hadath and found enough water for wudu, he must remove the khuffs and perform wudu, and wiping is not permissible for him, because when ghusl became obligatory, the hadath settled on the foot, so it is necessary to remove that by ghusl. And his saying: 'lines with spread fingers, starting from the toes of the foot to the shin' - this is the description of wiping in the sunna manner. If he did not spread the fingers but wiped the obligatory amount, it is permissible. If he wiped with one finger, then wet it and wiped a second time, then similarly, it is also permissible provided that each time he wipes a different area than before. If he wiped with the thumb and index finger spread apart, it is also permissible because what is between them is the measure of another finger. His saying: 'lines' - it is a tamyiz from the subject of 'it is permissible', and it could be a hal from it. His saying: 'he begins' - in the active voice, its pronoun refers to the one having hadath or the wiper, or in the passive feminine voice, and the pronoun refers to the lines, and this is an independent clause explaining the manner of wiping and the lines. His saying: 'from the toes of the foot' - its apparent meaning is that the toes have an effect on the place of wiping, such that if he wiped over them and achieved the obligatory measure, it is valid, and this is the purport of most matns, but the apparent ruling of fatwas is that it is not permissible, for they said: the interpretation of wiping is that he wipes on the top of his feet between the tips of the toes, and this indicates that the toes are not included in the place of wiping, and this is stated explicitly in al-Khaniya. Thus in al-Bahr. His saying: 'to the shin' - this is the limit of the sunna wiping; as for the place of the obligatory wiping, its limit is the tie of the shoelace, which is the joint in the middle of the foot.
Source pages p. 457

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling of wiping over khuffs, specifically addressing the exception of janabah (major impurity) and describing the sunna method of wiping. The commentator begins by correcting the author's phrasing from 'upon him is ghusl' to 'except the one required to perform ghusl' to include all types of ghusl, even those that are not obligatory (like Friday or Eid). Then a scenario is presented to illustrate the case: a junub person who performed tayammum, then a minor hadath, then wiped and wore khuffs, later found water adequate for ghusl but did not perform ghusl, then again found water for wudu and performed tayammum. After that, when he experiences a hadath, he must remove the khuffs and perform wudu because janabah had settled on the foot. The commentator critiques some interpretations and gives the clearest ruling: if one becomes junub while wearing khuffs after having a complete wudu, and then performs tayammum for janabah, then has a minor hadath and finds enough water for wudu, he must remove the khuffs and perform wudu; wiping is not allowed because the hadath settled on the foot when ghusl became obligatory. The passage then describes the sunna method of wiping: forming lines with spread fingers, starting from the toes to the shin. It discusses the permissibility of wiping with less than full spread, with one finger repeatedly, or with two fingers apart. The commentator also notes that the toes' inclusion in the wiping area is disputed: most matns seem to include them, but fatwas exclude them, stating that wiping is on the top of the foot between the tips of the toes, so the toes themselves are not part of the wiped area. The obligatory limit is the tie of the shoelace (the joint in the middle of the foot).

Key Terms
خف (khuff): A leather sock that covers the foot up to the ankle, over which wiping is permitted in lieu of washing the feet during wudu.
مسح (mash): Wiping the foot over the khuff, rather than washing it directly.
جنابة (janabah): The state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl, such as after sexual intercourse or wet dream.
خطوط (khutut): Lines or marks left by the fingers during the sunna method of wiping, indicating that the fingers should move in a sweeping motion.
أصابع مفرجة (asabi' mufarrajah): Fingers spread apart, not held together, while wiping.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person is in a state of janabah and is wearing khuffs that were put on after wudu, what must he do?
A) He may wipe over them and perform ghusl without removing them.
B) He must remove the khuffs and wash his feet during ghusl.
C) He may keep the khuffs on and simply perform tayammum.
D) He must only wash the feet and may keep the khuffs on if he has water.

Key Takeaway
Janabah invalidates the permissibility of wiping over khuffs; the sunna method involves spread fingers from toes (excluding toes) to shin.

Sunnah Method and Obligatory Measure of Wiping over Khuffs
Describes the sunnah method and validity conditions of mas-h over khuffs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the sunnah method and obligatory measure of wiping over khuffs, and distinguish between the fard and sunnah components.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuffs has a fard minimum of three fingers from the hand, but the described method is sunnah.

This lesson unpacks the rulings on mas-h over khuffs from the commentary of al-Wiqayah. You will learn the sunnah method (starting from the toes with separated fingers) and the obligatory measure (three fingers of the hand per foot). We also address an intra-Hanafi dispute over whether the toes are part of the wiping area and the important condition that the water used must not become 'used water' in the process.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two aspects of the ruling
First, notice that the passage distinguishes between the sunnah manner (separated fingers, starting from toes to shin) and the obligatory amount (three fingers of the hand). The fard is only the minimum coverage; the rest is recommended.
2
Understand the sunnah method
The sunnah method is to wipe with separated fingers, beginning from the toes and drawing up to the shin. Several variations are mentioned: wiping with one finger multiple times (covering different areas), or using thumb and index finger (the gap counts as a finger). These are all valid because they achieve the sunnah.
The key is that the fingers are separated; the exact number of passes is flexible.
3
Determine the obligatory measure
The obligatory (fard) wiping must cover an area equal to three fingers of the hand on each foot. This measure is taken from the hand (not the foot), as stated by the majority of Hanafi texts. Al-Karkhi's view (from the foot) is rejected. The measure applies individually per foot.
If one foot gets less than three fingers, or if the amounts differ between feet, the wiping is invalid.
4
Analyze the dispute about the toes
The literal phrase 'from the toes' might suggest the toes are part of the wiping area. However, the relied-upon fatwa holds that the toes are not included; the wiping is on the top of the foot between the ends of the toes. This is based on the interpretation that 'from the toes' indicates the starting point, not the place.
The practical effect: wiping only the toes without the top of the foot is invalid according to the mufta bihi view.
5
Recognize the condition about wetness reuse
When wiping multiple times, if the water on the hand becomes 'used water' (musta'malah) and is not dripping, it cannot be used again for the fard wiping – that would invalidate the fard. However, for the sunnah portion, using such water is permitted as a subordinate.
This distinction shows that fard and sunnah have different standards for what is acceptable.

Lines with separated fingers, starting from the toes of the foot to the shin. [1] For janabah, then if he had a minor hadath after that, he should perform wudu and remove his khuffs and wash his feet, because janabah dissolved the foot by its passage over water. [4] (Lines (3) with separated fingers, starting (3) from the toes of the foot to the shin): This is the description of wiping in the sunnah manner. So if he did not separate the fingers but wiped the obligatory amount, it is permissible. And if he wiped with one finger, then moistened it and wiped a second time, then likewise, it is also permissible if each time he wiped an area different from what he wiped before. And if he wiped with the thumb and index finger separated, it is also permissible, because what is between them is the measure of another finger. [1] His statement: 'and remove his khuffs': there is in it that when he performed tayammum for janabah a second time, he is no longer bound by ghusl, so how is this correct? This is an explanation of the author's statement 'except one under obligation of ghusl'. It could be said: the meaning of 'except one under obligation of ghusl' is except one under obligation of washing the feet; its absurdity—nay, its falsehood—is not hidden, especially since this explanation involves excessive lengthening. The clearer way is to say: If he put on khuffs with complete purity, then became junub and performed tayammum for janabah, then had a minor hadath and found enough water for wudu, he must remove the khuffs and perform wudu, and it is not permissible for him to wipe, because when ghusl became obligatory, the hadath was attached to the foot, so it must be removed by washing. [2] His statement: 'lines' is a tamyiz from the agent of 'is permissible', and it could be a hal from it. [3] His statement: 'starts' in the active voice; its pronoun refers to the one in hadath or the wiper, or in the feminine passive voice, and the pronoun refers to the lines. This is an independent sentence explaining the manner of wiping and the lines. [4] His statement: 'from the toes of the foot': apparently, the toes are included in the place of wiping, so if he wiped and the obligatory amount was achieved, it is valid; this is the purport of most texts, but the apparent [view] of the fatwas is that it is not permissible, for they said: The interpretation of wiping is that he wipes over the top of his feet between the ends of the toes. This indicates that the toes are not included in the place [of wiping], and this is explicitly stated in al-Khaniyah (1). Likewise in al-Bahr. [0] His statement: 'to the shin': this is the limit of the sunnah wiping; as for the place of the obligatory wiping, its limit is the ankle joint, which is the joint in the middle of the foot. (2) [6] His statement: 'in the sunnah manner': Indeed, al-Mughirah ibn Shu'bah said: 'I saw the Messenger of Allah' and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) was asked about the description of wiping, and he said: 'He should place his fingers on the front of his khuffs, separate his palms, and extend them to the shin, or he should place his palms with the fingers and extend them all together (1) [2] But if he wipes with the tips of his fingers and separates the bases of the fingers and the palm, it is not permissible, unless the [required] wetness from the khuff at the placement is the measure of the obligatory amount, which is the measure of ... then he came and performed wudu and wiped over his khuffs, placing his right hand on his right khuff and his left hand on his left khuff, then wiping to the top of them in one wipe, until I saw the fingers of the Messenger of Allah on the khuffs (2) narrated by Ibn Abi Shaybah. [1] His statement: 'it is not permissible' because the wetness becomes used water upon first contact; so if it is not dripping, the wetness used first becomes used water a second time in the obligatory act, unlike if it is dripping, because then the wetness used in the second wipe is not the same as that used first. And unlike performing the sunnah when he places his fingers then extends them and the water is not dripping, because nafl [optional acts] allow what fard [obligatory acts] do not allow, and it is subordinate to it, so it is performed with water that was used in it as a default due to the necessity that repetition is not legislated; indeed, the occurrence of the action of the Prophet (peace be upon him) in this manner is sufficient for permissibility, and fard is not analogized to it because it is stronger. This is from Ghunyat al-Mustamli Sharh Munyat al-Musalli (3). [2] His statement: 'the measure of three fingers' means from the fingers of the hand; al-Karkhi said: from the toes; the first is more correct considering the instrument of wiping. In al-Hidayah it says: 'This measure is considered for each foot, such that if he wipes on one of his feet the measure of two fingers and on the other the measure of five fingers, it is not valid.' Likewise in Durar Sharh al-Ghurar. (4)
Source pages p. 458

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah is a commentary on the matn of al-Wiqayah regarding the method of wiping over khuffs. It begins by describing the sunnah method: wiping with separated fingers, starting from the toes up to the shin. If one does not separate the fingers but wipes the obligatory amount (which is three fingers), it is valid. Wiping with one finger multiple times on different areas is also valid, as is wiping with the thumb and index finger separated since the gap between them equals another finger. The author then explains a scenario where a person who performed tayammum for janabah and then had a minor hadath must remove the khuffs and wash his feet for wudu; he cannot wipe because the janabah required washing the feet with water, and the later hadath does not change that. The grammatical notes clarify that 'khututan' (lines) is a tamyiz, and 'yabda' (starts) can be read actively or passively. The text then addresses a dispute: apparently the toes are part of the wiping area, but according to reliable fatwas, the wiping is on the top of the foot between the toes, so the toes themselves are not included. This is confirmed by the Khaniyah. The sunnah wiping reaches the shin, while the obligatory limit is the ankle joint. The hadith of al-Mughirah ibn Shu'bah is cited to show two permissible sunnah methods: placing the fingertips on the front and drawing them to the shin, or placing the whole palm and fingers together. A critical issue arises: if one wipes only with the fingertips and separates the palm, it is invalid unless the water on the khuff at the initial placement is enough to cover the obligatory area. The reason is that the first contact makes the water 'used water'; if it is not dripping, reusing it is invalid for fard, but for sunnah it is allowed as subordinate. Finally, the measure of three fingers is from the hand (not the foot), and it applies to each foot separately; wiping different amounts on each foot does not fulfill the obligation.

Key Terms
مسح على الخفين (mas-h 'ala al-khuffayn): Wiping over the leather socks (khuffs) with wet hands in place of washing the feet during wudu, under specific conditions.
البلّة المستعملة (al-bullah al-musta'malah): Water that has been used for a previous act of purity, which becomes legally impure and cannot be reused for obligatory acts.
مقدار ثلاث أصابع (miqdar thalath asabi'): The obligatory area of wiping over each khuff, measured as approximately the width of three fingers of the hand placed together.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The fard of mas-h over khuffs is to wet an area of three fingers of the hand on each foot; the sunnah method (separated fingers, starting from toes) is recommended but not obligatory.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate

Conditions for Wiping over Khuffs
Rulings with proof on wiping over khuffs — methods, water reuse, and area.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for valid wiping over khuffs and explain the ruling on using used water during the act.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuffs replaces washing feet; the key is avoiding used water — the minimum is three fingers.

Wiping over leather socks (khuffs) is a concession that substitutes washing the feet in ablution. However, it is governed by precise conditions regarding the method, the amount of water, and the area covered. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi rulings based on the prophetic practice and the need to avoid using water that has already become 'used' (musta'mal).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is wiping over khuffs (mash 'ala al-khuffayn) during wudu. Determine its hukm level: wajib when conditions are met. Note that it substitutes for washing the feet.
Hanafi: wajib; other schools differ on its obligation.
2
Examine the two permissible methods
Two methods are given: (1) placing fingers on the front of the khuff and extending to the leg, keeping palms separate; (2) placing palms together with fingers and extending as a whole. Identify the key difference.
Both are valid if water conditions are met.
3
Understand the problem of used water (bulla)
Moisture becomes musta'mal upon contact. If the water is not dripping, the used water is reused in the obligatory act, invalidating the wipe. If dripping, fresh water reaches the khuff, so it is valid. Contrast with sunnah acts where reuse is excused.
This is the central condition: the water must be fresh, not used.
4
Determine the required area
The minimum area is the size of three fingers from the hand (length and width). Al-Karkhi said from the foot, but the preferred view is from the hand. The amount must be uniformly applied on each foot.
Al-Hidayah: wiping less on one foot invalidates even if more on the other.
5
Reconcile apparent contradictions and note the sunnah method
Al-Muhit says wiping with fingertips is invalid unless the khuff gets wet at placement; al-Dhakhirah says it is valid if water drips. The two are not contradictory: either condition suffices. The sunnah method is to wipe with the inner palm and fingers, but using the back of the hand or varying direction is permissible.
The place (top of khuff) is essential; the manner is not.

وسُئِلَ محمد له عن صفة المسح ، قال : أن يضع أصابع يديه على مقدم خُفَّيه، ويُجافي كفِّيه، ويمدهما إلى السَّاق، أو يضع كفيه مع الأصابع ويمدهما جملة

ثلاث أصابع ، هكذا ذكر في «المحيط»).
وذكر في «الذخيرة : أنَّ المسح برؤوس الأصابع يجوز إذا كان الماء متقاطراً، فإنه إذا كان الماء متقاطراً، فالماء ينزل من أصابعه إلى رؤوسها ، فإذا مد كانه أخذ ماءً جديداً، ولو مسح بظهر الكف جاز ، لكن السنَّةَ بباطنها ، وكذا إن ابتدأ من طرف الساق ، ولو نسى المسح
قوله : ثلاث ...الخ ؛ أي طولاً وعرضاً ، فلو مسح بثلاث أصابع منصوبة غير موضوعة ولا ممدودة لا يجوز. كذا في «البحر»
قوله : وذكر في «الذخيرة» ؛ بصيغة المجهول أو بالمعروف، والضمير راجع إلى صاحب «المحيط»، وإنما نقل عبارة «المحيط» ؛ لأنّ في كل منهما بياناً لأمر ليس في الآخر، فإن عبارة «المحيط» تشهد بأن المسح برؤوس الأصابع لا يجوز إلا أن يبتل قدر الواجب، وعبارة «الذخيرة» تشهد بأنه يجوز إن كان الماء متقاطراً.
ومنهم من ظنَّ أن بينهما منافاة، والحق أنّه لا منافاة ؛ فإنّ الشرط لجواز المسح بالرؤوس أحد الأمرين : إما التقاطرُ وإما الابتلال عند الوضع ؛ لأنّ المدار على عدم المسح ببلة مستعملة، فذكر في «المحيط» أحدهما، والآخر في «الذخيرة».
قوله : لكن السنة بباطنها ؛ أي المسنون المتوارث هو المسح بباطن الكف والأصابع، ولو مسح على باطن خُفَّيه أو من قبل العقبين، أو جوانب الرجلين لا يجوز مسحه ؛ لأن الأخبار إنما وردت بالمسح على أعلاه، فلا يجوز ما سواه ؛ لأنه خلافُ المحل الذي ورد به النص. أما مخالفة الكيفية كالمسح بظاهر الكف أو الابتداء من جهة الساق إلى الأصابع، فلا تضرّ ؛ لأنّ الكيفية غير مقصودة بالذات، بخلاف المحلّ. كذا في «الغنية)
قوله : ولو نسى ... الخ ؛ قال في «المنية» و«الغُنية»: «لو توضأ ولم يمسح خُفّيه ولكن خاض في الماء لا بنية المسح ، ولم يغسل إحدى رجليه أو أكثرها، أو مشى في (يتبع)
Muhammad [al-Shaybani] was asked about the description of wiping. He said: He places his fingers on the front of his khuffs, keeps his palms separate, and extends them to the leg; or he places his palms together with the fingers and extends them as a whole. However, if he wipes with the tips of his fingers and separates the bases of the fingers and the palm, it is not permissible unless the khuff becomes wet at the time of placing to the extent of the obligatory [amount], which is the amount of three fingers. Then he came, performed ablution, and wiped over his khuffs: he placed his right hand on his right khuff and his left hand on his left khuff, then wiped to their tops in one wipe, until I saw the fingers of the Messenger of Allah on the khuffs. [Narrated by Ibn Abi Shaybah]. His statement: It is not permissible because the moisture becomes used water merely by contact. So if it is not dripping, the moisture used first becomes used a second time in the obligatory [act], unlike if it is dripping, for then the moisture used second is not the one used first. And unlike performing the sunnah when he places his fingers and then extends them and the water is not dripping, because supererogatory acts are excused what is not excused in obligatory acts, and it is subordinate to it; so he performs it with water used in it subordinately due to necessity, as repetition is not legislated. Moreover, the occurrence of the Prophet’s action (peace be upon him) in this manner is sufficient for permissibility, and the obligatory act is not analogized to it because it is stronger. This is in Ghunyat al-Mustamli Sharh Munyat al-Musalli. His statement: The amount of three fingers, i.e., from the fingers of the hand. Al-Karkhi said: from the fingers of the foot. The first is more correct, considering the instrument of wiping. Al-Hidayah states: “This amount is considered from each foot, such that if he wiped on one foot the amount of two fingers and on the other the amount of five fingers, it is not permissible.” This is in Durar Sharh al-Ghurrar. Three fingers, thus mentioned in al-Muhit. And it is mentioned in al-Dhakhirah that wiping with the tips of the fingers is permissible if the water is dripping, because if the water is dripping, water descends from his fingers to their tips, so when he extends it, it is as if he takes new water. And if he wipes with the back of the hand, it is permissible, but the sunnah is with its inner part. Similarly, if he begins from the end of the leg. And if he forgot the wiping... His statement: Three... etc., meaning length and width. So if he wipes with three upright fingers that are not placed nor extended, it is not permissible. This is in al-Bahr. His statement: And it is mentioned in al-Dhakhirah — in the passive or known voice, and the pronoun refers to the author of al-Muhit. He only transmitted the wording of al-Muhit because each contains a clarification of a matter not in the other. For the wording of al-Muhit testifies that wiping with the tips of the fingers is not permissible unless it wets to the extent of the obligatory, while the wording of al-Dhakhirah testifies that it is permissible if the water is dripping. Some thought there is contradiction between them, but the truth is there is no contradiction. The condition for the permissibility of wiping with the tips is one of two things: either dripping or wetting at the time of placing, because the criterion is not wiping with used water. So al-Muhit mentioned one, and al-Dhakhirah the other. His statement: But the sunnah is with its inner part, i.e., the transmitted sunnah is wiping with the inner part of the palm and fingers. If he wipes on the inside of his khuffs or from the direction of the heels, or the sides of the feet, his wiping is not permissible because the reports only came for wiping on the top; so what is other than that is not permissible, because it is contrary to the place mentioned in the text. As for violating the manner, like wiping with the back of the hand or starting from the leg towards the fingers, that is not harmful because the manner is not intended per se, unlike the place. This is in al-Ghunya. His statement: And if he forgot... etc. It is said in al-Munya and al-Ghunya: “If he performed ablution and did not wipe his khuffs but waded in water without the intention of wiping, and did not wash one of his feet or most of it, or walked in... (to be continued)
Source pages p. 459

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah deals with the rulings on wiping over khuffs (leather socks) during ablution. It begins by stating two permissible methods of wiping: either placing the fingers on the front of the khuff and extending to the leg while keeping the palms separate, or placing the palms together with the fingers and extending as a whole. Then it addresses a key issue: if one wipes only with the tips of the fingers without the inner parts, it is not valid unless the khuff becomes wet to the extent of the obligatory amount (three fingers) at the moment of placing. The reason is that the water on the hand becomes used (musta'mal) upon contact; if the water is not dripping, that used water is reused in the obligatory act, which is impermissible. However, if the water is dripping, fresh water reaches the khuff, so it is valid. The text then contrasts this with sunnah acts, where such reuse is excused because supererogatory acts are more lenient. A hadith from Ibn Abi Shaybah shows the Prophet's practice. The discussion also covers the required area: the minimum is three fingers—scholars differ whether these are fingers of the hand (the preferred view, considering the wiping instrument) or of the foot. It must be applied on each foot uniformly; wiping less on one foot invalidates it. The text reconciles a seeming contradiction between al-Muhit and al-Dhakhirah: wiping with fingertips requires either dripping or wetting at placement, and both conditions are valid. Additionally, it clarifies that the sunnah (preferred method) is to wipe with the inner palm and fingers, but wiping with the back of the hand is permissible though suboptimal. The place wiped must be the top of the khuff; wiping the inside, sides, or heels is invalid because the texts specify the top. However, varying the direction (e.g., starting from the leg) does not invalidate the act, as the manner is not essential. The passage ends with a discussion of forgetting to wipe and whether wading in water suffices (continuation on next page).

Key Terms
المسح على الخفين (al-mash 'ala al-khuffayn): Wiping over leather socks (khuffs) with wet hands as a substitute for washing the feet in ablution, under specific conditions.
البلّة (al-bulla): The moisture or water on the hand used for wiping.
مقدار ثلاث أصابع (miqdar thalath asabi'): The minimum area to be wiped: equivalent to three fingers (width and length).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum amount of the khuff that must be wiped according to the Hanafi school?
A) The entire front of the khuff
B) Three fingers from the fingers of the hand
C) The whole foot
D) The heel area

Key Takeaway
Wiping over khuffs is valid only when fresh water contacts the khuff over at least three hand-fingers on the top surface, and using used water invalidates the act.

Wiping Method: Three Fingers, Fingertips, and Sunnah Manner
Expansion of the matn on the method and conditions of wiping khuffs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligatory minimum area for wiping khuffs and identify when wiping with fingertips is valid according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Three fingers' area is wajib; manner affects sunnah, not validity.

Wiping over khuffs is a concession in wudu, but its method has precise requirements. The matn states that the obligatory wiping is with three fingers. The commentator expands on what this means—three fingers in length and width—and clarifies a seeming conflict between two Hanafi authorities about wiping with fingertips. Understanding these details ensures your wiping is valid according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its obligatory minimum
What is the wajib act in wiping khuffs? The matn says 'three fingers' – we need to determine whether this refers to length, width, or both.
2
Distinguish obligatory from sunnah
The text contrasts the obligatory minimum (three fingers) with the sunnah method (inner palm). Identify which aspects are non-negotiable and which are recommended.
3
Understand the controversy about fingertips
Al-Muhit and al-Dhakhira give different conditions for wiping with fingertips. Why do they seem to conflict? Identify the common principle that resolves the contradiction.
The key is avoiding used water (billa musta'mala).
4
Apply the resolution
Under what two conditions is wiping with fingertips valid? Use the commentator's synthesis to state both conditions.
5
Differentiate place vs manner
The text stresses that the place (top of khuff) is fixed by nass, while the manner (inner/back of hand, starting point) is flexible. Why does this distinction matter for validity?

Three fingers, thus it is mentioned in al-Muhit. And it is mentioned in al-Dhakhira: that wiping with the tips of the fingers is permissible if the water is dripping, because when water is dripping, water descends from his fingers to their tips, so when he draws (his hand), it is as if he took new water. And if he wipes with the back of the hand, it is permissible, but the sunnah is with its inner side, and likewise if he begins from the side of the leg. And if he wipes with three fingers raised, not placed nor stretched, it is not permissible. As in al-Bahr. His saying: and it is mentioned in al-Dhakhira: in the passive voice or with the known (form), and the pronoun refers to the author of al-Muhit. He only transmitted the expression of al-Muhit because in each of them there is an explanation of a matter not in the other. The expression of al-Muhit testifies that wiping with the tips of the fingers is not permissible unless the obligatory amount gets wet. And the expression of al-Dhakhira testifies that it is permissible if the water is dripping. Some thought there is contradiction between them, but the truth is there is no contradiction; the condition for permissibility of wiping with the tips is one of two things: either dripping or the moistening at the time of placing (the hand), because the criterion is not wiping with used water. So al-Muhit mentioned one, and al-Dhakhira the other. His saying: but the sunnah is with its inner side; meaning the transmitted sunnah is wiping with the inner side of the palm and fingers. And if he wipes on the inner side of his khuffs or from the heels or the sides of the feet, his wiping is not permissible because reports only mention wiping on the top, so what is other than that is not permissible because it is contrary to the place mentioned in the text. As for violating the manner, like wiping with the back of the hand or beginning from the leg side toward the toes, that does not harm because the manner is not intended in itself, unlike the place. As in al-Ghunya.
Source pages p. 460

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the matn's ruling on the method of wiping over khuffs. The matn states that the obligatory wiping is with three fingers. The commentator explains that this means three fingers in both length and width; if one wipes with three fingers raised but not placed on the khuff nor stretched, the wiping is not valid. There is a discussion between two Hanafi texts: al-Muhit says wiping with fingertips is not valid unless the obligatory amount becomes wet, while al-Dhakhira says it is valid if water drips onto them. The commentator resolves this apparent contradiction by stating that both conditions are acceptable—either dripping or wetting upon placement—because the key is to avoid using water that has already been used (for ablution). The sunnah method is to wipe with the inner palm and fingers, but if one uses the back of the hand or starts from the ankle, the wiping is still valid because the manner is not essential; rather, the essential element is the place—the top of the khuff. Wiping on the inner side, heels, or sides of the feet is invalid because the prophetic reports specify the top. Thus, the place is fixed by the text, but the manner is flexible.

Key Terms
ثلاث أصابع (thalaath asaabi'): The obligatory minimum area to wipe is the area of three fingers combined, length and width.
رؤوس الأصابع (ru'uus al-asaabi'): The tips of the fingers; wiping with them is valid if water drips or if they are wet from the khuff's moisture.
باطن الكف (baatin al-kaff): The inner side of the palm; the sunnah method is to wipe with the inner side of the hand.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The entire top of the khuff
B) An area equivalent to three fingers in length and width
C) Just the toes
D) The inner side of the khuff

Key Takeaway
Wiping over khuffs requires at least three fingers' area on the top; the manner is sunnah, not wajib, and the use of fingertips is conditional on avoiding used water.

Passive Wetting Suffices for Wiping Khuffs; Only Top Required
Expansion on the ruling that water on top of khuffs suffices as wiping, and refutation of wiping the bottom

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on what suffices for wiping khuffs when forgotten, and identify the correct place of wiping.

Core Idea
If water wets the top of your khuff without intention, your wiping is done – and wiping the bottom is not required.

This lesson examines two important details of masah ala al-khuffain: what counts as wiping when you forget, and where exactly you must wipe. The Hanafi school takes a lenient view on passive wetting, and strictly limits wiping to the top surface. Understanding these points will clarify common scenarios when wudu might be valid even without the intentional act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is wiping the khuff (masah ala al-khuffain). It is wajib in the Hanafi school, established by the Sunnah.
Wajib is a level just below fard; missing it requires compensation but does not invalidate wudu if forgotten.
2
Locate the scenario and its ruling
The passage discusses a person who forgets to wipe his khuffs during wudu but later wades in water, walks in rain, or walks in wet grass, causing the top of the khuffs to become wet. The ruling: this suffices as wiping, even without intention.
The same applies to wiping the head: if rain wets a quarter of the head, it suffices.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof is based on istihsan and the general practice of the Companions. The obligation is to have the top wet; intention is not a condition for the act to be valid when it occurs passively.
Contrast with Shafi'i, who require intention for every part of wudu.
4
Distinguish the Shafi'i opposition
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that intention is required for all acts of wudu, including wiping. Thus, passive wetting does not count. The practical difference (thamarah) is that a Hanafi need not repeat wiping if the top is wetted, while a Shafi'i must redo it with intent.
The Hanafi response is that intention is only required for the first part of wudu, not for subsequent acts that occur through external means.
5
Confirm the place of wiping
The matn specifies 'on the top of his khuffs' (ala zahir khuffayhi). This refutes those who also wipe the bottom. A hadith about wiping both top and bottom is weak (da'if) according to Abu Zur'ah, al-Bukhari, and Ahmad, so it is not used as evidence.
Thus, in the Hanafi school, wiping is restricted to the top only.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو نسى المسح على ظاهر خفيه قال في «المنية» و«الغُنية»: «لو توضأ ولم يمسح خُفّيه ولكن خاض في الماء لا بنية المسح ، ولم يغسل إحدى رجليه أو أكثرها، أو مشى في المطر وأصابَ المطر ظاهر خُفِّيهِ حصل المسح ، وكذا مسح الرأس، وكذا لو مشى في الحشيش فابتل ظاهر خفيه ولو بالطل) هو الصحيح». (على ظاهر خفيه) الحشيش المبتل بالماء المفاض عليه للسقي أو بالمطر، يجزئه الحصول المسح ضمناً، وعدم اشتراط النية فيه. وكذا إذا أصابه المطر ينوب ذلك عن المسح ، خلافاً للشافعي له في ذلك كله ; لأنّ النية عنده شرط في الوضوء، والمسح جزء منه. قوله : المطر...الخ ; التقييد به اتفاقي ; فإنّ الحكم في كلِّ ماء، مطراً كان أو ماءَ النهر أو غير ذلك واحد. قوله : وكذا ; أي لو ترك مسح الرأس فأصاب المطر رأسه وابتل مقدار الربع منه كفى ذلك. قوله : هو الصحيح ; إشارة إلى الخلاف في الصل) : بفتح الطاء المهملة، وتشديد اللام ، يقال له : شبنم ; فإنّ منهم من قال : لو كان مبتلا بالطَّلِّ وأصابَ الحُفْ لا يجوز; لأنّ الطِّلّ نفس دابة يجذبه الهواء، والصحيح أنه يجوز; لأنه ماء ضعيف. كذا قال الزيلعي في «شرح الكنز ) ، وليطلب تفصيلُ هذا البحث من «السعاية». قوله : على ظاهر خُفِّيه ; متعلّق بقوله : «جاز»، وبقوله: «خطوطاً»، على أنه حال منه، أو بقوله : «يبدأ»، وفيه إشارة إلى الردّ على من أوجب مسح باطنهما أيضاً أخذاً مما أخرجه الترمذي وابن ماجة وأبو داود وغيرهم عن المغيرة ه قال : «توضاً رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فمسح على الخف أعلاه وأسفله» (ه) ، وهو حديث ضعفه أبو زرعة والبخاري وأحمد وغيرهم من ال الحفاظ.
And if he forgot to wipe on the top of his khuffs, it is said in al-Munyah and al-Ghunya: 'If he performed wudu and did not wipe his khuffs but waded in water without intention of wiping, and did not wash one of his feet or most of them, or walked in rain and the rain hit the top of his khuffs, the wiping is achieved; likewise for wiping the head; and likewise if he walked in grass and the top of his khuffs became wet, even with dew, it is the correct (opinion).' (On the top of his khuffs) The grass that is wet with water poured on it for irrigation or with rain suffices for obtaining the wiping implicitly, and intention is not required therein. Likewise, if rain hits him, it serves as a substitute for wiping, contrary to al-Shafi'i regarding all of that, because intention according to him is a condition in wudu, and wiping is part of it. His saying: rain, etc.; the restriction is by agreement; indeed the ruling is the same for all water, whether rain or river water or other. His saying: likewise; i.e., if he left wiping his head and rain hit his head and wet a quarter of it, that suffices. His saying: it is the correct (opinion); an indication of the disagreement regarding dew: with fatha on the ط and tashdid on the ل, it is called shabnam. Some said: if it was wet with dew and it hit the khuff, it is not permissible because dew is a kind of insect (?) that the air draws. The correct view is that it is permissible because it is weak water. Thus said al-Zayla'i in Sharh al-Kanz, and the detail of this research should be sought from al-Si'ayah. His saying: on the top of his khuffs; it is connected to his saying 'it is permissible' and his saying 'lines' as a state from it, or to his saying 'he begins', and in it is an indication of refuting those who make wiping its inner side also obligatory, based on what al-Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah, Abu Dawud and others narrated from al-Mughirah who said: 'The Messenger of Allah performed wudu and wiped over the khuff, its top and its bottom.' This hadith is weak according to Abu Zur'ah, al-Bukhari, Ahmad and other hadith masters.
Source pages p. 460

Commentary
This passage discusses two interrelated issues: (1) what suffices for wiping when one forgets the specific act, and (2) that wiping is specifically on the top of the khuff only. The matn states that if a person performs wudu but forgets to wipe his khuffs, then walks in water, rain, or wet grass, and the top of the khuffs becomes wet, this counts as the required wiping, even without the intention of wiping. The same applies to the head: if one forgets to wipe the head and rain wets a quarter of it, it suffices. This ruling is contrary to Imam al-Shafi'i, for whom intention is a condition for every act of wudu, including wiping. The commentator emphasizes that it is not specific to rain; any water, from a river or otherwise, works. There is an internal Hanafi disagreement regarding dew: some say dew does not count because it is like a vapor, but the correct view (al-sahih) is that it does, because it is essentially weak water. Finally, the commentator addresses the issue of the place of wiping. The matn specifies 'on the top of his khuffs' (ala zahir khuffayhi). This phrase refutes those who claim that the bottom or sides must also be wiped, based on a hadith in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) supposedly wiped both the top and bottom. This hadith is declared weak by major hadith masters such as Abu Zur'ah, al-Bukhari, and Ahmad. Therefore, in the Hanafi school, only the top of the khuff is the place for wiping.

Key Terms
الطل (al-tall): Dew; considered weak water that suffices for wiping if it wets the top of the khuff.
النّية (al-niyyah): Intention; in this context, the Hanafi view is that intention is not required for the passive wetting to count as wiping.
ظاهر الخف (zaahir al-khuff): The top part of the khuff; the only place for wiping.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person forgets to wipe his khuffs but then walks in rain and the top of the khuffs gets wet, what is the ruling?
A) The wudu is invalid because the wiping was not done intentionally.
B) The wiping is achieved and the wudu is valid.
C) He must repeat wudu.
D) He must wipe again with intention as soon as he remembers.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, passive wetting of the top of the khuff suffices for wiping, and wiping is only on the top, not the bottom.

Indirect Wiping via Rain or Dew: Intention Not Required
Explains that rain or dew on top of khuff suffices for wiping without intention.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on indirect wiping via rain or dew, explain why intention is not required, and compare it to the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
Rain or dew on the khuff suffices for wiping without intention – the water itself performs the act.

Imagine walking in the rain: water hits the top of your leather socks (khuff). According to the Hanafi school, your wudu is complete without you ever intending to wipe. This ruling stems from the principle that the water itself, when it reaches the required area, fulfills the obligation of wiping. The Shafi'i school disagrees, requiring intention for every act of wudu. In this lesson, we unpack the evidence and the practical difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school rules regarding rain, dew, or any water wetting the top of the khuff. Note that intention is not required.
2
Identify the opposing school and its objection
Recognize the Shafi'i position: intention is a condition for every part of wudu, including wiping. Understand why they reject the Hanafi view.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
Understand the Hanafi argument: the water itself performs the wiping; intention is only needed at the start of the act, not for each component. Also note the additional point about dew being weak water.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Apply both views to a real scenario: walking in rain. Hanafi: wudu valid without intention. Shafi'i: must intend wiping, otherwise wudu is invalid and must be repeated.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute on dew
Some earlier Hanafis rejected dew because they deemed it not water. The correct Hanafi view (mufta bihi) holds that dew is weak water and suffices.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
