وأصابَ المطر ظاهر خُفَّيهِ حصل المسح ، وكذا مسح الرأس، وكذا لو مشى في الحشيش فابتل ظاهر خفيه ولو بالطل) هو الصحيح".
(على ظاهر خفيه)
الحشيش المبتل بالماء المفاض عليه للسقي أو بالمطر، يجزئه الحصول المسح ضمناً، وعدم اشتراط النية فيه. وكذا إذا أصابه المطر ينوب ذلك عن المسح ، خلافاً للشافعي له في ذلك كله ؛ لأنّ النية عنده شرط في الوضوء، والمسح جزء منه) [١]قوله : المطر...الخ ؛ التقييد به اتفاقي ؛ فإنّ الحكم في كلِّ ماء، مطراً كان أو ماءَ النهر أو غير ذلك واحد.
(٢) قوله : وكذا ؛ أي لو ترك مسح الرأس فأصاب المطر رأسه وابتل مقدار الربع منه كفى ذلك.
[٣] قوله : هو الصحيح ؛ إشارة إلى الخلاف في الصل) : بفتح الطاء المهملة، وتشديد اللام ، يقال له : شبنم ؛ فإنّ منهم من قال : لو كان مبتلا بالطَّلِّ وأصابَ الحُفْ لا يجوز؛ لأنّ الطِّلّ نفس دابة يجذبه الهواء، والصحيح أنه يجوز؛ لأنه ماء ضعيف. كذا قال الزيلعي في «شرح الكنز ) ، وليطلب تفصيلُ هذا البحث من «السعاية». [٤]قوله : على ظاهر خُفَّيه ؛ متعلّق بقوله : «جاز»، وبقوله: «خطوطاً»، على أنه حال منه، أو بقوله : «يبدأ»، وفيه إشارة إلى الردّ على من أوجب مسح باطنهما أيضاً أخذاً مما أخرجه الترمذي وابن ماجة وأبو داود وغيرهم عن المغيرة ه قال : «توضاً رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فمسح على الخف أعلاه وأسفله» (ه) ، وهو حديث ضعفه أبو زرعة والبخاري وأحمد وغيرهم من ال الحفاظ.
On the top of his two khuffs: If rain hits the top of his two khuffs, wiping is achieved, and similarly for wiping the head, and similarly if he walks in grass and the top of his khuffs becomes wet, even with dew (it is correct). On the top of his two khuffs: Grass wet with water poured on it for irrigation or rain suffices as wiping implicitly, and intention is not required. Similarly, if rain hits him, it substitutes for wiping, contrary to al-Shafi'i in all of this because intention in his view is a condition for wudu, and wiping is part of it. [1] His statement: 'rain... etc.'; the restriction is coincidental; the ruling for all water, whether rain or river water or otherwise, is the same. (2) His statement: 'and similarly'; i.e., if he left wiping his head and rain hit his head and wet a quarter of it, that suffices. [3] His statement: 'it is correct'; an indication of the disagreement regarding dew: with fatha on the ط and tashdid on the ل, called 'shabnam'. Among them there is one who said: if (the khuff) was wet with dew and it hit the khuff, it is not permissible because dew is a kind of insect that the air draws. The correct view is that it is permissible because it is weak water. Thus said al-Zayla'i in Sharh al-Kanz, and the detail of this research should be sought from al-Si'ayah. [4] His statement: 'on the top of his two khuffs' is related to his statement: 'it is permissible' and to his statement: 'lines' as a circumstantial accusative, or to his statement: 'he begins'; and it contains a refutation of those who made wiping the inside obligatory as well, taking from what al-Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah, Abu Dawud and others narrated from al-Mughirah: 'The Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, performed wudu and wiped over the top and bottom of the khuff.' This is a hadith that Abu Zur'ah, al-Bukhari, Ahmad and other hadith masters declared weak.
Source pages p. 461

Commentary
This passage deals with a ruling on mas'h 'ala al-khuffayn. The matn states 'on the top of his two khuffs', and the sharh elaborates that if rain wets the top of the khuff, it counts as wiping. Similarly, if one omits wiping the head and rain wets a quarter of the head, that suffices. The same applies if one walks on wet grass. This ruling applies to any water, not just rain. The key point is that intention is not required for this indirect wiping, because the water itself serves as the wiping. This is in contrast to Imam al-Shafi'i, who requires intention for all parts of wudu, including wiping. The commentary also discusses the case of dew (al-tall). Some scholars argued that dew does not suffice because it is not liquid water but rather a moisture drawn by air (like a small insect). The correct Hanafi position is that it does suffice because it is still water, albeit weak. The text then addresses the dispute over wiping both top and bottom of the khuff. Some narrations report that the Prophet wiped both top and bottom, but these are weak according to major hadith critics. The Hanafi school relies on the practice of the Companions, especially the statement of 'Ali: 'If religion were by opinion, the inside of the khuff would be more deserving than the outside, but I saw the Messenger of Allah wiping over the top of his khuffs, not the bottom.' Thus, wiping only the top is sufficient, and wiping inside alone does not fulfill the obligation.

Key Terms
الطل (al-tall): Dew: moisture that forms on surfaces, considered weak water in this context.
المسح على الخفين (al-mash 'ala al-khuffayn): Wiping over leather socks as a substitute for washing feet during ablution.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, does dew on the khuff count as valid wiping for wudu?
A) Yes, because dew is water, albeit weak.
B) No, because dew is not water.
C) Yes, but only if one intends to wipe.
D) No, because it is impure.

Key Takeaway
Rain or dew on the top of the khuff suffices for wiping without intention because the water itself performs the act.

Definition and Conditions of Al-Khuff for Wiping
Definition of khuff and its conditions for wiping

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of the khuff for wiping and identify its four conditions, and explain why only the top of the khuff is wiped.

Core Idea
A khuff for wiping must cover the ankle, have no large tear, be worn on the foot, and permit normal walking.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi definition of the khuff that permits wiping (mash 'ala al-khuff). This specific leather covering must satisfy precise conditions, including coverage of the ankle, minimal tearing, proper fitting, and durability. The passage also clarifies that wiping is valid only on the top of the khuff, not the inside or heel, based on the practice of the Prophet and his Companions. Understanding these conditions is essential for the validity of this concession in purification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the object and its definition
Locate the definition of 'khuff' in the text: 'What covers the entire ankle, or the exposed part is less than three fingers.' Note that this is not a generic definition but the specification for permissibility of wiping.
Khuff is not any shoe; it must cover the ankle joint (ka'b).
2
Analyze the tear condition
The text states that if a tear exposes an area equal to or larger than three of the smallest toes, wiping is invalid. Understand the measurement: three smallest toes placed side by side.
This is the limit for a 'large tear' that nullifies the khuff's legal status.
3
Determine the proper wiping area
The passage, citing the hadith of 'Ali, establishes that wiping must be on the top (zahir) of the khuff. Wiping only the inside, heel, or shin is not valid.
This is based on the Sunna, not analogy.
4
List the explicit conditions and note further ones
From the commentary, extract three conditions: (1) covering the ankle with minimal tear, (2) being occupied by the foot, (3) allowing normal walking. Recognize that other conditions will appear later in the text.
These are basic; the full list includes other requirements like being leather, etc., mentioned elsewhere.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخف : ما يستر الكَعْبَ كله ، أو يكونُ الظَّاهرُ منه أقل من ثلاث أصابع الرجل أصغرها، أما لو ظهر قدر ثلاث أصابع الرجل فلا يجوز ؛ لأنَّ هذا بمنزلة الخرق الكبير
وقد كثرت الروايات عن رسول الله له وأصحابه في الاكتفاء بالمسح على أعلى الخف، وقال علي : لو كان الدين بالرأي لكان باطن الخف أولى من ظاهره، لكنّي رأيت رسول الله يمسح على ظاهر خفيه دون باطنهما»، أخرجه أبو داود وغيره في «تخريج أحاديث الهداية»(۳) للزيلعي ، وابن حجر ومن هاهنا يعلم أنه لو مسح على الباطن أو العقب أو الساق فقط من دون المسح على الظاهر لم يجز، صرَّح به في «الدرر )) [1] قوله : الخف ما يستر...الخ ؛ هذا ليس تفسيراً لمفهوم الخف بل بيان للمراد ، وحاصله أنّ الذي يجوز المسحُ عليه هو الخفَّ الذي يستر القدم مع الكعب، وهو المفصل الذي ينتهي إلى الساق ، بحيث لا ينكشف من القدم شيء، إلا أن يكون نقصانه أقلّ من الخرق المانع، وهذا إحدى شروط جواز المسح على الخف. وثانيها : كونه مشغولاً بالرجل ؛ ليمنع سراية الحدث ، فلو كان واسعاً فمسح على الموضع الخالي من القدم لم يصح ؛ لأنه لم يقع المسح في محله، وهو ظاهر القدم، فلو قدمه إليه ومسح جاز. كذا في خلاصة الفتاوى
وثالثها : كونه مما يمكن فيه تتابع المشي المعتاد ، وله شروط أخر أيضاً يأتي ذكرها متفرقاً في المتن والشرح.
The khuff: what covers the entire ankle, or the exposed part from it is less than three of the smallest fingers of the foot. But if the size of three fingers appears, it is not permissible, because that is like a large tear. Numerous narrations from the Messenger of Allah and his Companions have come regarding sufficing with wiping on the top of the khuff. And 'Ali said: 'If religion were by opinion, the inside of the khuff would be more deserving than its outside, but I saw the Messenger of Allah wiping over the top of his khuffs, not their inside.' It was narrated by Abu Dawud and others in Takhrij Ahadith al-Hidayah of al-Zayla'i and Ibn Hajar. From here it is known that if he wipes on the inside, the heel, or the shin only without wiping the top, it is not permissible. It is stated explicitly in al-Durar. [1] His statement: 'the khuff: what covers' etc.; this is not an interpretation of the concept of khuff but an explanation of what is intended. The summary is that the khuff upon which wiping is permissible is that which covers the foot with the ankle, which is the joint that ends at the shin, such that nothing of the foot is uncovered, unless the deficiency is less than the preventing tear. This is one of the conditions for the permissibility of wiping over the khuff. The second: that it is occupied by the foot to prevent the transmission of hadath. So if it is loose and he wipes over the place empty of the foot, it is not valid because the wiping did not occur in its place, which is the top of the foot. So if he moves the foot into that place and wipes, it is valid. Thus in Khulasat al-Fatawa. The third: that it allows normal succession of walking. There are other conditions that will come later scattered in the text and commentary.
Source pages p. 462

Commentary
This passage defines the khuff on which wiping is permissible. The author clarifies that the khuff must cover the entire ankle (ka'b). If there is a tear exposing part of the foot, the tear must be smaller than three of the smallest fingers of the foot measured together. If the exposure equals or exceeds this, the khuff is like a large tear and wiping is not allowed. The text then cites the practice of the Prophet and Companions: wiping only on the top (zahir) of the khuff is sufficient; wiping on the inside (batin), heel (aqib), or shin (saq) without the top is not valid. This is supported by the well-known narration from 'Ali. The commentary then lists three conditions for valid wiping: (1) The khuff must cover the entire foot including the ankle, with the exception of a small tear less than three fingers. (2) The khuff must be worn on the foot, i.e., the foot occupies it, so that if the khuff is too loose and one wipes on an empty part, it is invalid. The place for wiping is the top of the foot, so if the top of the foot is not under the wiped spot, it is invalid. However, if one then moves the foot into that spot and wipes, it becomes valid. (3) The khuff must allow normal walking, i.e., it must be durable enough for continuous walking. These are basic conditions; others will be mentioned later in the text.

Key Terms
الخف (al-khuff): A leather sock that covers the foot including the ankle; if torn but less than three fingers, wiping is permitted.
الكعب (al-ka'b): The ankle bone; must be covered by the khuff.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a khuff has a tear exposing three of the smallest toes, is wiping over it valid?
A) Yes, because the khuff still covers most of the foot.
B) No, because such a tear is like a large hole that prevents wiping.
C) Yes, but only if the tear is at the top.
D) No, because the khuff does not cover the ankle.

Key Takeaway
A valid khuff for wiping must cover the ankle entirely, have a tear smaller than three toes, be worn on the foot, and allow normal walking, and wiping must be on its top only.

Conditions for Wiping over Khuff: Coverage and Wiping on Top
Commentary on conditions of khuff and the proof for wiping on top

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for the permissibility of wiping over khuff in Hanafi fiqh and explain why wiping must be on the top using the hadith proof.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuff is only valid on the top, not bottom, as proven by the Prophet's practice.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains the essential conditions for the rukhsah (concession) of wiping over khuffs instead of washing the feet in wudu. The author clarifies that the khuff must cover the ankle and that wiping must be performed on the top part of the khuff. A hadith from Ali (ra) serves as the primary evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is wiping over khuffs (al-mash 'ala al-khuffayn). Its ruling is permissible (mubah) as a concession, considered sunnah in the Hanafi school. The passage sets conditions for this permissibility.
Wiping over khuff is a rukhsah, not an azimah.
2
List the conditions for the khuff itself
First condition from the text: the khuff must cover the entire ankle (ka'b) and foot. If the exposed part is less than three small toes, it is permissible; if three toes or more, it is not (like a large tear).
The definition of ka'b differs between Hanafi and Shafi'i, affecting coverage requirement.
3
Examine the dalil (hadith)
The hadith of Ali: 'If religion were based on opinion, the bottom would be more deserving than the top, but I saw the Prophet wiping on the top of his khuffs.' This is a dalil naqli (textual proof). Its thubut is zanni (ahad hadith), but its dalalah is qat'i (explicit meaning).
The hadith is reported by Abu Dawud and others, classified as sahih.
4
Derive the ruling from the dalil
From the hadith, the Hanafi school derives that wiping must be on the top of the khuff, not the bottom. The passage states that wiping on the bottom, heel, or shin only is invalid.
This is based on the explicit action of the Prophet, which is normative.
5
Note additional conditions from the commentary
The commentary adds three conditions: (1) The khuff must cover foot and ankle with only small tear allowed; (2) The khuff must be filled by the foot to prevent impurity transmission; if wide, wiping must be on the part directly over the foot; (3) The khuff must be suitable for customary consecutive walking.
These conditions ensure the wiping is a genuine substitute for washing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخف : ما يستر الكَعْبَ كله ، أو يكونُ الظَّاهرُ منه أقل من ثلاث أصابع الرجل أصغرها، أما لو ظهر قدر ثلاث أصابع الرجل فلا يجوز ؛ لأنَّ هذا بمنزلة الخرق الكبير وقد كثرت الروايات عن رسول الله له وأصحابه في الاكتفاء بالمسح على أعلى الخف، وقال علي : لو كان الدين بالرأي لكان باطن الخف أولى من ظاهره، لكنّي رأيت رسول الله يمسح على ظاهر خفيه دون باطنهما»، أخرجه أبو داود وغيره في «تخريج أحاديث الهداية»(۳) للزيلعي ، وابن حجر ومن هاهنا يعلم أنه لو مسح على الباطن أو العقب أو الساق فقط من دون المسح على الظاهر لم يجز، صرَّح به في «الدرر )) [1] قوله : الخف ما يستر...الخ ؛ هذا ليس تفسيراً لمفهوم الخف بل بيان للمراد ، وحاصله أنّ الذي يجوز المسحُ عليه هو الخفَّ الذي يستر القدم مع الكعب، وهو المفصل الذي ينتهي إلى الساق ، بحيث لا ينكشف من القدم شيء، إلا أن يكون نقصانه أقلّ من الخرق المانع، وهذا إحدى شروط جواز المسح على الخف. وثانيها : كونه مشغولاً بالرجل ؛ ليمنع سراية الحدث ، فلو كان واسعاً فمسح على الموضع الخالي من القدم لم يصح ؛ لأنه لم يقع المسح في محله، وهو ظاهر القدم، فلو قدمه إليه ومسح جاز. كذا في خلاصة الفتاوى وثالثها : كونه مما يمكن فيه تتابع المشي المعتاد ، وله شروط أخر أيضاً يأتي ذكرها متفرقاً في المتن والشرح.
The khuff: that which covers the entire ankle, or the exposed part of it is less than three of the smallest toes of the foot. But if the amount of three toes appears, it is not permissible, because that is like a large tear. And there are many narrations from the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) and his Companions about being content with wiping on the top of the khuff. Ali said: 'If religion were based on opinion, then the bottom of the khuff would be more deserving than its top, but I saw the Messenger of Allah wiping on the top of his khuffs without touching their bottoms.' Reported by Abu Dawud and others in 'Takhrīj Aḥādīth al-Hidāyah' by al-Zayla‘ī, and Ibn Hajar. From this it is known that if one wipes on the bottom, the heel, or only the leg without wiping on the top, it is not permissible. This is explicitly stated in 'al-Durar'. [1] His saying: 'al-khuff'... etc.; this is not a definition of the concept of khuff but rather an explanation of what is intended. In summary, that which it is permissible to wipe over is the khuff that covers the foot together with the ankle—which is the joint that ends at the leg—such that nothing of the foot is exposed, unless its deficiency is less than the prohibiting tear. This is one of the conditions for the permissibility of wiping over the khuff. The second condition: that it is occupied by the foot, so that it prevents the transmission of the hadath (ritual impurity). So if it were wide and one wiped on the part empty of the foot, it would not be valid because the wiping did not occur in its place—which is the top of the foot. If he brings his foot to it and wipes, it is valid. This is in the 'Khulāṣat al-Fatāwā'. And the third condition: that it is possible to walk consecutively in it in the customary manner. There are other conditions that will be mentioned later in the matn and sharh.
Source pages p. 462

Commentary
This is a Hanafi commentary passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah. It first explains that the khuff must cover the foot including the ankle (ka'b). If the exposed part is less than three small toes, wiping is still permissible. If it is three toes or more, it is not permissible because it is like a large tear. The text then provides the hadith of Ali (ra) emphasizing that wiping is on the top, not the bottom. From this, the author derives that wiping on only the bottom, heel, or leg without the top is invalid. The commentary then clarifies that the initial phrase is not a lexical definition but an explanation of the intended meaning for legal purposes. It then lists three conditions for valid wiping: (1) coverage of foot and ankle with only a small tear allowed; (2) the khuff must be filled by the foot so that impurity cannot reach it; if wide, wiping must be on the part directly over the foot; (3) it must be suitable for customary consecutive walking. Further conditions will follow in the text.

Key Terms
الخف (al-khuff): In this text, it refers to the leather sock that covers the foot including the ankle.
الكعب (al-ka'b): The joint where the foot meets the leg, i.e., the ankle.
المسح على الخفين (al-mash 'ala al-khuffayn): The act of wiping over the khuffs as a substitute for washing the feet in wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a person wipes only on the bottom of the khuff (the sole)?
A) It is permissible and valid.
B) It is not permissible because the hadith requires wiping on top.
C) It is permissible if the khuff is wide.
D) It is makruh but valid.

Key Takeaway
Wiping over khuff is a concession with specific conditions: the khuff must cover the ankle and foot, be filled by the foot, allow walking, and wiping must be on the top, not bottom.

Wiping Over Jurmuq (Overshoes) and the Badal Objection
Dispute on wiping over overshoes over khuffs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping over jurmuq worn over khuff and explain how the hadith overrides the Shafi'i qiyas objection.

Core Idea
The Prophet wiped over jurmuq — direct evidence overrides qiyas of 'badal al-badal'.

This passage addresses a practical scenario: can you wipe over overshoes (jurmuq) that are worn on top of your leather socks (khuff)? The Hanafi school permits it based on a clear hadith, while Imam al-Shafi‘i objects on logical grounds. Understanding this dispute reveals how hadith and legal theory interact in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school permits: wiping over jurmuq whether worn alone or over khuffs. Recognize that this is based on a hadith of the Prophet (ﷺ).
The ruling is mubah (permissible) with no restriction on material.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi‘i disallows wiping over jurmuq when worn over khuffs. His reasoning: the khuff is a substitute (badal) for the foot; a substitute cannot have a substitute.
The Shafi'i objection is based on qiyas, not on direct text.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the Shafi'i argument: if the khuff is a substitute for the foot, then the jurmuq worn over it would be a 'substitute of a substitute', which is logically invalid. Additionally, if jurmuq were a substitute, removing it would require washing the feet.
This is a purely rational argument (qiyas) without a hadith.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response has two parts: (1) the hadith is direct evidence and overrides qiyas; (2) conceptually, the jurmuq is a substitute for the foot directly, not for the khuff, so the 'badal al-badal' objection does not apply. The substitution is temporary (only while worn).
The hadith mentioned includes narrations from Bilal, Anas, and Abu Dharr.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a Hanafi may wipe over jurmuq over khuff, while a Shafi'i must remove the jurmuq and wipe directly on the khuff or wash the feet.
This difference affects daily practice, especially in muddy conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بأس بأن يكون واسعاً بحيث يُرى رجلُهُ من أعلى الخفّ. (أو جُرْمُوقَيه ) : أي على خُفِّيْنِ يُلْبَسَان فوقَ الخُفِّين ؛ ليكونا وقاية لهما من الوَحَلِ والنَّجاسة. فإن كان من أديم ، أو نحوه، جاز المسحُ عليهما ، سواءٌ لَبَسَهُما منفردين، أو فوق الخفين”. [1] قوله : ولا بأس؛ إشارة إلى أنّ المراد سترة الكعبين من الجوانب لا من الأعلى، وهذا هو مذهب الجمهور، خلافاً لأحمد . [٢] قوله : أو جُرموقيه : بضم الجيم والميم بينهما راء مهملة ساكنة، وقد ثبت عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم المسح على الجرموق من رواية بلال (1) له عند أبي داود وابن خزيمة والحاكم، وأنس (۲) له عند البيهقي ، وأبي ذر له عند الطبراني). [٣] قوله : أو فوق الخفين ؛ أما في صورة لبسهما منفردين ، فلكونهما كالخُفّين فيمنعان سراية الحدث إلى الرجلين، ويكفي المسحُ عليهما ، وأما في صورة لبسهما فوق الخفين، فيخدش جواز المسح عليهما أنّ الخَفَّ بدل عن الرجل، والبدل لا يكون له بدل لا سيما بالرأي ، وبناءً على هذا لم يجوزه الشافعي . ونحن نقول : قد ثبت «أنّ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم مسح على الجرموقين»، ولا نسلم أنه بدل عن البدل، بل هو بدل عن الرجل ، فلا يلزم البدلُ من البدل، ولا إثبات البدلية بالرأي. فإن قلت : لو كان كذلك لوجب غسلُ الرِّجلين عند نزع الجرموقين كما في نزع الخفين وليس كذلك. قلت : وصف البدلية فيه عن الرجل إنّما هو ما دام في الرجل، فإذا نزع زالت
And there is no harm if it is wide such that his foot can be seen from the top of the khuff. (Or his jurmuqayn): i.e., two khuffs that are worn over the khuffs to protect them from mud and impurity. If it is made of leather or similar, it is permissible to wipe over them, whether worn alone or over the khuffs. [1] His saying: 'and there is no harm' indicates that what is intended is covering the ankles from the sides, not from the top. This is the position of the majority, contrary to Ahmad. [2] His saying: 'or jurmuqayn' with a damma on the jim and mim, with a sukun on the ra between them. It is established from the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) that he wiped over the jurmuq from the narration of Bilal (1) in Abu Dawud, Ibn Khuzaymah, and al-Hakim, and of Anas (2) in al-Bayhaqi, and of Abu Dharr in al-Tabarani. [3] His saying: 'or over the khuffs'; as for the case when they are worn alone, they are like khuffs in preventing the transmission of hadath to the feet, and wiping over them suffices. As for the case when they are worn over the khuffs, the permissibility of wiping over them is questionable because the khuff is a substitute for the foot, and a substitute cannot have a substitute, especially by opinion. On this basis, al-Shafi‘i did not permit it. But we say: It has been established that the Prophet (ﷺ) wiped over the jurmuqayn, and we do not concede that it is a substitute for a substitute; rather, it is a substitute for the foot, so substitution of a substitute does not follow, nor is the substitution proven by opinion. If you say: If that were so, then it would be obligatory to wash the feet when removing the jurmuqayn, as in removing khuffs, but it is not so. I say: The description of being a substitute for the foot only applies while it is on the foot; when removed, it ceases.
Source pages p. 463

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on wiping over khuff. It first addresses a condition: the khuff may be wide such that the foot is visible from the top, because the requirement is only that the sides cover the ankle. This is the majority view, unlike Imam Ahmad who may require top coverage. Then it discusses jurmuq (overshoes). The author defines jurmuq as two khuffs worn over the khuffs for protection. It states that wiping over them is permissible whether worn alone or over khuffs. However, the latter case raises an objection: if the khuff is a substitute (badal) for the foot, then wearing another substitute over it would be a substitute of a substitute, which seems problematic. Imam al-Shafi‘i therefore disallows it. The Hanafi response is twofold: (1) the hadith explicitly proves the Prophet wiped on jurmuq when worn over khuffs, so it is established by direct evidence; (2) conceptually, the jurmuq is a substitute directly for the foot, not for the khuff, so the 'badal al-badal' objection does not hold. Furthermore, the substitution is only while worn; upon removal, the original obligation of washing returns. The commentary demonstrates careful Hanafi legal reasoning by combining hadith evidence and conceptual analysis.

Key Terms
الجرموق (al-jurmuq): Overshoes worn over khuffs for protection from mud and impurity. It can be made of leather or similar material.
البدل (al-badal): Substitute in legal theory; here refers to the khuff or jurmuq taking the place of the foot for the ruling of wiping.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason the Hanafi school permits wiping over jurmuq (overshoes) even when worn over khuffs?
A) Jurmuq is made of leather and thus treated like a khuff.
B) The Prophet (ﷺ) wiped over jurmuq while wearing khuffs, as narrated by multiple companions.
C) The jurmuq is a substitute for the khuff, which is itself a substitute.
D) Wiping over jurmuq is allowed only if worn alone, not over khuffs.

Key Takeaway
Wiping over jurmuq over khuff is permissible in Hanafi fiqh due to the direct hadith of the Prophet, and the objection of 'badal al-badal' is rejected because the jurmuq is a direct substitute for the foot.
